O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is behind the science of medicine, having accomplished it, through his explanations and by his declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it was given to me in vision that I would complete this treatise with this work, which is part of the book of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the book of hands is distorted in our region and is strange throughout, so that it is lost knowledge and forgotten, and there remains from them only a few small descriptions in books of the ancients who had moved their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arose errors and vanities, and the intentions were closed, and the knowledge was withdrawn.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will be able to revive life by following the order of this treatise according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and come together with the forms of cautery instruments, and other tools of the work with the adjustment of its declaration and preparation as such, for it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is fitting for one who enters into this that to surpass in anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the joint of the limbs, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and marrow and the number of joints, and the departure and movement of the veins, and their rest, and so that he know the source from which they issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this Hippocrates says that the nose with the skin is much, and with the work it is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Let us say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things that are to be said, will guard himself from falling into error and from offending people; just as I have wanted many times to prevent those who intervene in this science from abandoning their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Because I saw a mad doctor who cut into an abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and cut into her arteries at the neck; because so much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another doctor who treated a large stone from an old man's body; he removed a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died three days later within him.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have seen that this is called for the treatment, and I see the state of the patient and the size of the wound, and I know well whether the patient will die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another man who was treated for the injury of our duke, who had broken his leg and then got infected with plague; and the healer, blind to the knowledge, tied the break to the wound with strong bandages, and did not leave it exposed, and so I finished it in this way, and he commanded him not to lift it again; and he stayed like that until his leg was completely infected and his feet came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come to untie the leg; and when I saw that it had been loosened, he felt at ease and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all corruption has already been confirmed in the member, and it cannot be cured; and does not cease the corruption from spreading through the member until the entire limb is lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there are other signs that can cause an abscess to form and then inflame, due to the malice of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humors, does not suit to touch it with iron unless there is some relief so that one can remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear sons, it is most necessary for you to know that work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, to see if there has been any danger or risk in more than one place; and I will show you in each one of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For the reason that you must keep yourself safe, so that no one can speak ill of you. If you take up your arms in comfort, and gently but firmly take hold of your sickly condition, and use the best course if you please through God's grace, then you will come to safety and be praised; and let go the fearful sicknesses of poor health; and keep your arms clear of those things that make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Galen advises against taking in a serious illness, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cautery and aqua medicina, and the chapters are ordered from head to feet; and about the forms of secretions, and the instruments of cautery, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the use of forceps and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is organized and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and this chapter is organized around the lower part of the head just as it was previously cut, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Also that we remember the work, it is fitting to say which quality of aid and how much pain each condition causes.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and pain are the longer words and subtle knowledge and the secrets in response; and many of the wise men speak about this and agree upon it; and they are lenient with my words because I am short of length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I am saying that cautery is useful universally for all conditions regardless of matter; and there are two kinds of conditions: that is to say, hot condition with matter, and dry condition with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry condition with matter, some have considered it to be of great help; but the others said that cautery is not worth anything for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be cured with hot diseases by heat, nor with dryness; but it is those who say the opposite that cautery does great aid to hot and dry diseases that come into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you buy the body of a man and its moisture is in the condition of fire, you find the body frozen.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And for any path, do not insert fire unless he who has tried it knows by long use the cautery of cutting, and the diversity of human constitutions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and remedies and space of time; we have no fear, myself, from cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians agree with it.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that cutting is a fire composed of cures, and has greater benefit than burning with hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire cautery, it is simple, and does not come from fire to other limbs except when applied to the limb that is burned, and does no harm to another limb if its name is known.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The hot medicines come from limb to limb by removing, and bring sickness of disease or healing; and by chance the patient is freed from the fire because of its high heat and the goodness of its substance does not do this, if there is superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experiment and through long service and study, which is the truth of things; and for that I excuse myself from the length of speech, because it displeases me to share with you the secret that is revealed by fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures diseases of the body, as the philosopher said in demonstration; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agree on when the cauteries should be made, and take oaths.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable in all times, because the harm that lingers on by the cautery is removed from under the skin with its aid; and itself, when cauteries are done, brings forth necessary pains and hurts that cannot wait until greater mischief comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think on it, dear son, how some people act; because the disease that is cured by cautery has no return; and he says so; but it's not as they think, because cauteries are not just a medicine that moves the complexion, and dries out the humors that cause pain, but rather a medicine for its speed of effect, and for the virtue of its work and its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And there are many possibilities that the sickness comes upon the person at no time according to the complexion of the patient and the state of the disease and its virtues; and there is assembled in him the excess by acquiring food and similar things, unless you administer cauterization to him when he has little excess and moisture, as cauterization for pain and similar things, and this pain does not return; but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand it, for what cauterization is called the rear of medicine, and this is seeing; but they do not believe that cauterization is useful after medicine, but their opinions are false, and cauterization is considered the rear of medicine because when we administer various kinds of cures in no disease and they do not work, then we give them cauterization, and it is valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And then open the fire cautery carefully, because it is on the back of medicine, not contrary to the understanding of the mad doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more effective than with iron, and they did not say those who do it only because of the quality of the gold and because of its high value; and they said that the lead of cautery does not cause corruption, but that's not true because I've tested it myself, and found out that it's not true for some people; cauterization with gold is more valuable than with iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And you don't know when you use an instrument of gold how much it is damaged by its color, and if it cools down quickly afterwards; and if you heat it too much, they take it to the fire; and thus there are enough impediments.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery which we have tried many times on our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or we have ordered this chapter of the lower limbs to be written first because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	for the olive oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the head, and in it there are two remedies: one made because of a disease called 'soda', and another because of many humors that come out from the head to the eyes, ears, and nose, and for many headaches and pain in the teeth and throat, and likewise for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The patient should be purged with medicine that makes the head sweat or cry out III times or IV, according to what virtues and ease can bear the patient; and then wash the chief of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit crossed-legged between your hands, and put his hands on some cloth; after putting the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his two eyes; and if there is a wound that comes from this, then take up the cautery called "olivare", because this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the signet ring of ink on the wound, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little in a twisting motion; then lift your hand immediately, and treat the wound so that you see the bone small; if you don't see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I told you before; after take some wool, put on gauze and soft cotton inside, and place on the wound, and let him rest for III days; then put a linen cloth soaked in lard on top, and let it be so long that the swelling is removed; afterwards treat the wound of the ligature which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until he is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they say the ancients, when the wound stays longer on the body, it purges more; and therefore aid them.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must cut the cautery so much that a part of the bone is burned, and then replace what was burned with the bone, and then be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that one must cut the cautery so much above, and push it so hard as you lower down to the bone, so that the size of the incision is as large as a spindle which women put in their dress for it to make the humors move out; and after that one must cure and suture.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two kinds of cautery do not seem good to me in general; fires whether or not anyone has had a voice of fear; and I think that one should leave them; because the head is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have testified in other members; and even when the head of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more salutary and soothing for me, and from this come together a good remedy.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the whole head suffers from chronic pain that lasts long, the doctor must use the 'cochie' (suppositories and pills) which are called "cochie", and purgatives for the head, oils and plasters; and if he uses fire cautery as we have previously said, it is useless.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Beware if the lump in the patient is of great nature and not too hot; then cut it away with that fire cautery as we have previously said.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cutting fire on each horn of the head where it meets the bone, as we have previously said, and making a cauterization called "vasselz"; because it is that which you put on soles; and clean your hand so that you do not see it near the bone: the patient feels more intense pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary to make cauterizations of the horns more subtle than those for the ugliness of the head, which are the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head there comes sudden pain, and the disease is extended to the oil, and the joints are purged with medicinal medicines, and other treatments have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and none of these things bring any benefit: then perform cautery according to two manners, that is to say with hot medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with hot medicine is thus: take an ounce of salt, and pull off the skin and let it hang over two joints, and then make a mark on the temple where the pain holds in that manner so you can put back the ounce of salt under the skin; and when it is put back so that the skin is tied up well and left for 12 hours; and then take away the binding and treat with hot salt twice a day or three times, and put on cotton soaked in butter until the wound is healed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the healing from wound treatment, until he is well; and if you see him, then do this of any medicine-burning that I have written or prescribed to treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cauterization is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Burn the cauterization of how it is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the form of a clo or has little bit of blackness, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and puts on the painful place, and holds your hand, and twists the feather lightly, until the middle part of the red spice is burnt; and lifts up your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is away from it, and pours abundantly blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Instruct the patient to put cotton in the artery before cutting it on the third day; then put cotton on it for three days; after that put moistened cotton in butter, and cure the wound until it is healed; if you cauterize this emigration with a "cultellare" at its tip, be careful not to cover the artery, which is not old.
de emigraine	of the head or skull (emigraine in Old French refers to a severe headache)
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure head pain as we have previously stated in the divisions of diseases, and it does not profit, and you see that cuts with cauterization did not suffer from this medicine or iron, then it is necessary to heat the "cultellare" until it becomes white; and therefore put a line of half an inch of fat on the artery, and take your hand away once, and do not bind what will prevent the artery from bleeding, and be careful of the jawbone when you eat, lest the nerves ache in the mouth, and spasms occur for the sickness, and beware of the corruption of the vein after it is cut, or if the artery is cut with great fear and pain, and especially to him who cannot endure this, and who is not studied and proven; leave the wound alone in its place; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you to whom in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If it does not cure the fire cautery well for the illness, and the patients suffer greatly, cauterize them in the same way as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter of extracting an artery, with the cautery that has two holes; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from cold weather
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When ear pain comes from cold, and we have used soluble medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pains do not cease, then apply this cautery which is called "poins", because it has this form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After piercing around the ear that is ill, or around both ears where the pain holds, and you move a little towards the root of the ear from there when you mark it with the needle; and apply X points around each ear; after treatment, let him be healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by cauterization is not that of fire, except for those that cause swelling, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not perform any cauterization on false appearances that come from scab and pus of old wounds.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this appearance of torture that comes from swelling and pus in the head, and purging, and gargling, and is worthless, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and another near the temple, and the third between the two lips; and put the cautery on the healthy part, and let it burn in front of the head of the ear a little above the eyebrow, and another as long as a finger on the temple also, and leave the cautery so that its juice be burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the appearance of the cutlery that we have placed before us, but it is a bit more subtle and it must be so that the cuts are a bit larger; after the cure, let him be like I said, until he is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is an old thing and you treat it as we have said, and it does not benefit from it, and the patient does not have fever, then do IV cauteries: II on each of the two horns of the head, and I over the eye, and I in the "vassel" (which is what we have previously said), and the cough cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this sickness, it is fitting to give the patient large and pill-like granules of cereals; after removing the head of the patient, and putting on the occipital area the embalmer's paste of sinapis (which is written in the treatment of emplasters); and this is the manner of cautery: if you do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is sound so be it good; and if not he shall three cauteries of emmolation on the head when coming down to the neck, two spaces between each cautery one large and two small; and treat as the others, and if you see a blister appear, and the patient is suffering, do one cautery in the middle; and if it's fitting, do two more on the other two horns, and treat until he becomes sound; and let the cauteries which are called "olivare", just like I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purified with years and what we have said before; after taking the head from the patient, then do emmolation of the head and on each horn, one more and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers greatly, and the disease is severe, do four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let him stay as long as he gets a hotter fever, and lift your hand; after the cure, treat until he becomes sound, and let be the cauteries which are called "olivare" that we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of an epilempsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epilempsy doctors should use fire cautery only on those who are flaccid, and it is first necessary to soften the brain by years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, when the patient has great pain and suffers from a harsh remedy.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot bear to suffer, then he will make gargling and chewing softening the brain often with raw meat; after taking out his head in a certain manner, and making fire cautery as we have said before, and making fire cautery on the neck, and on each bone; and if the patient is ill and suffers, then he makes fire cautery like I told to the one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine at the back and at the throat, and with olives according to the manner that I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, then they must do fire cautery with subtlety according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excessive flow or corrupted moisture and a large fever, then cut off the cauterized parts as we have said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities decline into melancholy and the body of the sick person is moist, then let them drink something because their cerebrum may be purified, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After dressing the head of the sick person; after making a piece of linen well-made, like a circle, if you tie it around the head; and let them cross their arms, and be well held from all parts; after presenting the linen bandage, and apply mucus of old sheep fat; and warm the cauterized area temperately, so that it may not cause him pain when he has to endure it; after filling the circle inside around the head, and let it cool down; and do this to each sick person once a week with another good governance, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see someone being cauterized while making many pinches all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization increases the brain injury, and then he puts a moist cloth wrapped in butter and animal fat on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eye
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye comes first through division as I have said, then begin and give the patient a medicinal drink, cleansing the head, and warding off all moisture, and let him sweat or take a bath several times a day.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he has had the patient read his head, and makes cauterization on the middle of the head, and makes two more cauterizations on the temples if there is any sign of eye damage in both eyes together, or if it is only in one; and cut all the veins and arteries under the wound, and cauterize long according to the width of the temple; and guard against bleeding and stop if you see too much blood coming out.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and at incising, how to do it safely; and never do this twice with both the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the eyes' shape
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or if the arteries that are visible from the forehead outside; and one sees that it's a superfluity of cold, flaccid humors, then do the cautery as I said at the beginning under the eyelids: I cautery the head, and II cauteries on each temple, and II cauteries or hatteril over both bones; and if it needs more, so cauterize the edge above the eyebrow carefully all around the little cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the flesh by within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	As soon as you have given the medicine according to what we said in division, and if it does not benefit, then give the patient three bad things: after the king the head, and make fire or mileau of fire olive oil; and make two cauteries of the cautery which is called "clavilis" on the two sores, a little below the eyebrows; and be careful of the artery that you do not cover.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of oil is softened by sickness and moisture, then make the cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	This part of the body
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see this done twice on the two wounds as long as the wounds are, do not leave your hand away except until the third part of the paper is burnt, in the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	one hair that sticks out
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	There is never the case that the hairs of the nails are converted to paraffin, and prick the nail, and one does cautery according to two manners: namely by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then put the patient in bed; after that, on the paper of their eyes draw a figure like that of the flame of myrtle, and as it begins with the signs of the hairs; then put cotton moistened in wax and musk of pyrethrum on the oil, then take out the cautery of this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have drawn a little at a time many times, so that the colors are heated in the right direction; and the signs of health over the work are that you see the paper withdrawn, and the hairs lifted to the point of the oil; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for 3 days, then put cotton moistened in butter until the cauterization is removed; after the treatment of ointment until he is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow after this, and the paper is softened then resume cautery on the same spot as before, just like you did initially; and if the hairs are fallen off, cauterize them until the paper rises back to its natural place, even and not touching the hair.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of medicine burning is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are great and even; then make a piece of parchment in the shape of mint leaf; take French soap and vinegar wine, one from each, and grind them together well; and quickly prepare it, if it doesn't cool down, then place it above the form that you have made like the mint leaf, and put on the paper of the eyes; and if the patient holds only oil, it must be applied once, and twice as well; and so with the oil cotton moistened in an olive oil vessel; and place the chest of the sick person on a clean bed and show on your forehead the medicine, and press one pulse and feel all the time that the patient feels pain from the medicine, because he feels pain just like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, so hold tight to your health.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the morbidity is passed, lift the limb again, and bind it if you see that its position has been lifted just as it was lifted by force of fire or incision; and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not the case, then again apply medicine to the limb or if medicine has failed, until your wounds are even and your eyes are bound tight; then put on cotton cloth soaked in butter until the keys fall loose, after applying the "dyafenis" wound dressing and others, until he is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to guard your work with great care, so that the wound does not come loose from its place.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	If the paper becomes soggy after, and the hair is pricked in the oil, then recommence the medicine on that person who has become soggy because of the paper properly, as you have done before; after the cure until they are sane; and this is the form of the fire cautery:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to this, your constraints; and do not reply to the straight path to one who has no study in this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by fire cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula just as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures are not beneficial, then it is necessary that you make it cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in a clean place; and tie the menisters' fingers around his head in such a manner that he does not move or shift his head; afterwards put cotton soaked in wine or persil juice on the oil; afterwards heat the cautery which is so shaped as the shape of a pen of walnuts, to assemble it so that they fit together; if you see this, it has been applied from one end of the head to the other, and if you see this, it is just like a tent; but however, this will be useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is opened, and extracting the filth, and drying it; and if it is closed, then work on it, and extract fire from the bowel; afterwards put on the cautery which has been heated to a pen-like shape, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part where the skin ends, lest you go mad; and put the cautery into the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery procedure just before the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If this does not work, you must repeat the cautery procedure once more, and if it is necessary again, and let it for three days; after that put cotton soaked in butter on the wound, and apply an ointment drying antiseptic until he is cured, and if forty days pass and he is still not cured, put medicine to corrode the bone so that the bone is exposed; and the remedy as described according to what it came in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cautery for fistulas that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand that fistula means an opening, and make it clean; after put in the fissure a thin thread of what is this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it is made to the quantity of two hundred and seventy-one pints; and hold your hand over the anus firmly, and do not move the patient at all, until the plums are melted and their juice flows into his body; for it is necessary that one puts on a moist cloth, wet in wine or oil: the plums will cure the fistula, and heal the patient with marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	But if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to administer purgatives to the belly, and bring the fistula back into the body as much as seems proper to him in his own house.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often cavities occur in lips called "poil", and even more often in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cavities of those which we have mentioned in the division, and if the cure does not profit, then apply a small cautery surgical instrument according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it instantly into those cavities until they come to a boil; after the cure, put the patient on castor oil till he is cured.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the uvula, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it becomes putrid and rotten and is dried out and forms a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not profit: therefore it is fitting to apply cautery according to the size of the fistula; after removing or destroying the fistula, hold your hand until the iron needle comes into use again, and then proceed thus once or twice, after the cure which we have stated in cures, till he is cured; and if so treated, it is good; but if not, it is fitting to discover the root and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in your book.
dou movement des dens	any movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat him with medicines and it does not work, then put the head of the sick person on a clean cloth; after apply fire cautery in that manner so that you place a string on the tooth; and pour hot caustic in there tightly, and hold your hand as long as the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after release your hand and continue the cautery according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let him eat for an hour and rich fires.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in that manner the teeth that were moving are compressed again, and the gums are restrained, and the moisture is corrupted and dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from coldness, or there is coldness in the vein, and medical remedies do not help, then it is necessary to cut according to two methods: and cutting with butter and cutting with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cutting with butter is done like this: you take butter from the vagina, and put a piece on the end of a iron or tine spoon; after that you take cotton and wrap it over the point of a tent, and the wound in butter boils, and apply to the painful tooth immediately and hold until it cools down; and so do many times until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the wound is covered with lard and cotton in butter burn, and apply to the tooth aching, and put iron hot over the top of the tooth so that the heat reaches the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Instruct the fire cautery to assemble the fire so that you grip a cane of iron or flint and it is thick enough so that the heat does not come to the mouth of the patient; after heating, see how the form comes and put it above the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, because the pain will be removed on the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is fitting that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the haste of applying this cautery, and then remove it; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And do fire cautery on the head that you wish, and according to what power you have; and this is the form of the iron:
des scrophules	Warts
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When warts are infected and moist with cold, moisture, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, therefore heat the cautery on the hair of that part which comes after this; and make openings for the pus to come out from the cautery in the other part; and apply the cautery hot above the abscess once, or whenever it is convenient, until it comes to a head of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put cautery according to the size of the abscess, and let it be so for three days; and put cotton soaked in fat on top until the ulcer is closed; after treatment give ointments and poultices until he is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the ring
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistors win on the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be voided first by solvable medicines; after, they should apply fire cautery to the root of the throat, and beware that you do not come near the throat again, and do not burn with heat but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the other fire cautery is applied to the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and it is the "knuckle" (clavicle) because we have a form like that; cure the patient in such a way as we have said until they are healed.
de la toust	of the throat.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the illness of the pimple is caused by cold moistors, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and it's an old sickness, then they do two fire cauteries on the swellings in their veins; and another fire cautery is applied between the two nipples; and the cauteries are those called "knuckles" as per the form that was previously said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, do cautery in pricking with all the cautery called "pins" because of which the form is thus before in the disease of the ears; and be the pins just at XXX.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment as previously said, and be the cauterys at three joints according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because they are easier to cut, because you do three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After sovining the patient on his back and on his chest; after lift the liver which is in the right breast due to your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, then apply the cautery that has two horns shaped like this:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the liver until it is perforated just below the breast, and it comes together with the figure of the cautery made from four horns; and for this reason there is made a cautery with the cautery that has three horns, because the figures of cauterization are thus four horns; and it is the nerve according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the shape of the cautery that has three horns:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes they press on this nerve because it has eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying heat with a cauterized needle, instruct the patient to let them rest afterwards and do not move their limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if the dislocation occurs above, then the case is poor, so make cauterization on the thick part with a cauterized needle or many cauterizations in a point.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joint is closed, and the moist part is healed, and the patient's sickness is alleviated.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When colds and many moistors come to the stomach, and they extract them from his complexion, and multiply the catharres in him, and do all sorts of accustomed cures which he does not benefit from, then it is fitting that the sick person be laid on their back, and stretch out their legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	De those after, let the fire cautery be done III times beneath the thumb of the finger per the quantity of two measures, to all cauterization nails, and II times away from the II sides so that the figure of the cauterization is at III angles, and has this space between one and another so they are not joined together when they rot; and let the cautery be done in such manner so that it pricks the two parts of the tongue, and so be the figure of the cauterizations according to this form and surrounding.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see the cautery done with a great cautery in the stomach according to this form; and if anyone fears this cautery, do puncture and point above the stomach at one point according to how much ink is used; then cauterize all the cautery which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment we had previously, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As for the liver, pain comes from frost and moisture and great swelling, until it is forced to its natural condition through excess; and patients are cured according to what we have said in divisions, but if they do not benefit, then let them be put under a poultice on their haunch; signifying three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, excluding the apothecaries, at the cost of an ounce to each cautery; and leave space between each cautery the growth of one pound; and let the cauteries be long along the body, and do not press too hard with your hand throughout all the cautery; and only burn the middle part of the wound, and let the patient lie on his sides; if he cannot, so let him sit, and stretch out his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If you wish it so, cauterize these cauteries with the sword, if you are subtle and wise in this art, and beware that you do not burn all the flesh, for you will dry out all the body; and if it does not come to boiling, because the blood is very subtle at the point, and the knowledge to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you see if it is within the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, he feels the patient a little pain not very great; and if it is in the membrane, he feels sharp pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure requires the removal of a tumor, it is fitting that the patient be seated on his head; then sign in which direction the abscess is, and then heat the cauterary like an arrow, because here is its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Instruct the fire cautery so that the wounds are seared, and it comes to a stop just as it's about to enter the vein, so that the prickling is completely extinguished; after the treatment according to the treatment of cuts, until he is healed; and it should not be used by anyone else than one who has studied long in the art of medicine, and through whose hands these diseases have been cured once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	So it can be done with great courage, and I must say that it seems to me to be worth leaving.
dou cautere de pleuresin	How to cut the pericardium
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that to treat pleurisy you should use the root of arsurgium, and in this way: take a long root of arsurgium, the largest you can find, and dry it, and make it as big and as long as your thumbs; and pound it with oil, and apply it to fire, and cauterize between the lung and neck, and make two punctures one below the chin; and one between the fifth rib and sixth, with an oblique direction; and one on the navel, and one between the two shoulders, and one behind each rib, where the cauterized spot is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make it open as if you were applying a perfume.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	Instruct an old man that no one uses cauterization of fire similar to the razor, and place the sheaf between the ribs until it comes to the abscess; and when a fever burns, as we said in the chapter on the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear for the sick now, or a fistula appears that cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.
