When you treat the sickness of the mouse, as we have said about divisions of cures, and it does not profit, then they say there are three ways of cauterization that all are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one is that you make three cauterizations, or four, in a manner according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of cauterization of the liver that we have said before; and do not press hard with your hand on all the cauterization, and let the patient sleep on his back; and another way of cauterization is that you place the cautery which has two nails, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the wound where the mouse is, or when the veins come from the left side, and lift the swelling according to the size of the body, according to the length of the limb, and the cauterization be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After the fire is applied, let the two nearest parts be inflamed until they are perceived by the other part, and then take fire the cautery, and thus it will have four nails. And if you see, cauterize all the cautery to three nails.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the wound has gotten putrid due to long time, and this is an excuse that the other treatments before mentioned.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery does not apply to dropsy, except when done in the way called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the ways we have said in divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries inside the belly, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the navel, and two behind the back on the spine, and one towards the groin; and so let the cauteries be close to the root of the wound.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the cautery open for a long time to clean out putrid flesh, and do not stop the treatment of the patient after the cautery, the healing would hasten, and there will be two kinds of intentions with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery on the abdomen should be like a nail that we have shown before; and for the back, it should be olive oil, as has been placed here beforehand.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the bones
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the bones swell in someone who is dropsical and filled with a yellow bile, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery as you turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, for so would the fire burn the citrine, and thus the cautery should be done in this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, perform two cauteries on each leg, at the point of the cutlass, and thus the cautery should be done on both sides, one in front of the knee and the other behind it, in the leg; and let the cauteries remain long in place to cure what ails them; after curing the other wounds that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the illness
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the virtues retained and digestible in the stomach and intestines are loosened, and cannot be cured by any treatments; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with very foul breath, do thus a grant cautery on the stomach as he has said before about a cautery of the stomach, or a cautery of the gut; and four cauteries around the belly, subtle ones to all the cautery sharp points, and two cauteries on the haunches.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	If you see moistures abundant and the patient suffering, then make fire cautery on the navel, and fire cautery on each joint, and twice make fire cautery on the stomach near the great one, because the cure is beneficial when it has good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the seat, or one or more of them, and they are old and have great cold and moist humors corrupted, and are treated as we said in divisions, but it does not profit, then make cauterization: three on the spine at the back of the neck, that is all behind the armhole little by little in a triangle shape, and one below the breastbone two; and if you think its stomach is cooled down, and its meat doesn't burn, and swelling appears on the face, then apply a cauterization to the stomach as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the mouse bone all around with cauterization; and leave the cauterization for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment the limb must be allowed to recover.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	from the fat which is called "thelel
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the "thelel", if you heat the cautery that resembles a razor, and then put it all ablaze on the cut "thelel", and let your hand rest until the cautery comes to the vein's birth, without any cutting; do this once or twice, and if there is much "thelel" left, cauterize each one as we have said; after curing with ointments, allow them to recover until they are healthy, and if you cauterize a great cautery on the cartilage, it will give greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of badly treated wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure torture or opening, we will tell him in his own words, if he comes to this illness that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is an ulcer, and it is old and covered with putrid pus and corrupted moisture, if you press to see whether the entire wound is tender, observe that you know how deep the wound is.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After the cautery which seems to shave with a razor, and pour it into the ulcer according to how much the wound has entered, repeat the cautery until the pus and corruption are burned off, once or twice, or three times, depending on the quantity of blood needed; and be careful not to hurt the nerve that is inquiring, and the great veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	In case the fistula follows the course of the uterus and the intestine, be careful with these things, and do not make heat treatments like this only in the groin area, and think that it is not very painful; after treatment, keep the patient as long as they are healed, and if the fistulas are hardened, and the materials are ossified for a long time, then you will know that the patient is completely healed; and if the materials do not ossify, you will see that the patient is weak, and corrupted bones at the site; and in this way, just like what we will say to him.
de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from a fracture comes to the kidneys, and great swelling, and does not take effect in women, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on both kidneys of one part and the other, with the clavicle cautery that we have previously mentioned; and if they are cauterized on both sides at once, three cauterizations in line will be made, and greater relief.
de la vessie	From the vessel
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft from fire and moisture, if the patient retains urine, then he must cut in the area behind where the hair grows at the navel, on both right and left, since they are long as one's finger; and he cuts to the back of the body, where he needs it most, or wherever he has need.
de la marris	From the intestines
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the intestines are cold and moist, and do not conceive because of this, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are late; and when they come, it causes great pain: therefore it is fitting that one cuts into them around the belly, as we have said in cutting from the vessel, and also cuts behind the back; and cut with a claw, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the shoulder
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist viscous fluid descends to the bony shoulder, and because of this he stops moving in his own place, and it is known that the calf is longer than the other when measured together; and if you find the veins swollen in departure, it is fitting to cauterize the patient on the bony shoulder with a cautery similar to the circle, and apply pressure before the vein turns towards the bony part so that the bone lies within the circle; and apply such cauteries as those for which the stomach has been cauterized.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make three cauteries of olive oil and apply them as deeply as all the keys; and the doctor until he is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin, and it is cold and moist, and those who are sick are cured with what we have said in division, but the cure is worthless, and the sickness is ancient; therefore it is necessary that you purge the patient of the thick humors, or fetid pills, or other hard-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After purging, then apply cautery; and the method of cautery is according to two manners: that is to say, assembling hot medicines, and cautery by fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Cautery by fire is according to many manners, of which some are such: that you cauterize above the groin so that you do three cauteres in this form, and make a good depth and great, and have between each cautere the space equal to the thickness of two fingers, and use olive oil; sometimes one does cautery at the midpoint on the top of the groin, because there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	If you see, as the fire cautery on the cautery of the circle which we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the gout; but do it in this manner that the circles contain all the gout, and all the points that touch be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatique, when the pain holds in the gout, and does not come to just below the knee or just below the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes just below the knee and the leg, then you make two fire cauteries where the patient says that the pain holds, and four cauteries are made above the ankle, on the left side a little; and either the cutlery cautery is used, or the burning of the thickness is done; and if the patient feels that the pain extends just below both feet or near it, then the cautery is made where he feels the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	Instruct the master to do it again if he does not; and if he sees that the pain is below the joint towards the thigh, perform fire cautery on both cutting and circular knives, and take good care in all your cauteries so you do not let the cautery burn the nerves and great arteries, and do not make the patient more troublesome and constricted.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen others who had fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and let them burn so that the leg was completely severed, and also the toes, and they became recognized and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a belly solution that killed him.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in both parts together, perform fire cautery on one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	Instruct the wise men to make in the fire cautery of hawthorn thus: make one such iron and it should be as big as an unwary man's thumb or slightly less, and let it pass between the interstices like this from one interstice to another, with space equal to a grain of barley; and let the interstices be twice as wide, and they should be like wheat, and have a well-made iron bar; and thus is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is completely red and burns seltzer, and then place it on the hawthorn of the sick person, and let it turn towards the healthy side; cut off once with the cautery and leave three days; after that apply ointment of butter, and let the wound heal for a long time; afterwards treat with oignement until he is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cauterization because of fear of its sting, and if it is seen to be used, then all are good cautersies, which can endure it.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauterization of medicine burns if you make an instrument with two crossed pieces in such a way that the edge of the tool descends along the margin of the vein, and it can be made of iron or bronze to a long appearance, and in its upper part there should be three, and between each one the quantity of the thickness of a penny; and they should overhang and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the hedgehog's awl on the patient lying on his side near where it was injured, and press your hand strongly above the awl of the hedgehog; then pour between the two circles of the hot water which is heated a little in the fire, and let it remain for an hour or two, and suffer the patient the heat and the pain from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	If the pain has spread to just the thigh or just the knee, make an instrument that holds according to what you have done in the groin area; and this is the way of applying heat, and I have written it in treating the correcting of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take quicklime and live sulfur, equal amounts of each, grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	so that the small opening be free, so that a point of an arrow may not enter; and put it in another pot well-placed, and put quicklime and sulfur and hot water upon it, until you have two puffs above the powder, as when you had well mixed it with your hand; then leave it thus until it comes out hot and cold water or pot lead, then take all that hot water, and pour it upon sulfur and upon quicklime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And when so it will be very wet and is managed in the movement of various medical works and cauteries of other members, for it does every work with fire, and does with other medicines that one cauterizes well the vein just like this sieges and honey acacia and caldron with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Greeks tell us of a cure that one man was cured of the pain of his vein and sciatic nerve, and he spoke highly of it, and said that no other cure is needed, and he became sane for only once when this cure was performed, and he took a bath as he taught later on.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this way that you take some fresh and dry vertigris green on your bed, and crush it much with a little of fat, and apply it to the vein and to the thigh and knee and to the joint where the pain is, and bind it; and then he lets it sit for three hours by the amount that the patient feels no more pain.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put him into the bath so that his body may be slightly loosened, and put him to bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery of such medicines, unless they are after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dyascorides said that when the sciatica vein is cauterized with horsehair, it will cause much pain; and therefore they must make the cautery in a certain manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and anoint it with old oil, and put it on the fossa that is between the little toe and the other one called the foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dry horsehair and holding it to the fire until it is charred, anoint it with oil on linen, and put it on the fossa so that it stains; and repeat this again, and do not stop doing this until you think it has come close enough to the hank of the foot, and that the pain is ceased; for this manner of cautery is called "cautere de chievre".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or by percussion, or by excessive evacuation, or because of swelling of cold matter, none of these things is worth cautery, except for those who come from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the sick person be given pills fetid or other signs, on their back, where the pain holds, three lines marked of enche, and in each line one cautery or more according to virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and it should be done the cautery as called "poins"; and if you see, do III cauteries or IV with the clavile pin straight according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness comes to small children many times, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow spine when they lift up, and fear; and you will find in the lower back space on the back, and in the appearance that comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and observe how to cure it, cut off the affected area according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If you prick with cauterization each part of the spine increasingly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, if you cut into the spine at a point just behind the second vertebra, or the third, and the points are close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, keep the patient until he is healthy as we have said, and be careful not to apply cauterization to areas of swellings or inflammation which are in the grasp of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by moisture that has spread to each limb of the body, and when the pain comes from the foot, which they call "podagre" in its proper place, and because of cold causes and medicines cannot be cured, if it is healed through cautery in this way: make a mass of cautery around the joint of the foot, and use olivary cautery according to this shape:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is pain where you press on the face of the foot, do cautery to the entire point that we claim.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, do cautery on each knee three cauteries or four of each part, all the olivary cautery; and if you need more, then make more, but do not hold back your hand from heat as long as the spell of the cure is hot.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the groin and the back, instruct the patient to apply the fire cautery that we have discussed in his chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make pain in the armpit two lines deep; and if there is no more pain after that, make pain on each joint and on the skin of the hand; and if the pains come just below the elbows or just above the shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good governance to the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	But if you make good governance and purge the swelling, he will be made whole by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of a surgical incision of the flesh.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When there is an incision in the flesh that brings pus down to the joints and it's new, it is necessary to cure his eyes daily so they do not infect him again; and he should use things that lie on his belly so that his fever descends from his belly; after that sit him on his back between your hands, and instruct him to pull out his leg until the swellings are repaired, and then bring it to your hands, and stitch over the incision above the bone of the finger, and make a sign similar to half a circle above the bone; this is how they have done the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	Until he is white and his senses are clear.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then take out the bowels at their place; and let the physicians tie his hands so they do not return to their original position; and work well on the patient's thighs, and put one cussin and another serjant on the thighs, and another on the foot that keeps his hands in place; then apply the cautery to the sign at the tip of the fingers, and keep the right hand and the left hand until you touch the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, let it happen again as many times as you live until you reach the bone; and be careful so that the bowel does not escape when you make the cautery; so that you do not burn it; and that the patients do not die, or from another malady.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And instructs you to know that when you do not come close enough to the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is fitting that the cautery for children should be subtle according to their size, and for great people also great according to their size; after three days of treatment with butter so that the swelling is drawn off, cure the other wounds afterwards until they are healed, and rest the sick person on their back forty days under their back, so that the wound is well closed; and it is fitting that their movements be slackened for a long time, so that the boils do not burst when he goes to walk in his chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, give him a well-made bandage and apply it for forty other days; and let him have good rest, so that he works little and avoids excessive drinking and eating, and too much shouting; and as soon as you follow this teaching, he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after his treatment in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the operation on the abdomen.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When they come from other stomachs and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, if it is cut with the cautery, do according to its quantity, and burn off one-third of the wound; after the treatment as we have said; and none of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized at the three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the left side of the wound and make a line for its width, and another one afterwards, and tie your thumb tightly around the entire cauterization.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more gentle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of olden pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, whether from a fall or from injuring it, and the pain lasts for a long time, and medicine cures are not effective, then it is necessary to be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and to be cauterized according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twisting and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the wound from the first cautery heals well; but if it does not heal again on that same place, because sometimes it is necessary for the member to grow and change, so that you should make more cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of clumsiness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The trouble is treated with no success by cauterization for great help, and the same illness that comes from the rotting of pus and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see this cauterization, taking precautions if the illness is at the beginning, and treating it as we have said in division, and neither cutting nor staying (there), and doubting that corruption seeps into the whole patient, so make a cautery on the head: I emmolate the head new, and the other towards the front until the hairs; and two over the two horns, and one behind the hilt; and leave your hand thus long as the cautery comes to bone, and as far that the scabs come out forth so that the vapors of great humors can come out; and cauterize on the skin according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the cauterization is everywhere sparse; and it pertains manifestly, so it must be that you apply this fire cautery to these cauterizations which we have told you about in the head, and one cautery in the neck, and two on the spine of the back, and one grant on the elbow and another on the other side, and two on the shoulders; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet; and beware of the nails that are under the skin, lest you burn them; and never do cautery on the bone of the finger, and one cautery on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when you do more cautery, the patient gets more benefit, and the effect is greater; and know that the sick do not feel pain from the cautery if they are healthy, because the body is already entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that the fire cautery should be large or small depending on the member and joints, as you will find in various iron tools.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, wash the patient with flour and honey several times until they are healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When an inflammation occurs in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but does not heal, then make fire cauteries on the member according to its size and size of the member; let the cautery be a little inside the wound that is inflamed; then cure it with ointments until they are healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at no time should one perform a cautery with their hand and foot and back, after the nerve that causes the member to be mute; and thus if there is swelling, it must be removed; and let none of them intervene unless they are familiar with the members and the paths of moving bones.
de albaras	De albaras translates to "of wounds".
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound, called an "albaras", is old and medicine has no value, then cut with cautery on one end by one finger length, according to how thick the flesh is, until the blanching is done, and the color changes; then the cure of flour from violes and lentils with olive oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of colon and blood of alondre, each a part; and mix them all together, and tie with a bandage, and apply to the patient as long as they are cured.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure of cancrer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When cancrer comes at the beginning, and you look to stop it, then cut with cautery on the cautery that seems to be around the entire circle of the cancrer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all the wise people said that you should do cautery in the middle of a wound; and I don't think this is good, because I fear it will cause ulcers and corruption, and I have never seen it happen before; and there is no more serious thing than being cauterized inside, with the "circule" cautery, as we said in many other cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of an edema that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have a disease called "adubelati" which delays death or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the age of the sick person when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood or for the time; and you see him hasten to die: then cauterize inside with many small cauteries in puncturing; after leave so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	It will soon die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced all with the cautery, so that the cauterization is of this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauterization has pierced the vein, and so that the cauterization is made with such precision that the patient feels pain before it happens in this manner, so that the course of the infection may be delayed.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until he is perfectly recovered.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cautery by iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of disease that is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a gangrene of the limb, because it corrupts the limbs in the same way as fire corrupts dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a person who can suffer fire cautery together, then heat the cauteries small and large, according to what is suitable for the patient or the illness; after cauterizing all parts until you have eradicated the whole corruption, and nothing remains, so that everything corrupted should be destroyed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let him lie for three days, and put on the patient's cauterized wounds with a cloth soaked in oil until the scalds from the fire are destroyed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After this remedy is done with generated splinters.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that a healthy growth does not appear, it is good; and if this does not happen, then resume the cauterizing on those who remain corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this meat is sometimes cured with medicine in place of fire cautery; but all ways fire cautery is of greater help, and I have said the treatment for the medicine before in the division: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of worms that come to the bones.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that at the bones due to weakness a disease is born which is called "closed" according to our intention, and it is a big thing that wounds the bone.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the fire cauteries of this disease are according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, cauterizing with fire, and cauterizing with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautering with fire is that you heat the cautery like a hair comb also as a nail, and it is made of good iron to the measure that it can penetrate all parts, and has subtle edges; after putting it hot on the nail, turn your hand around the nail until it comes out at the font of the nail; and let it be so for three days till it begins to rot; then make an ointment of vinegar and sweet marjoram ground with salt, and put the ointment on all the wound, and the nail will come loose and will be desirously separated from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint with application of heat until it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are swollen due to the body's moisture, and this happens many times in the hands and feet, it is advisable to apply hot cautery; and thus: take a thorn or iron rod, or a quill of wood, and place it on the skin, as if pricking warts; and put the thorn on so that it stings all around, then put a little warm water on it, and hold your hand tight, and press your hand in such a way that the edge of the thorn comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water running through to its root; and let the patient suffer for an hour under the cauterization of the hot water; then leave him so, and he will drain all to his roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Instruct a doctor to do this after that one, until you have checked all those who are in the body, then cure the limbs that bind tightly.
li cure dou trembler	cure of shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold or fever, quartine or another, it is advisable that you make four cauteries on the spine of the back, four on either side; one on each spine; and one over the stomach at the olive cautery; then let him stop trembling, and hasten his health from this cold disease.
des pustules puans	of painless boils.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never appear in its natural state the chest's boils or painless boils, which come from corrupted large matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is fitting to use the first cautery on every head of each pustule: a subtle cautery made from a fust of myrtle, so that the point is gripped by fire, or from the root of aristotle long, or with a cautery lens.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time are cauterized when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow any larger in front, but the superfluous swelling that comes from them is broken open and they heal; but it is fitting that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times it happens that great bleeding from the artery occurs at the wound that comes near by, or with the incision of the abscess, or with the cautery on the limb, and such similar things; and it is a very grievous matter to smell.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Instruct all who have this illness to hasten and place his two fingers on the vein wound, and strain them very much so that the pain is not caused below your two fingers, and that no more blood flows from it; then put the olive oil cautery in various small and large sizes until they are all red; next take one, either great or small according to the wound and how the artery runs, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your two fingers, and hold it there until the swelling is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the fire jumps up when you lift your two fingers over the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take haste and take another cautery that is on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the swelling is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is near, and that no other evil comes upon the sick person; and know that when the blood does not flow out of the artery, it cannot be effectively stopped unless in one of the four ways we have mentioned: by cautery, by extraction since it has not been treated, by a strong tie with thread, or by medicines placed there which have power to stop the bleeding; and if tied and strained happens as a result.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will provide restening of a tightly bound member by covering it with bandages or putting hot things on top of it, or other similar things, unless there is no benefit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has no remedy or medicine available, he must put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and carefully extend it above the wound and above the vein; and he should not move him, but apply cold water frequently so that it becomes very cold until the veins are congealed and swollen and extended; and make incisions in front of what is necessary for cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on the treatment of cuts.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	As we have said in the first chapter of all diseases by which it is necessary to cauter with fire or with hot medicine, the causes and the effects and the symptoms and the forms of cautery; and I have written that chapter on the head just above the eyes, and I will go through this same book by the same way because those who study here find it easier.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this work, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than with the first cautery, and therefore it must be approached with greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to be foolish.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come in for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who have been cured so easily with their disease that they die quickly because of the strength of their disease and its great power; and for this one must fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And when I have explained this to you, and said "wait, I am cured"; and the sickness is stubborn.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not necessary only that you grant your consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetise, and do not be weakly, but wisely, of those from whom you are certain, and from whom you can take; and use the prophecies and indications for the cures of your sicknesses, so that salvation may be converted; and this will help you to gain a good reputation, glory, and remembrance.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three most precious sons, our Lord gives you good understanding and right judgment, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I shall translate the text line by line into English.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The chief full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Knows that this illness comes very often in children at birth, and when the baby holds tight too tightly the child's head; and sometimes it is due to a return caused by not knowing.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this illness occur more than in children, and with all those I have seen it quickly spread the disease; and for that reason it seems to me that it should be treated with care.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw that in one child the joint was full of water, and the head became swollen every day until it could no longer be supported; and he thought so much that he was dead, and this moisture is assembled under the bone above, between the marrow and the bone; and the wound is such that when the moisture is between the bone and the marrow, you cut open the skull a wide incision; and make it as long as II, since the moisture runs; and behold the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more deep, and the abscess is bigger, then you should make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see cause the commissure of each cheek to overflow with blood when you press your hand into it, and that does not return: then it is necessary to make three incisions in the skull according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, take out all the moisture that is flowing.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After closing the incisions with bandages and powder, and applying vinegar and oil, and leaving so for five days; then release, treat the wound by binding and ointments, and leave to drain the head, and feed the patient dried meat of a little moisture until the limb is comforted and made whole.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of making an incision is that you look or open the large opening of the abscess, and the assembly of the water; for it is sometimes in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right side, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure therefore when you cut to the opening of the abscess, and the filling of the water, and make the cut according to what you have the skill for; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and give a small quantity of blood, so that the patient may die due to bleeding and evacuation of fluid.
de reume	of lead.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it has happened to any disease that is called "cough" and affects the eyes or the worst, and the disease is old and does not benefit from medicinal treatment, then the last remedy is to cauterize with what one covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Instruct the patient to cover his eyes when you perform cautery, so that he does not see; after you stroke the left with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then take out the patient's neck with all the cloths; then look where the vein is being cut, and the pulse of one and the other is after the ears, and do not return soon; then sign the pulse on both sides, then cut one and the other with a good spatumile of two parts, until the vein becomes visible just at the bone, and so that it be done over the wide space of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, pour out the spatumile under the artery and cut it above, in cutting as much as two parts to pass through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, make it stop without any further bleeding continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
de emigrainne	is coming from
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old inflammation comes, and a catarrh is good, because of the moisture of the tears and the heat in the temples and the ancient sore, and similar things, and it is treated with various kinds of medicines and cure medicines, and all this does not benefit him, if we cut out the arteries from the temples and the cauterized parts, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is such that the patient makes his hair back on his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and it is not repaid with heat like in some men who are too cold; and if it is revived, then he ties the neck of the sick man with certain cloths, then rubs him with a harsh cloth, and awakens him with hot water until the artery becomes manifestly visible; then take the spatula whose form is:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Instruct the patient to scrape lightly the skin until you see an artery, then take it up in its entirety as close to its origin as possible, and pull it off gently at the base of each part; if the artery is subtle, then twist with a needle point until it breaks, then cut off that particular part according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it will not be severed, do not leave it attached without any pain or discomfort at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And take out the vein at six cubits, just three from its origin; and if the artery is large, it is wise to tie in two ligatures of a strong double thread made of silk, so that there will be no purulent discharge before the wound heals; watch it every day until the vein closes; then cut off the swelling that lies between the two ligatures at this same hour, and if you see, then cauterize with the cautery cutlass just to the bone until the joints are severed; and this is the more careful work, if the patient has no fever and it is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is aid to finish the moister: for this it has more aid than the moisters.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries, fill the vein with wool from an old person and put on well-made tents; and when they are pulled out, cure him with dry medicines that produce charcoal, and with tents, until he is healed; and if you do not cut at the artery when working on it, then hasten to cover it with fire cautery, or apply a poultice of vitriol and pull off with your hand so that they are not stained; and if you don't have this present, put wool onto the vein for as long as you can, until it becomes frozen, and tie up the vein tightly like it is necessary; and what is more muddled and lighter in the extraction of the artery should be cauterized with a cautery trenching two thirds, but the trenches must be well-spaced to last longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the urine is too dark, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have two incisions of about an inch, then when you've marked out two spaces between them, and the hot iron is placed so that it comes just to the bone, cut the vein in two spaces; and let them be separated between the two incisions because there's no heat from this cautery throughout everything; and this is the form of cautery:
des larmes	from tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are flowing into the veins on the forehead, near the bone of the head of the force, and they do not benefit from any medicine that we make, and you see the face of the sick person inflaming, and feel or sense the pain in front as if with frost; and since the oil is cold and moist so that the hair of the papilla is wet, and are dried up the papillae, and burnt by the heat of the tears, it may be necessary to apply this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	Instruct the patient to call them "cure of the contused", and you must make a reference back to the patient who has this illness.
