Let the hairs grow on the face as much as possible, then make III equal cuts on the front, according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be so that II parts join the forehead in the downward direction like new bone, and the other II cuts are II rows over the eyebrows, and you must avoid cutting the arteries which are located over the eyebrows; and pull away your hand from continuing with II jawbones, and each wound shall have III doves tied through it; and take an sponge piece and a lot of cloth to soak up the blood, then use a good spatumile, two parts as its form.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision at the temple, to the second incision; and scrape all the blood that is between II cuts, until the surface of the bone, then make another cut from the first incision up to the second one, and then pull out this spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you cut into the fire with command of the physician let him let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the scalpel cutting towards the raw flesh at the point, and the back of the scalpel soft towards the bone, and let it cut until it reaches the middle wound.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut through the vessels that descend from the head towards the eyes until the incision is continuous just as far as that which opens the wound, and then make another cut in the middle wound just up to the other side; and then extract the blood normally, and press out the leech for the blood drawn; then put a linen cloth in each wound, and place drapered moist cloths of wine and oil and herbs on top, and keep away from swelling; and on the third day unbind the bandage, and administer a large quantity of fresh water, and cure with basilicon oil with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Do not move your eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a certain catarrh comes to the eyes accustomed by nature, and you see the eyes cloudy and small, and weakened by the sight, and the papers burn; and the hairs fall out, and in the forehead there is great pain and the patient coughs; then observe these accidents that those materials and that catarrh come from only many veins, and the mother's cure, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to cover his forehead, then make a great incision in front of the forehead, and another small one behind.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the temple on the left to the temple on the right, and make the incision just up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the temples that move when you cut; and as soon as the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with an sponge, then dress between the two lips of the incision with wool cloth soaked in wine and oil; and be careful not to touch an abscess; when it is opened, it seems that you should rub the bone so that the blood will start to flow, then cure with things that burn or char.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner, take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of coal-tongue, and let them be soaked; and administer it in these wounds to ward off the evil for all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear stoppage
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is among the four things: grain, animal flesh, stone from mines, or similar things as iron; seed, like poppy, millet, beans; or something flowing, like water and ash, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or another kind of thing that does not adhere to the ear, nor grows in the ear, if one puts the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a little violet oil or sennet oil, and administer extraction; and make it vomit the condisi, and put in the nostrils when vomiting comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool into the ear; and put the ear under.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times comes fever by this cure; and if it does not come, take out the extraction with fine pins, for that is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If the needle bursts through the pin, that's good; if not, take out the extraction with a small, thin thread of cloth; and if it does not burst, make a ring of straw and pour hot water into the ear or ear canal very deeply, and stop up what is behind the straw with melted wax so that the needle cannot enter through the straw; then pull out the needle, for this often comes by the same way as we have said; and if it does not come in this manner, grab a handful of cloth because you will take out the ears, and put in some sort of instrument having a point to do this, and insert a little bit of cotton behind; then press the cloth onto the bone or whatever it is, and pull out the needle.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And instruct the patient to let go of all those things that we have said, so she hastily pierces her ear even before opening the abscess and causing spasms; and the manner of piercing is such that you first heal the patient from the head, and extract the blood according to its power, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear up high, and make a small incision at the root of the ear at the fatty part or where it depends, so the incision is as a crescent moon, until you arrive at the joint, then pierce according to your strength, and suck out hasteningly into your mouth; and the treatment will continue until she is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a swelling caused by pus and it cannot be extracted, then administer the poultice made of subtle mixture according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that sort.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make this when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many cuts; then extract with subtle pinches and on the surface, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water therefore what is cast into the ear should be used by the sick of mustard and comfits first, and fill the ear with fine cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And it can also be placed above that same ear or in the water itself.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it falls down because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	if it does not, then take many stitches according to the length of the wound should be tied and light, and put on hot ashes; and put the patient an arrow or a stud in his ear, and stand above one side, and press with another side, and fear from one bone over the bone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this until the water has become all done, and so it falls to be done; and if you see, take a joint, and poke an arrow into the ear, and put hot ashes on the other shoulder until the one is well warmed up; then make another joint of other arrows until the water becomes all done, as we have said in the bone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	When extracting the best part of an ear, if it is of small size, like a wart and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great size which can be felt, extract with pincers; and this is the thing that is easiest to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting the worms from the ear, mark the ear with wax while you cure it as we have said in the division and when treating distillations; but if this cure does not work, so that you may see which is the form: if no worms are seen, try using fine pincers, and if they cannot be seen, take a thread to find out why this is the case.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it may be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And pour the most subtle head in the ear according to the quantity of suffering in the patient, then suck them in all together; do this often until they all emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out as I said, put a cone of cotton inside the ear just like I said in the stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, administer enemas as the ancients have experienced in the operation of worms, and you will find them or treat with enemas; and infuse your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, for so is its form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is made of gold or lead, put a small hole in the little entrance, and above the overs pour out the distillation; and to press into the distillation with the well-made lead instrument for that, and when you see the razor and you pass it through the cotton along the edge, then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines into the tube, and let the tube be in the ear; then put the razor inside the cotton all at once, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled out or nearly from the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and so the distillations should be done on fire as they are being poured into the ear; and beware that they do not get too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the rupture of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a single hole in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults when there is an ear rupture, or from a blow inside the ear, and this ruptures sometimes come out of the ear if one cannot see; and at times there is a small defect, and the person sees very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	This one that comes out if one cannot see it is due to disease in more cases and in this case you must put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opilation apparent, then the operation should have taken place at this spot because of this form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And if it is old and wrinkled both in front and behind the ear, if the ear does not bleed; if the opilation is caused by a bone or part of the ear, if you have fine needles, and carefully cut so that this bone is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	If the inflammation is deep in the ear, then take a subtle razor and shave it lightly with hot ashes, then put on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the inflammation which the sick person feels great pain in the ear, then carefully shave it lightly, and keep that you do not weigh down the ears of the ear; then put a tent over the ear according to its large size and puncture, and apply poultice in Egyptian manner.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do this on any day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and apply poultice in rose water, and powder with vitriol crushed; and if you see that the ear has flown away, then cover it so that you treat the tent and move another tent which is moistened in cherry made of olive oil and wax, until the inflammation is removed; then cure until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If there is bleeding from the nose, plunge a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that take away the swelling of the nose which are used to treat nasal bleed.
de la char des papieres	about the ashes of paper.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Cover the eye with paper from the eyelids when they are wet and dry, so that you should stretch them out with tweezers and pincers, and cut off with a spoon-like instrument at its roots; then apply vitriol to it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	If without peeling, if the lens is cautered with subtle fire cautery, and the lens is cut after incision, it will heal; and it heals many times, unless anything remains in its roots; and when they are cautered by fire, those roots are burned off and do not return.
de la gresle	of the flesh
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	there are often times paper-like things coming out of the eyes which seem like flesh in shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called “grandine”, and it’s an assembly of gross moisture on both sides of the paper; the symptoms are such: take care if the grandine comes from one side and another, and this is a light thing to know; then do accordingly, make them larger, then scrape off each part lightly, then pick them up with pincers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot cut through the paper without piercing it slightly, so as not to harm the patient; and if a tear is large, if there is an opening or a seam in the assembly, and the treatment continues until it becomes healthy; and if it is small, do nothing further because the stitches will restore it immediately and bring on chagrin.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
de la graisse des eulz	From the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	This is a fatty substance that is woven into netting of paper above, and this often occurs in children with no one to take care of them, and they greatly suffer at their eyes, and they come the diarrhea in the mornings, and cannot look towards the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this they lie on their faces until, and sleep there, and are their papers moist above their eyebrows that swell and appear because of the exinach which opens in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the liver with your fingers and feel the exinach within it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way of opening it is that the patient puts his head on the healthy one; then takes a linen cloth, and makes a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach contained in each part, then places it there; and presses with your fingers from both sides so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moistness at the spot where you are cutting open a vein, making it no larger than the wound we make on the healthy vein; and make the skin tight enough until you reach the exinach; and in other positions, exinach comes out from the incision, according to the shape of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the cloth then to a whole piece of charcoal-soaked fabric between your two hands without fail, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread out; and guard that you do not add anything to the wound, lest you become infected with all the spatumile juice since the oil, lest you strike it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the arrow has not pierced in the beginning of the wound, then apply a small amount of the wound to make it appear; then cut as we have said, then bind with bandages easily and in water, and place on the limb, and tie around the joint.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if some of these men who cut up silks and put them on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure should be safe.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to a joint abscess, then the cure of emplastrumes applying so long as he is sanitized.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs from paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs from paper are born, other than nature's, and have grown old, they cause trouble to the eyes, and bring on various kinds of sicknesses, such as excessive sweating and skin softening, and pus, until it is a cause of eye destruction; and there is treatment in four ways: either by fire cautery together with hot iron, or according to medicine for those who are beforehand in cautery chapter, and made either by incision and suturing or by canes, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the patient's head on your safe side, then turn the paper of oil with your left hand; if it becomes smooth, it is good; if not, then cut off as much of the hair as is above the skin; and take the thread from under the paper, and turn it upwards over all the paper, and shave there; then make in the part underneath the paper, below where the hairs are stuck, a whole surface cutting, from the great laceration to the small; then pull out the thread, and place underneath the paper a small cloth of linen and silk, then sew above the paper an image of a needle, like the gall of myrtle, if you must see so it should be according to the size that you will lift the paper which is sketched all around.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Instruct the patient to put on as much bandage of paper as is necessary according to how the paper is softened; then do the entire procedure for the upper part that you have written two lines about, and begin with large stitches just like small ones; and let one of the incisions near the natural hair in the growth of a root, then pour some oil on one of the two corners of clean, then scrape all off; then assemble the two lips with a stitch made from an awl to all the fine threads of yarn, and bleed the wound, and dry the superfluousness of the hairs above the two wounds to all kinds of sticky things, if you see it being done like this; and if not, do not have any care, then let the stitches and hairs just three days or four; then treat the wound with dried and binding things, because the paper lives on the moment of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitching is weak (as the ancients said), and it’s a work without fear; and it is that you tie the paper with another figure which is like the fuel of myrtle, as we have counted, three times according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off the thing that is surmounting them equally according to their form.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the strength to hold the tongs, and they are not even, then prick an arrow or take a thread with it, and sew into the figure; and sew the other thread over the big gash, and the small one as well, and assemble the threads equally between your two hands; then tie your hand equally, and tie all the skin where you have stitched, as we have said before, and assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure until it is sane; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then assuage it with cerote and such-like ointments soothing; and sometimes happens that the hairs of the papyrus are converted: so it seems necessary to use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in both is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	Instruct the one who suffers from a gout as follows: and it is that you turn the paper and the finger inside according to what I have said, and then make two nails by art, and two subtle threads so long as the paper and the large space of the spatula are; and cut the two heads of the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above that which overhangs from the paper of the oil, and strain the two nails from the two parts formed; and let it be so for some days, and the skin who is stretched will harden and numb and prick, until it hurts by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it lingers, if the cut has some force, then the cure until he is healthy; and when the wound is sewn and the paper is lifted, and the hairs no longer ache; and this is the form of the two nails that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Instruct the patient to prick with an agile needle, and pour soft and subtle thread into the wound; then assemble the edges carefully and bind one and the other subtly, leaving space between the threads a palm's length; then order another subtle thread of silk quickly in the chase, binding well the chief thread; then put the patient's chief on your healthy hand; and expose to sunlight until the wound is declared clear, for it is a subtle and small wound. Then prick the needle all along the chase into the root of the attached hair, and make it pierce the paper hastily so that you may draw above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the chase, and pour into the chase that same hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then pull your hand until the hairs verge fire all along the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Et if the wound is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, so treat the wound beneath all the thread that you have ordered, until the wound appears to be full of pus above and what you see by the oil; then so treat the wound and the thread, and close the oil and let the patient close II days or III days, until the hair grows in its place and is born on the forehead; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the neck nature, and lift them with that which you leave, until they are stretched out and then release.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's rot
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the rot comes into the oil, there are two kinds of it: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And happens suddenly by a wound, or incision, or cauterization, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of this work is that you break that bond, and serve the lips with it, and put in linen tents, and tie it as long as it heals; and it is not fitting to use only those things for his cure which dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	But if you do that, the disease will return worse than before; but work with softening things, like fenugreek; and burn rosewater or aloes and let them be cooked in linseed seed, and use a fumigated oil on any of these, and wrap it up in a linen cloth, and perform his cure.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the secrets of your cure are that you protect yourself so that it does not become sour according to its original form; and those operations which we have said do not burn unless they are exactly like this disease, which does not return according to its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the charcoal that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is under that name "axacrati", and is truly called "accident" by nature.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of opening the vein if so that you prick an needle, in which it has two strands, and a thread in the charcoal, and then make piercing both sides starting with the left arm, until they come out at two joints of the head; then put the charcoal on top all over the needle, and strike at one span length.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper figure returns according to what you like, it's good; but if not, take a razor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two incisions on one side inside the paper; and so that the joints of the two incisions are at the two angles of the cut you made, and make an angle so that when they assemble, the figure will be as if of a letter with no "I" called "griesche"; then remove that charcoal according to how its edges were above, from what was written on the paper; then add both parts together, and sew with a thread of linen; then let him have the cure for what we said about soft medicines and poultices, until he is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	Et if the sickness comes from cutting or from sewing or from cautery, so it is fitting that you make a straight cut below the hairs of the paper-thin skin; and according to what was said before; then sew between the two fingers of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the shape of the sickness, for it is very diverse in shape, and the wise masters apply an engine of every kind of power so that it may return to its natural form; and the sick persons themselves, according to what they need of work and of instruments more often.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	Whenever this suturing has a strong hold on the hands in such a manner that the skin above is hardened with oil, and cannot move or do its natural work, so it is fitting then that you make a point of a rasping tool under the skin, and lift it up; and the extent as punctures, until you copy what is there with the fine stylus, which should not be too rough nor too sharp, so that the patient may suffer neither from being too rough nor from having the oil spoil; and make your incision, whereupon you scrape off that assembled mass lightly, so that the skin reverts to its natural form; and it is healed completely, without ever making a drop of oily salve or drawing out water, but then applying warm milk and vinegar; afterwards put between the skin and oil a linen tent, and put on the lard oil in abundance; and after three days use the poultice and other quick remedies until they are healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the unclean oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two kinds of pus: one is nervous and looks like the skin is raw, and another that is not nervous but resembles frozen mucus, when it is touched with iron and cared for in a pan, as if pinched by a finger, then it cannot be; and both of them begin to appear towards the great vein, and increase little by little until they cover the whole eye and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your healthy one, then they open their eyes; and they lift paper to your hand, then they sew as if pinching with small folds, and set it above; then take a needle, and put a piece of horsehair, or wool, or beefskin, and strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and stick it into the pus, and pierce all the way through the needle, and tie the pus with a thread and set it above, and scrape off all the hair on the cost of the pus that leads to the boil and the sores on the hair up to the head; then cut the remaining tissue in the root of the vein until the specified small amount of space, and leave the natural state of the vein, if the incision does not cause blood to come out from the veins accustomed; and sometimes the pus is only set aside, and with thread, as we have said; then scrape on all the space soft, for this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to keep the scabbard from touching the flesh and not to rupture it, and that the poultice should not be perceived; and after the incision, place a little bit of bruised grain in oil on the wound, and let it sit for just one day under the collar; then the cure will know what to do so that he may be cured.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nail is not swollen and you cannot push the needle in, and the nail does not enter, this condition of an ingrown nail is often cured with medicines; and just as I have explained in the division, if you cover it up, apply oil to the patient, and take the poultice lightly, in a soft manner according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And again take out the nail subtly, and if you see that it has not diminished at all and the reason is pressing, then distill from your mouth onto the poultice of oil, made with litharge, and into the collar, a crushed grain, and let the oil cool until the next day; then resume the other work according to the same operation, until it is completely hollowed out.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the oil, like an abscess on your foot, then let the pus, and cure the abscess first so it is healed, and then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	But if the appearance of the skin becomes red and swollen at night in the oil due to great inconvenience, if you lance a pus-filled abscess and remove only part of it, so that no blood comes from the wound; then distill coliere (aromatherapy) red oil which is made by litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the pupil.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	There are some men who never have red flesh, and cover the pupil and restrain it with paper and torn off (to prevent bleeding), and seem like a rose bud; and if wounds occur they make the patient put their head in good condition, then work on the eyes, and let that flesh grow with corresponding nails, and support them with strength; then cut the first piece of flesh, and go again cutting until the rasper reaches to the end, and beware not to bleed the oil at the work; and do like the incision of the spatumile which we have said in the incision of the ungue, and make small forces as if one removes wool, since it shows according to this chapter the shape; and when the incision is completed and all flesh has been removed, then apply oil of silk or distill coliere red and similar medicines corrosives, and put cotton on the oil with linen wool, so that it is secure of abscess; and if it remains nothing, and the wound does not heal, and you are sure of having an abscess, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with gentle things like abscess. Then return to your work until it is healed, and do thus cut flesh after being added in the oil by this semblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you alleviate the cure for each weak person through natural means; and of accidental means, in consideration of iron; and do not put your hand on any of these works until you see if this member is suffering from that injury.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes' veins
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These veins are red and covered on the eye's surface, and they tolerate their injury and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is then that, at the first sign of an eye injury, you look to see if it's red, if it's swollen, and if there are no other diseases but the eye; therefore, he should do this in the manner: instruct the patient to put his head on a healthy one, and then suspend those veins for as long as possible according to his wisdom, and let the delicate ones double up according to that form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two on each side according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then take out the veins gently, and suck the blood hour after another, until you see remove those veins from the oil; and be careful not to strike the oil with the points of the lancets, and do this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your operation so that you only suck out those veins; and when you have done that, distill collier vert and rouge vinegar into the oil to corrupt what remains in the wound.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to suck out all of those in that hour, then apply a plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it remain for some days until the pains have subsided and ensure that there is no abscess; then continue according to this form as before until you are cured.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	the arteries are called "arissati" fistulas: when you treat it with fire cautery and medicine according to what I have said, and it is not healed, there must be an infection in the one that you cut into, where it must die, and drain all the moisture that is in it, until the bones are exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bones are exposed, and you see the corruption and blackening, if it is all of that which is in this form; and it is called "aspere chief", and it should be made of iron into a spear head like this, and point them so as to resemble a lime so as it is in its present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the lead of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand as little as you can until you feel that this corruption is reduced; and do this not once, but restore the body with medicinal excipients.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the swelling of the joint is such that it cannot be moved and the bones are swollen, and remain thus for forty days, and it does not heal and is no longer an abscess, and accidents do not happen, know that he is healed; if this is not so, if there is no other remedy except to return the fistula to the perforated area in that form: and first uncover the bone the second time by iron, and with gentle medicines, and when it heals like before, take out the nails according to that form, and let the nails of iron be three angles, and the nail should be reduced as much as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place the nail on the bone near the marrow, and move your hand away from it a little bit, then turn around to the forest so that you feel the bone and the patient feels it when you hold your hand over his joint; and when you restore the healing of medicines dry, as I have taught you, and when the pain subsides and the swelling is healed, then put the material into the joint.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the oil's issue.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open all the time and they do not come to relieve the head, nor ease it, if you prefer to bind the patient; then put in ointments, put vinegar or honey to make them bleed, put on hot oil made of ice and aloe and incense and sarcocoolce, and then strain the oil, and apply plaster on of linen and cloths; and the way of the cloth is that you take linen enough, soft, and double it up four times, and then put one over another according to how much need the eyes have; then strain by putting under a stiff bandage, and reapply the ointments to bleed again to cut; then remove the ointments and leave the oil in binding day and night, and if you bind him well, so that he will break; then remove the bandage after the day and the night, and if you see the oil healing, it's good; but if not, reapply the plaster and linen and the ointments and the ventouses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	A drop of blood from a vein.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes to the vein, then it opens up and comes out with papers as if like grains of resin, and this is unbelievable to see; therefore, look on the veins covered, the work is such that you inject an awl into the root of the part below the joint above, then inject another awl where there is a double thread from the part of the shoulder; and pierce it, and let the first awl stick according to its position; then cut off the second thread and tie up one side of the vein tightly, and pull out the awl and apply olive oil moistened with more than enough oil; and let it be until the threads stick to the vein, then cure the oil on comforting things until the wound is healed; and at no time does the wound become restrained by the vein from each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes do great appearance, so apply to the spot in the subtle sponge that comes forth from the oil, and clean the moisture albino and descend the eyelids, and enter quickly then; afterwards extract it when it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the fat of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness called "alcunnati" is not hot except for the fat of the oil assembled in it, which resembles cold dripping down and is not actually cold; and the manner of its appearance is that you sit the patient upright on a special seat, then take the head between your hands two parts, and press the lump until you see the fat coming up to your eyelids; then place it there, do not let it fall or be dislodged, and watch how the lightness appears, and see what things appear to the patient as they usually do; and if it does not fall off, know that it is cold, and if the lump of the fat is assembled so that we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you sit the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and draw up the corneal tissue by continuing the conjunctive with the corneal tissue and the crown, until the bow becomes loose; and when it has become so, distill into the oil hot and sweetened with honey or fenugreek, or boiled and honey is added, then cure her with another cure until she is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil's water.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have similar properties of water in the division, and that is what it is required to pierce. If this is done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You must sit the patient between your hands crossed, with water of light from the sun, and tie the oil strong and tight; then put the paper of the oil on your left hand if their eyes are left-handed, or on your right hand if their eyes are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if their eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if their eyes are right-handed; then put the point of the instrument between the crown by the thickness of a finger, on that spot at the lower edge of the meniscus, then insert the "almagda" instrument virtueously, and turn your hand until it pierces into the meniscus, and feel that "almagda" comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the passage of "almagda" be at the bottom of the measure of the space between the kernel from the tip of the nail to the end of the blackthorn; and that's the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the corneal tissue, then put the instrument just there near the water, then express it through one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the pain of this affliction has now descended upon him, then let him see the patient in front of him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After he has rested for a little while, and the pain of this affliction returns to him again, take hold with the instrument, and when it is embedded and does not come out, gently draw out slightly by turning your hand now and then; and then put in a little seed of vinegar, and clean out the oil within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put the oil out by spilling or pouring a clean cloth soaked in olive oil and plenty of lye, and bind with the pure oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	So too, and those of our age, let us put on a common balm with plenty of lye.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	If the magenta cannot enter into the oil by its hardness, because it has two people who have too hard eyes, so you should take the instrument called "alberit", of which there is this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then cut the conjunctiva only, and do not make it too deep, but do it subtly, then apply magenta, as we have said; and when the work is completed, the surgeon should attend to the patient, because he will sleep on his dark side; and you must be careful with all movements, and give him light food, and do not move his head or right arm or left arm, and tie it according to his disposition for just three days; then release him in the same dark house, and check his sight, and make him see some things, and then he will be released after seven days; and it is not suitable that you do this in the room of treatment now or after the incision, but it is necessary to alleviate it, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	For the abscess of a tooth comes, that you cut out the oil on the seventh day, and follow the advice of the one who cures an abscess; and when it is appeased, so free the eye and cover it with the bandage for each day, and remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then some drops of the house come and it transforms into its form; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in some other lands he heard of a black pearl piercing, by which the water succeeds, but I never saw it or heard of it in any books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of alum, because they who do not know them see them incorrectly; and they are of pure arsenic.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the heads of the same subtlety, and the backs in threefold angle.
de la char sor le neis	of charcoal on the nails.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There are no times that nails grow with different kinds of charcoal, because there are some that resemble scorpions almost in their size; and if they have charcoal encrusted with multiple colors, or with soft charcoal of bone-like color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case then, when the charcoal is soft and not encrusted with flux, it is advisable to place the patient between your hands in front of the sun; open their nostrils, and apply some of those chars to them, and press on the fumers; because if you do this, as long as you can sustain the subtlety of the splinter, until you know that the charcoal is entirely loosened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is anything left that cannot be covered, if you apply all the remedies in subtle ease, so that it does not stay; and if you do not have to take shelter, or abscess, cut as it is fit; and if it is malignant abscesses, take haste and cauterize until they are stopped and the bones are set whole; then put out fire or vinegar, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If there is no wine and moistors come to the place of the palaces, know that he is healthy; and if moistors do not penetrate as it is fit, know that there is a bone hidden in the upper part of the bone, for which the humors come not to cut: then it is fitting that you give him a small thread of linen, soaked and tied with your hands, and having no space between; and put the patient's head into the thread at some power, and treat with odorant until it comes out through the nose inside the mouth; and many times this is done by children in schools, and it is an easy thing to do for one who wants to do it; then hold the chief that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other chief that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other while we are sitting on the linen.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Instruct the patient so much that you know none of them have corrupted that flesh, then take the son, clean the wound, and moisten the son in Egyptian ointment, and put him straight onto the bone as before; do this for 3 days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put on a chain of onions some days until he is healed, and if it needs medicinal herbs, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purgify the head, because they distill oils and medicines in the onion:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or lead, resembling a lamp overhanging, like a chain, and conduct it similarly; if you see, then make a chain closed, and let the instruments be plain for purging the head; and have one chain at the head to hold it when the oil or any liquid is heated:
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh at the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often it swells at the head of the neck a disease called "telul", and grows and becomes large abscesses, so that you can see something with the eye; and for this reason you must dress the wound at the beginning, and cut out all the bone, then apply heat to the cautery or medicine; and if it is left unclothed for a long time, so that it becomes hard, take care of it, if it has turned red like wood, of poor flesh: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, because when you cut it once, it comes to bad in the patient; and if the abscess is tender to touch, not at all from rough color, and you see that it can be entirely covered, then take away the pus from the wound and restrict it.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When they are struck and pierced
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is known that when a solution of continued continuity comes from one of these old cartilages, it profits little, whether in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
