It is therefore necessary to consider this when it happens to no one, if one looks and the wound is fresh all over; and then add two stitches on a seam, and tend to the patient until he is healed; and if the lips are torn apart from one side and the other, it is necessary that you scorch all the parts of their flesh so that they heal, then reassemble the two lips on a seam, and tie them, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and incense broken, and put over the powders a piece of emplaster of strong or another emplaster binding, and let it rest for as long as it falls off by itself, then tend to the patient with ointment until he is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is that you assemble the seam: or by needles, just as we have said in sewing under the belly; or by thread, as I told you.
des apostemes des levres	of swellings of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With the hand inside the lips there is a swelling, like grains of rice, and smaller or larger; therefore it must be turned back, and each lip cut open, and the wound made with pins and struck on each part; then take out with pincers, and apply vitriol after the incision until it bleeds freely; and then clean it up with this, and treat with ointments of dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
des sordens	Of sounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Never are the teeth assembled in the chief of the gums, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and sharp scales; and sometimes there is black and yellow and pus, until corruption comes to the gum, and they become foul. It is good to seat the patient between your hands, and have their teeth or scales visible, so that nothing remains; and thus do a dressing of blood and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are cleansed. If it is discovered that there is something at the first stage, this is good; if not, continue again on the second day and on the third day, until you have all cleaned out. Know that teeth need various forms of instruments to clean them, according to what the work shows, because the file from which we remove the teeth has other forms than the one that is used between the teeth; and these forms and others must be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth's pain that you wait as long as possible for the treatment because it should not be done in a hurry; because this is a very high substance since therefore we have no excuse for hesitating.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is forced to have treatment, it is necessary that you be certain about the tooth's quality.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain torments the patient, and suppose it is from a good tooth, and has that good tooth treated; and it is certain that the pain will not depart because of this, until the bad ones are removed, for we have never wanted to do these things with such physicians; and when you are sure about the tooth being sound, then it is necessary to scratch around the inside of the tooth thoroughly with a sharp instrument for protection against the gums on all sides; then take your teeth or pincers carefully at first little by little, until they are well cleaned, then fasten them tight; and put the patient's teeth between your own in your abdomen, and hold it tightly so that it will not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the right tooth directly into the fracture, and if it does not shoot through, take any of these instruments and pour them inside each part lightly, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are pierced and mangled, it is wise that you fill them with cloths, where or where they are missing; and if you tie them tightly with thin fingers, so that he does not break by straining; and it is most prudent to overwrap under the gum for to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take care well that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient by the pain in the root, for greater pains than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not make it in the same way as the ignorant masters do, who by their haste and bravery break the chariot sometimes, and bring nothing but what we have told; but sometimes they come to bring some from the source of this great sickness for the roots that remain, or for the chariot that they break, just as our desire often is; and when the tooth is strong, wash it with wine or with astringent or salve; and if bleeding comes, as it usually does, then apply the lead alloy.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the strumens should have their points long and large nails, which do not double up when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have large limbs if they do not bend when pulled out, and they should be made of iron well-made, and have teeth to hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays in after pulling, it is necessary to put on the same cotton moistened with butter each day or twice.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the cotton is matted, for it is recommended to push into it with tongs called "algefri", which make the chest seem like a beak; and they are made in such shape as a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge at all these ties, so it is fitting that you uncover the whole root under which is the tie, and put the instrument which is called "althali", namely plain lance, in order that it is this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is broken and large and it does not break at all, and the root jumps at this, that's good; but if not, then you must help with all the instruments, for the forms will come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument which has two roots, that's the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front on the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, that's the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	For the force of this cautery is that he cannot break it, and you know that many instruments are needed; and also of other instruments, which are not counted; and wise masters subtle will find their own instrument by themselves, according to what his works and the illness show him, for there are some illnesses where the ancient do not teach any instrument because of the diversity of these and if it breaks or shatters on the earth or on other bones, so he seeks out the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with movements, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting so that they can hold the bone, but not break it; and then restore to him the suitable medicine, if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, then he should take all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not in their natural form and are ill-shaped, and even in young girls, it is necessary to know that if the teeth have grown after the tooth, they are not in their right place, and cannot be sorted or put in order: then take the file; and if it is dry with the tooth, so take this instrument which has this form, and it resembles a small beak, and is made of good iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file touches and touches in every jaw for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears as if it can be sorted, take a piece of file as is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also as the file of which we make the needles; and in file the tooth touches and touches in every jaw lightly, so that it does not move until it chips; then the flat part at the end has all a smooth surface, and if the teeth are too pointed, they will bleed on the tongue, so it is necessary to sort out the sharpness as long as it is even, so that it does not bleed on the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth lock
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth lock, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press them together so that they bite, and you treat them with medicines restraining them, but it doesn't work; if they need to be restrained with a thread of gold, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold does not move at all; and let the thread be neither too fine nor too coarse nor too small, according to the space between the teeth. If you see the teeth falling back, take the thread and insert it double between two healthy teeth, then put the stitches between my teeth, if there is one or more, until you see that they are securely fastened on the other side of the tooth; then resume covering just where you started, and carefully and gently pull out your hand so that it does not move at all; let my tie be loose to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Instruct the patient to cut off hair with scissors and assemble them, and put it between the healthy teeth so that it does not hurt his tongue; and then let it be tightened as much as possible until it bleeds, and if it comes loose or breaks, tighten it again with another thread; if it remains thus for a while and serves him well, that is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of two healthy teeth and two unhealthy ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, fresh as before, just like we have said; and do not introduce anyone who is untrained and suffering into this work, for at no time is the form of a bird bone tooth made, and put it back where there is deficiency, and tighten it as we have said, and keep doing so for a long while.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	For a ligature that comes from below the tongue or naturally, is thus born; or by accident of a burn wound; and the injuries are such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and hold his head to your own, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve of the tongue wide open until the tongue is loose from its place, and if it has dried up or not, and it is due to sudden injury, then insert a needle and cut wide open that ligature; and be careful that the wound is not too deep by the artery that is below; and when you have done this, lift the head over cool water and salt, or cold water, then put under the tongue a cloth of linen; and bind the tongue each night, so that the swelling will not occur.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If blood flows from the wound, put vinegar on it and break with a broken glass; if they do not bleed, then apply fire to the cautery in slow movement, which is good for them; then treat with another treatment until they are healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a warts color or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, so that no one touches it, because it's a chancre; and if it inclines to blisters and it has moisture, then take off the tumor, and do with a fine spatula, and deliver from both sides; and if they do not bleed at your operation, put vinegar on broken glass until they are stained, then return to your operation, treating all thoroughly; then lift up the limb gently and securely, and treat with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Evacuation of abscesses from the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There is no occasion when the throat has boils that are called "godath", and if one names them properly as two glands, and when you treat them, as we have said in division, they do not heal, be cautious: if it's an abscess of little sense and fusiform color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it's red and the root is big, do not touch it with iron, for the evacuation of blood; but leave it until it dies, then you will cut it off, or it would burst on its own; and if it has a white color that turns back, and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to cover it, but first examine whether the abscesses are closed and have healed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And then instruct the patient to sit in front of the sun, and let his hair be clean, and he opens the mouth and the surgeon presses the servant between his hands, and pushes the tongue down with all the instrument, so that this is the shape; and it should be made of silver or subtle gold just like our scales:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if take onion and thrust into the honeycomb, and pull it out above what you can; and pull no other thing from the netting, then cut with the instrument, so that this is the shape, which resembles a force; and look at the chief are curved, and one end the other, and are very fine, and made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, cut with shears, so that it is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Instruct the practitioner to cut both sides and name them; and when you have cut one of the glands, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot and cold water, and cold and warm, until blood is discharged, if not then cook apple skins or myrtle flowers and similar things, till they are dry, then continue treatment till the patient is healed; and sometimes there will be another abscess in the throat besides the two glands, which when cut as such, do just as the two glands fasten.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was near the throat, specifically the small gland; and I had closely closed her entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the constricted passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she remained in this state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high that they had been put in two wounds on either side of the navel.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Therefore I immediately, and sewed in one of them, then applied a burning solution, and took a great portion of bowel; then sowed another in the other opening on the navel, and applied the tongue to it and pressed it hard; after that sewed the onion in these abscesses, and cut off part of it, and there came out only a little blood; and thus began to treat the swelling of the throat, for now she could drink cool water and then wine, and did not stop cutting at the abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing, and filling up the cavity that I had emptied, until it became very big; therefore I applied some pressure and cauterized inside the throat: thus endured without increasing for a while; and I left those parts, and I do not know but God made them better after me.
de l’uve	Of the ulcer
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it protrudes to the ulcer and it is inflamed and it is long, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is of a larger size and rounded, it is called an "ulcer".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cut so that we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit at all, and you see that the swelling of the abscess is diminished, and it is subtle, then it is fitting to copy it; and that which is rounded and is not long; and if it is bloody or has a flesh color or black, it is fitting to remove the incision from the wound.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great risk on the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its size and shape, you must seat the patient in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument whose mention we made before; then insert a needle into the ulcer, and draw it out slowly, and cut at II fingers' worth of the II instruments which I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is fitting that you not cover more than the natural surplus; for if you do so, it will grieve your voice and speech, and after the incision, use what we have said about the incisions of the two almonds, and care for the patient until they are healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of cutting, it is fitting that you use an engine at the cautery of their fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of the cautery is like water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts their head on your healthy one, and then presses the tongue with the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and mixes it with hot vinegar juice, if not too thick nor too clear; and employing the tip of this instrument, which is thus shaped:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the cautery, whether it be done by incision or cautery. If it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take camphor and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avocado and similar herbs, and mix them all together in a pot, and put ash easily, and make boil; and the pot must be well glued to a piece of bone, according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it can be of silver or lead, and one of the horns is put in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises through the nose by the heat, until the nose is numbed; after that repeatedly, until the nose dries, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the advent of the fever, for many things happen, and do not make it unless during the decline of the fever.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	In case the instrument is not present, take a thorn and insert it into the head of the patient, so that the mouth does not get too hot; for the cold thorn does not weigh down the breath, and this is a good treatment to save the person.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often when there is a sore at the throat or from a fishbone or nothing, you should treat what you can see, and press the tongue on the sun for the entire instrument, so that you see what it is; and if you do not know and something returns to the throat, it is best to make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it worsens with vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, a piece of bread, a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread, and ties the thread to it, then takes it out, and if it does not come back due to what we have said, take an instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Instruct the curved instruments to be placed in the neck so that it can more easily enter into the throat, and lift the head upwards; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all of the breath comes out or else push the bone inside; and moisten well that the patient may spit on the instrument, because he will moisten whatever is there; if the patient spits it up, or carries the thing forward to make the entire instrument equal, until they are done.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the cauterizing of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is medicine applied to the cauterized throat, as I have said in division, by the cure of medicines; and if it does not benefit, then look at the patient's throat in the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound open, then if it has just one small thread or has very fine nails.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	But if that does not work, then take a candle hair, and pour it into the patient's throat, and pour or burn the length of the iron hot, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is poisoned with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and operate the mouth, and let it swallow in that direction, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the wound feels the water, vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	But if she does not vomit as we have said, then submerge the patient in assesfete, at the instrument I told you for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, because she will fall with tarrier.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the maniere of the fumigation is that you take an ember or where there are coals visible, and it has a cover set over it in mid-air, and in that pit are the keys of the instrument; then take your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes just to there; and now the humbug will come, and if it does not come out, you repeat the fumigation several times; and let the patient suffer thirst, eat unclean things and ashes, and do not drink any water; and then the instrument is done by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which you treat the humbug is such that when you can see it, it appears like curved tongs for nails to enter into the throat; and has the appearance of a beak, and has roughness of lime, so that what takes hold of it, will not let go; and thus it looks:
li chapistres des apostemes	The medical practitioner's hand is useless
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what is remembered in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it's two kinds, one being like the other, and because of that, it gets moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is for when they are inside or in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because the abscesses of the head are different from those in the lower body, and the abscesses in the thigh bone are different from those that come into joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if it is not necessary to pierce them, until the bowel has dried out according to its completion; and if some of those who require piercing must be pierced when they are sure, but do not die according to their completion, just like abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from the joint, and it is left until it is putrid in that place, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is on the main part of the limb, and if you delay perforation until it has died, if it harms the principal limb; or it is on the foundation, if you pierce it so that it dies; and it should not be pierced with an abscess when one believes digestion to have been completed, because fire that is on the foundation will cause it to decay deep into the bone, and a fistula will form, and it cannot heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the size of the perforation of the abscess when it has died according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of the fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the easing of swelling and the sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it should be necessary that you make the perforation sit higher according to its position from the abscess, where it opens; or the perforation on a long part of the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or joints, nerves, arteries, and wherever they are equal, without any pressure.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When this part is swollen, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the groin, so that you value (value to leave) the perforation until it is confirmed to be completed digestion accomplished, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it in front of that one, the body will let loose its venous blood and it is full of much filth; and by chance its lips harden and its depths become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is perforated according to the size of the body, according to that which the limbs have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	It is necessary to perforate small abscesses, small breaches; and large abscesses, large breaches, and many openings according to the resemblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is suitable to apply the poultice, and cover; when it has become like an old rag, and has lost its power, then it is necessary to do as one does with blisters: and if there are those that have been divided into three angles, and those whose opening is made like a bee's comb, abscesses of anger; and if there are those where you make a round shape, and other shapes and seeming perforations.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	In the case of those who have no head, such as an abscess that is soft and superficial, it is necessary to pierce the skin completely; and it is also necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected a great amount of pus, and you pierce it, so that you do not take out all the bowels in that hour, but only one part; then stop the abscess just the day before next, then pull out nothing more on either side; do this many times with great care, until the bowel is completely gone. At the same time, if the patient has weak vitality, or a woman carrying it, or small children, or old men who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	But the expectation is that it will not occur again at all with the outcome of the bowel, lest by chance the patient dies, and you do not take consolation.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct then this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if it heals, and look to see if the wound is small; and if it's a plain incision, sew it up with linen or old cotton; and if it's large incisions and many are broken, it's fitting that you put one stitch in each so they don't come against each other; and if you have pierced the abscess in part of the skin and tied it inside, it's fitting that you fill it with old cloth or rags of linen dampened with moisture, and tie it up every day; then apply the bone, and the dressing of ointment until it is sane.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood comes out of the incision, sew it up with a moistened cloth and linen, and tie on over it repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to persevere with bloodletting if they are recovering, and give them good government and treatment, and the powders that I have said in this book, in your hands; and if it is now winter, and the pus is much nervous, it is necessary that you put on tents and soft drapes in wine and oil; and if it is in this state, and the pus is foul-smelling, it is fitting that you put on soft drapes in water and oil, or in wine and oil melted, just like we have said every three days; and then remove the abscess and clean it up and treat it, as it seems necessary, until they are sane.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is fitting to be known universally about the treatment of abscesses: for I have told you how to approach before performing abscess treatments, and this chapter.
des soros	The sorrows
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come from on the head, and are of various kinds, like in cloth, just as those from a piece of cloth, or similar to those from a mouse's skin, and there are many such.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and others like those that come from moist flesh, just as they come from fat. And there are also those that are hard and stone-like to cut, and there is no doubt in such cases when the artery does not cause a change.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the injuries of the groin are such that if you have found in all the instruments called "entremisoire", of which the shape comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	Because if it contains moisture, they cut through with the long ones.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	In the case of moisture being absent, if you want to clean without leaving anything on the skin where that moisture was, because it will return when you leave nothing; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and wool, and apply the wound with oil, and leave it till the next day; and those who are left over at night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the bandage, until you see well that it will not stay overnight; then treat the wound with ointment suitable to the patient, until they are healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	If the abscess holds firm, cut it according to this form, long and deep; strip off your skin, scorch from all parts, and put on all your care of treating the wound or where it lies; and if the artery makes it contrary, do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus also do with the abscess if it is pained, and as you cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting on the painful abscess and the moisture, if it is lighter, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are any of these abscesses or head wounds with no moisture, and such like the ones I copied from an old woman's head; and I found this abscess just as hard as a cold, rough stone, which cannot break, and if anyone had pierced it, they would have done just as well a wound as one made from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come or head wounds, however those which come on the child's head and at the roots of the ears, cut open wherever it is so that the bone may be made to emerge; and treat as it seems fitting.
des scrophules	dead sores
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often happen abscesses at the throat, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes appear elsewhere on the body, and are very painful, and join one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each dead sore is properly located in its own place, just as the abscess and the boil of the head, which we have said; and the symptoms of these sores are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malignant and will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then where you see a person with good disposition at the elbow, and is similar in color to the body, and mute from all parts and is not hot in the neck or artery or vein on the arm, nor deep; it's necessary to copy from above, and scrape off from each part, and keep both lips moist as in abscesses of the head; let it be slow and slow, and be sure that you do not scrape the nerve or vein, and do not pierce too deeply, lest you cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	Instruct the patient to let the vein or artery bleed if that does not stop bleeding, apply vitriol to the wound or use any powder that stops the bleeding, and bind the wound; and let it be so until the abscess is closed, and the wound becomes soft, and begin to clean.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the skin is clean, return to your work until you complete it; then seek advice from someone else if the wound does not heal for small sores, cut and lance them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If there is great blood in the root of the sore vein, it is not advisable to cut that sore at its root, but rather tie off one end with a strong double thread and let it fall out without causing harm; then apply the wound with Egyptian ointment and cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you strike the scrofula, it is necessary to assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, for there will be no more swelling because of the great size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is necessary that you understand to cut at the root of the thing, and apply force, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that hold swelling, cut into it or open; and cut as we have said, in dependence on the location, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, if it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, apply the poultice of ointment, until he is healed.
de squinance	of suspicion
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient people spoke about sewing the throat, but I have never seen it done in our land, and that is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	It is necessary to close the cut of the throat that is called "epiglottis"; and do not give aid to this, because all the veins and the flesh of the patient are affected by those who have inflicted wounds in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in a state of purging, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to escape the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four small cuts through, between the two circles or according to the size of the cut on the surface, not in the cartilage; and thus if it is made in this way, no bone remains, and the vessels are long in coming.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then it is fitting that he stretches the skin of the throat to its entire length, then cuts the wound so that it comes to a point when the blood starts to flow; and removes the stitches of blood, if you see anything, and then strikes at the sac, as we have said; and it will be shown by the section of the femoral vein which bursts through the joint that is broken, and by the voice defect; and let the wound be left to heal over one piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed in which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound at the cut and the entire surface so that it be whole up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause birth, until he is made whole.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	But do not perform this operation until the throat is entirely stuffed and the patient is judged to be on the verge of death and has begun to fail.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Instruct the patient to close the throat so that he cannot inhale, and he breathes through the wound, and thus death is guarded off; and because the ancients ordered him to leave the wound uncovered until the malady is passed, and it is passed in three days or four, then they commanded him to sew the wound and cure it, until it is cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took out her knife, and put it in her throat, and cut off some of the fatty flesh around the womb; and I was summoned to cure her, and found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found out that blood had come out of it, and I knew well that she hadn’t cut into a vein or carried it to her neck, but that the veins had burst out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I have hastened and sewn the wound, and cured it so that it became healed; and it happened to the young girl that she was red in the throat, and returned after her condition; therefore I say that there is no fear of having a sore throat in the larynx.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	The swelling of the abscess is called "thorn of the throat", and it is a large swelling in the color of ebony, and it is much in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; or if it occurs naturally it has no ingenuity.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is according to two manners, because one is like fatty flesh, and the other is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it does not seem wise to apply hot fires, except for those who are small, and prove and search along the entire interior: if you find it in the same way as fat tissue, and there is no desire to harm it, if you cut it, just like one cuts into us, and draw out all its contents, if there is any; and search well everywhere, and cure it as it should be, until it becomes completely healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many kinds of us (injury/evil), and I will say all the similarities; and it is necessary that I tell you all the difference that exists between injury and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that when an issue exists and fever remains, as long as the burnings (inflammation) are not passed, and it is completed by putrefaction; then rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	When an injury does not have heat, fever, or pain, and contains the abscess, which is its own sack and according to the color of the body, and begins as a lump, and grows so that it becomes large; and are according to such similarities, or graining, or moisture, and much in color, like what I said in division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of one not known, that you examine and inquire first at all the instrument which is called "entromissoire", according as its form comes or to chapter who follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way of the inquiry into the abscesses is that you prick or more moisture in it than you find inside the abscess, and turn your thumbs little by little, until you know when the instrument has pierced the vein, then as according to the size of the abscess; then pull out the "entromissoire", and take care not to burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the corrosive is cut short, as it has color in it, if it penetrates like I have said with other abscesses; and if after that the instrument does not come out moist, know that it is fatty, then make a cross mark on it, and take hold of it with pincers, and carefully shave it lightly from each side and protect the coat where it lies in order to treat it sound with the nose.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it stays in one place, it will return again and again; and if it stays for a little while without causing any pain, apply the wound with some corrosive powders sharp, hold the wound tight, and put on soothing things such as caustic powder, and treat other treatments until the patient is healed; and if the swelling is great, cut off two fingers of the wound, and treat the one who brings on the rash.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is swollen or inflamed in a different place when it suddenly happens, and you hasten to apply vinegar of vitriol, break it into two parts after one or three days, until the wound has closed, and let the swelling subside; then return to covering that which remained untouched.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of interstitial strumae, and they come in three kinds: great, medium-sized, and small; and among them there are three quarters called "albaret", and one called "breb"; and also there are three kinds: large, medium-sized, and small, to enclose fistulous tracts; and they are like the needles with which you sew wounds, made of citron wood, iron, or silver; and they are worth a great deal for those who have yellow pus, and they are more prized than anything black due to their enclosure of fistula corrobears.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of tumors are of great similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and those with two cornees in three manners also; and those with three cornees, and are in three manners; and those with two corneas, and a single cornea only, and are in three manners; all these are necessary for their treatment.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these wounds are cut with a sharp edge, and some of them have only one incision, which causes the nerves to burn, so that you do not cut the vein or the nerve; and these incisions are returned into small incisions in the hands, so that the patient does not lose anything when opening the abscesses; they come in three forms: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one should use no more than in the joints, such as elbows, knees, wrists, and ankles, and similar places; and sometimes a small other instrument is made, resembling scabbards of fistulas, according to this form, when one stains with blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put him on no occasion by the healthy person who has coped with veins, and arteries, and never again in that great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never do the breasts of some men swell when they begin to corrupt, until they resemble the breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, if it is necessary to follow this form along that line from b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound by pouring vinegar, then assemble the two lips of the wound on the side with stitches, and treat until it is healed; and if the nipple turns inward and swells as in women, if it forms two scars above, in two places like this: for so one stays attached to the other at the end of each, since the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from line b to line g; then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we said about stitching and powders, and all that is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completed entirely, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the corruption of blood, so you must fill the wound with wet cotton cloth soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it brings out the remainder and the fat, then treat until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the joints.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from under the joints are hard swellings or have ribs, and if there is moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those that contain moisture must be closed according to this shape, from the line .b. up to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowel that is in the abscess is empty, apply the wound with old cotton, and let it rest until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment suitable for that until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like swellings of scrofula, do it as we have said in cutting open scrofula wounds, and if the wound has a bowel, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the cauterization of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut, and the skin is sewn over it above, if many abscesses form, and just as often the vein swells and abscesses; and when one suspects that it's from the artery, if there are long abscesses along its path; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a strangulation; and when it's due to the vein, you see red signs appearing; and this is madness to cover up these abscesses, and just as much so when they're located under the joints and around the joints and near the neck and along other parts, and they are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.
