It is therefore necessary to cure the iron cauterization, and one who has a head should also be cured similarly, and in that who has swelling of an artery, perform it above the skin; then open the chest with needles, and carefully cut through the arteries until they are discovered; then insert a needle into the artery on the other side, and tie it with a double thread in two fingers; then keep the patient tied between the two ligatures for as long as there is no bleeding; then apply the cure that has been poured out of the bowel, until the ligature ceases; and if necessary, apply this again to what is left of the artery, according to what I have said before, with a thread from one part of the two fingers; and if you doubt whether the threads will not come loose, insert another needle through all the thread under the remaining swelling, and tie them in four fingers; then cut off the swelling as much as possible, then cut off the excess skin at the knife's edge and leave what is tied; then place a moist cloth with vinegar and oil on it, then keep applying cures of tents and oignements until he is sane.
des apostemes des ners	From the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	When an abscess comes from the artery and vein, it comes to the nerves when they are dried up, or due to excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the joints and bones where there are many joints, and it's an abscess, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and is more prone to death; and when they are strained too tightly, the patient feels pain, and it doesn't come from the strength of the body, but from the wound itself, and is mute in all parts, and does not move forward or backward, nor upwards or downwards, and one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: by chance, it may cause contraction; and those who are on the head or forehead, make a mark with spatumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have tongs, and cut it in its root; and if it's large, if you press on the lump, scorch, then pull out the bone and assemble the wound to the ribs, and hold the cure until he recovers.
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There is no case in the stomach and not at any other part of the body; it's a disease that's called "fungus" because of its appearance, and has subtle roots and large stones; there are small ones and big ones; I saw one man who had two swellings in his belly that were like fungi, but unlike anything else, and they weren't different from any other fungus, and they were white, and had fine roots, and they burst open, and became rotten with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copy them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI Z., and the works in the incision are such that you look whether the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is bluish and moist and has a subtle root; if he cuts at the spatulum large, and so be in your presence the cautery with fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	But when cutting comes many times too great bleedings of blood, and if he does not beware, then hasten to the cauterizer; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with iron, take a fine thread well made, and tie the artery as we have said, and let it be two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the thread until he cuts the artery, and feel by him the work; and if the roots are thick, there is fear in cutting himself on the abdomen, but you can cover half of it, then cauterize so that he does not bleed again; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cauterize the part with fox-colored flesh and poor sensation and raw edge.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is an enchantment of an abscess, and I have come to this cure for the chancre after.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil exists.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or a cut on a suture, and is on the abdomen with some boils, as it happens in other routes, such as when veins are cut or arteries are slit according to what is before, or from a wound; and if this is by the route of the suture and through the boil, then its color is like that of the flesh, and is a light thing with pain, and opens with diverse issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the outcome of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press on both sides so that it returns, and then comes back, and by chance it gets scarred, and becomes much larger at the entrance to the bath and for great work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	Et se c'est pour moistor, c'est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it suits you to leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to a tumor or a boil, instruct the patient to tie his girdle, and stretch himself straight, then pull out as far as possible towards the bruise; then order him to lie still between your hands, then go around the limb you have marked with chalk; then cut open half of the abscess above at all the large joint; then tie it tightly around a strong thread or cord of fine silk firmly, and keep it loose like an allowance; then open half of the abscess stretched out on the thread, and pour your medicine into it, and take the intestine; if you find the tumor caught in the thread, release it, and pour the intestine according to the wind; and if you find the boil, cut off the surrounding superfluous tissue; and if the artery does harm or the vein, go carefully towards them; then return to your work and take II needles, and pour II strong threads, and pierce the two needles as we have pierced before; then strain the abscess in four leus above the needles, and if you see, loosen the needles, and let the limb remain until it becomes firm, and cut off the dead flesh by yourself; or when they are gone with subtlety and disappear, then treat the cure as needed, and cut the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the limb as needed, and close the limb.
dou chancre	dough chancere
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in division about the characteristics of a chancre and how to treat it with medicines, and how not to use iron treatment; we say that a chancre begins in the armpit, and there is great care required in its cure; the ancients say that when chancres are in you, where you can scratch them as one scratches a sore on the breastbone, or in the groins, and similar places, and you should remove it all at the beginning; and when they become large and old, do not think it is safe to approach them, because I have never seen anyone heal from such, nor has any been healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the surgeons, when it is in you or can be removed, as we have said, are that you purge the sick person of black bile once; then make them healthy if they show signs of repletion, and then make the patient good for having a chancre; then apply your ointments or sores, and cut off the head from all parts, and leave nothing of the bone in any part; and let the wound heal completely, and expect well that the patient will be healthy at your hands or with anything, and if they bleed from the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until there is no more bleeding; then give them another cure until they are healed.
de ydropisie	From dropsy, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	As we have said in the division of dropsy and how it is formed, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each kind, and the cure that is done with medicines, and the one that is cured by iron: if only one cavity remains; and do not touch with iron in these two similarities: this means tympanites and phlegmon, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you treat the similarity of dropsy called "eclites" with medicine, and the patient does not benefit, examine whether the patient is weak or has another illness besides dropsy, such as inflammation of the stomach and similar things; do not touch with iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient strong and healthy, and only suffers from dropsy alone, and is neither too young nor too old, then so: lift the patient straight up by your hands, and the attendants press the abdomen towards the lowest part of the belly, then take out the thorny spatula according to this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And so are the rules of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Pointed instruments should not be so deeply inserted that they can come into the intestine when they are thrust in, and it cannot be closed; then check if there is an inflammation on both sides of the intestines: if it is advisable to cut down on the right side of the third rib; and if it's for liver disease, then you should cut on the left side of the third rib; and if it's for the stomach, then on the right side. And it's not good for patients to have an opening that allows the excess fluids to flow into a weak part. Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, insert it, and lift your hand so that the sponge-like material comes out between the skin and the suture as if you were scraping away until the quantity of one nail; then pierce the suture up to when the sponge comes out to eight, and that's where the liquid flows in; then pull it out and insert this instrument which is the shape.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It is like a fine silver chain, and it is made of iron or archer's nails lighter, and in the lower part there are small holes; and on one side there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one more on this side; and the bones are cut as if they were feathers, and that is the shape of the incision from which the scribes write feathers:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it is the alamel, so when the instruments come near the water, pull them now up against the instrument; empty then only a third or half of it, because if you empty more than it's due for that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit in the arm, or he will cry out, or he will approach death; but empty according to the quantity of the patient's virtue, and according to what the signs of the virtues mean, and their feet; then take up the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now by the pressure that stops the hole above the syphac, which I spoke of, so you must pierce in this manner; then continue with the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering from it, and take a small amount of water; do not do this one day only, and keep yourself from fooling about until he no longer takes but a little bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the patient, and let them take much medicine, if the cure applies a poultice or hot sand, and then has them sweat or take a bath in the sun, and if they drink broth; and the cure gives medicine to desiccate their humors until they are healthy, and cauterizes on the stomach and liver and spleen after the extraction of the fever, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the swelling of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	There is never an infant born without any swelling in the penis, or if there is swelling, it is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it seems that soon they will pierce at all the sensitive places, very subtle and according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Instruct the patient to put on a tunic made of thin cloth beneath their clothing, and tie it and your belt in such a way that it remains so for three days or four. And when he wants to urinate, if there is an opening in his bowels, then sew it shut, make him urinate, and then remove the stitches; and by chance, if nothing comes out, because the urine that comes out does not leave a wound closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is in his foot, then put on a tunic made of thin cloth, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have an opening in their own body are affected, because none are born with the opening in their head of the penis, for that prevents them from urinating before they lift up their penis to relieve themselves; and they cannot defecate because the matter cannot come down until it reaches its final destination, and this is a very bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to lie on his back, so that his chest is raised, and you stick the head of a needle into him just as high, as if it were as long as a grain of wheat, so that the puncture wound opens up in the middle, so that it may occur; and be careful not to let blood come out which often happens, and if it does, when he bleeds stop the bleeding, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	from pimple of the prick
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	and often there come cysts on the prick, and it is an ugly appearance; and in some cases are malignant and not malignant; so you should pick them at one subtlety, cut and lance all of them, then put cotton wool soaked in Egyptian ointment on the wound; and cure with a defibrillating ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the bath is malignant, of a foul odor and stench, it is fitting that you should apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the bath is in a warm place, and has both parts inside the flesh and also outside, it is fitting that you should remove the part that is inside first; and when it is hot, take out the one that is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat the whole together, it is not certain whether the joint of the vertebra will be felt, and then there comes blackness and corruption to the vertebra and on that spot; it is fitting to remove all that which is black and corrupted, then cover with the plaster made of honey and flour, which is made from the rind of pomum greanium and vinegar, then the cure does other treatments until it is sane.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if they bleed from the wound comes, so apply lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is effective in two ways: it is applied as follows - to bleed and to corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, so that you push or draw out the penis of someone who has not been circumcised because they have a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to burn him with a heated instrument on the shank, until the ligaments are loosed, and the head of the penis is released from all parts; and if this is a painful thing to consider, then so that you burn him with a scabrous spoon one by one, near the top of the penis and skin; then sew well between two, and put in a subtle linen strip soaked in cold water, so that it does not come to a head.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a source of continued illness like other wounds; it is allowed by all because we do this work with our own will, and especially in children, since it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest to bring health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not say that circumcision was done for their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have sought the greatest part of the masters and doctors who performed circumcision in India, Egypt, and everywhere else, and acquired many forces and novelties; since the keys were lost because they had two sets, and by chance someone was killed above and that below remained.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	For the recovery cover, and it is the patient's pain double, and at the purification which is dull when the tip of the member is not secure; and by chance in purifying the limb may escape the iron, and the ulcer heals, and many times are born thus as they have need of purification, and I know.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is made with force, all along the whole tendon of thread I have found the good fortune of the experiment, because the forces cut exactly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, the fingers are equally cut all along the whole line of thread; but if the thread is well tied inside the skin; and if the manner of the first operation is such that you make the child think it is being tied around the vein so only, and then set it aside in all possible ways that you can; then take it between your hands straight, and release the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them or any other deformity; then put your hand on the vein and blow out the wound, and pull it up as high as the joint is cut; then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled there; then tie the new bandage with a double thread, then tie it under the other bandage; and take hold of the second tied bandage by the pouch and the dovecote, and clip between the two bands, then pull up the wound quickly and lift the head of the vein; then let the blood seep little by little, because it's the most gentle thing; and apply powder on top and inside the powder glue made with a moieuf of dried rose water, congealed with good olive oil and fresh, and leave it above the other day, and cure with another cure until it is sane.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The two shoulder joints should be tied together and be cut in the same way, and they should be cut as large as the middle finger.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the mundification is when the keys [likely referring to veins or tendons] inside are cut with the incision; therefore, it should be extended to your joint, so that the skin makes an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold it to your joint, if you have claws [presumably referring to fingernails], then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it transpires three days and the one below the vein is inflamed, then let him wait until the skin abscesses are healed, and lightly scrape it; and cut as you can move, and guard yourself from the part of the vein, for it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the joint of sudden pain from powder wounds which we have said to treat with powders, and if they strike at the joint out of proportion, and it goes above, so as not to cause harm; cure then, just as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	When retention of urine occurs
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	When retention of urine occurs due to obstruction of a stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or gall stones, or similar things which we have said in the division; and if the urine does not come out, and you see that the retention is caused by the stone lodged at the neck of the bladder, so as to make the patient stoop his knees; and the knees be placed on his back, and he extends his belly from the top of the back, and restrains the patient until he can; and thus constrains the necks of the bladder to express the stone above, because the urine does not come out; and if it comes not as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, so as to require extraction of all the equipment called "siringue", for this reason: it is made of thin, light silver wire, like a bird's feather; and it has a chain of a palm-and-a-half length, and is subtle in shape.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides. des maladies de la vessie	Of urinary afflictions

de la piere	From the stone

I say that stones in the bladder occur more often in children, and this is a sign that they have had an accident of blood similar to the bladder's subtlety; and they become inflamed, and the patient's penis hurts, and they cut it repeatedly, and then enure. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	But there is no use when it comes to cutting the stone.

puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. de hernie carnouse	of a swollen hernia.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non. Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this mucus is weak that it comes to the joints, and spreads out that material.

de l’aposteme des coions	From the abscess of joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Says that in the cutting of this branch there is much suffering and many deaths, which I think it would be better not to do; and I will tell you about the origin and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that most of the abscesses come from the body, and similarly from the joints; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	Which is to say that it comes from superfluity of sour and bitter fluid which spreads to the joints or by percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and does not cause pain, but is an abscess of a sore kind; and sometimes there are some abscesses sore and painful, and of a purple colour, and at other times it comes from nowhere else than an artery or an inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not by an artery, so it appears from the shape of the abscess, when you press on your two fingers; and do not be so bold as to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	This one who has swollen vein is known by its shape when touched with the fingers of the two hands, and you can well make the incision on this appearance, and on the other marks; and so you cut at the place of the veins, then press up high, and draw out the suspension of all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is already swollen with these marks, then it is now necessary to treat the vein and cut into it; and if there's air in the sac, or what's inside the vessels, it is necessary to deliver all that tissue, and make a round cut.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the hair of the arm is at their backside, it is fitting that you copy it all and extract the pus, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your operations are completed, apply the wound of woolen cloth in oil rose and wine, then cure with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses on the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess which has burst through an swelling similar to the groin, with the softening of the joints, and the patients suffer greatly when it heals; and the treatment for this disease is just as perilous as that which was done before, and we will tell you about the work on it, according to what the ancients used.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	Instruct the patient to sit upright on the raised bed, then pull down the suspenders of the clothes over their shoulders and at all the surrounding areas; then cut with a spatula around the edge of the joints, exposing them as much as possible, and then scrape off from each part, just as we have said in the extraction of arteries in the temples; then insert an arrow or where the vein is doubled, and tie it to the first place where the vein is found, and tie it directly opposite to the other cheek; then cut straight down according to the length of the body, and take out the corrupting moisture; then cure the wound as with the others, so that none of the vessels bleed, because through this there comes no harm, and if all the vessels come back, it is necessary to treat the vessels everywhere; so that the nose does not lose its swelling by the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	From the operation of the scalp
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The venous engorgement of this branch is caused by sectioning which comes from the scalp incision, or stretching it in the area of the ribs, because the intestines fall from that incision to one of the joints; and this incision is either at the scalp, or the stretching, and come from these two ways of many causes: by percussion, by a blow, by burning, or by raising a pain, and by similar things; and there are signs when it's an extension of the scalp, that it happens slowly, day by day, for a long time, and doesn't happen suddenly; and the abscesses are equal in size up to the center, because the scalp compresses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it's from the scalp section, that it brings sudden pain at its beginning, and the abscesses appear differently, under the skin close to the bone, and this is because of the intestine's movement and the body's avoidance of the scalp incision.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes he ties the intestines around it, and is retained in that place, causing great suffering to the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And for iron cautery, because of fear, he would rather shun it.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the treatment is that you command the patient to tie an intestine around his hand into the wound, if it can be inserted; then take some wine and pour it over his neck between your fingers, and lift the knees; then make a cut on top, and strike all the flesh from the joints long enough; then pour the wine of the intestines into the veins according to what you need to open the wound, and so that they can flow out; then scrape off the flesh from beneath the skin of the joints until it becomes white and smooth from every part; then pour your two fingers into the place where the intestine is inserted, between the white tissue which is under the skin near the vein, and between the second skin, and behind the vein, and move them to the hand with the right finger, and lift the joint above to your left hand, and command the minister to stretch the joint upwards, and untie that which is after the binding; and if you find no intestine wrapped around or white tissue dry, then pour it into the belly below; then take a needle and tie it with 2-inch thread made from 4 threads; then tie the intestine around itself in the form of a cross, and close the skin where the joints are, as we have said is under the skin of the veins, with a strong tie of 2 parts; then wrap the intestines tightly around it, so that no servant who feeds you can enter in, nor any bone comes through; and place the second tie after the first one long 2 times of that, and afterwards leave the skin which is under the keur des coions wide enough with a strip of the length of two fingers; then make cuts in the part under the skin of the joints until it does not reach or the bow; as we have said before; then apply moist flaxseed oil to the wound, and put it there, and apply the tie which we have told.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes cauterize the white flesh sac that we have said to be done after incising, by doubt of the slowing down of blood.

de hernie carnouse	of a hernia in the groin.

Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you strike the hairs, if they bleed and heal the wound, so long as it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilitic is constrained, and has no appearance in the routine, and the cautery is more moist in this location, and closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin on the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the joints is softened in some people, because the pus that is inside them is soft and can be seen, and it is necessary to treat him with great care; when you want to cure him, one must make the patient lie on his back, and strike the skin which is softened at the natural skin; then assemble the two lips to a suture, and if seen, cut through three stitches or four firmly; then strike between the stitches, and cure like other wounds, until he is healthy, and his hair grows back.
dou chastrement	doubtful pain
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	I know that the art of cutting is forbidden in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it here; and it is only necessary by two methods: one is that the midwife should respond to questions when asked by patients, and tell them how to cure; and the other, because we have often had need of cauterizing certain animals in order to help us, such as oxen and sheep and goats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that cauterizing is done by two methods: either through attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that method that we make by attraction, we sit the patient in hot water until their skin is softened and relaxed; then we press them with your hand, until they are fixed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: it is fitting that you dye the best, and press the skin of the knee with your left hand, then secure the suspension, and strike each one on I blow, when you have well scoured them; and leave no space large than a thumb's space near the vessels; and this manner of chastrement is more gentle than that which is done by attraction, for because of attraction some thing may remain in the skin, by reason of which it desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	regarding those with both sexes
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	The hermaphrodite is in two manners of home: one where between the two sexes it opens like the figure of a woman's nature, or he has hair, and sometimes without cut his urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another manner is in women, and it has on the nail as if a finger, and two wounds.

And the cure for fever and hunger is that you copy the joined characters all, and treat as other wounds; in the second manner, men whose urine bursts from the skin of the fingers, have no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tooth.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tooth is a joined character on the natural part, until it becomes too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a finger, and that's the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to paint over the superfluity of the tooth with your finger or on some bones, and copy it lightly; and do not apply too much force, lest bleeding come from the wound, then the cure is with other remedies until it is healed; and there is another character that appears in the mouth of a mare, and the temple, and by chance it bursts forth, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this they called it "kowee" disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it must be copied, as we have said about the testicle, and the treatment until it is healthy.
de erratique	of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratique is that of the woman's nature not being perceived at all, or those who are weak; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to illness that has come upon her, or it is caused by a fall, or by some subtle or stubborn pain in the crotch, and it is formed in the birth canal, or on the ribs, or under, or whatever; and they cannot conceive, and childbirth, and perhaps flowers will not bloom; and knowledge of this is through the examination of the umbilical cord.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If there are recent symptoms that appear, then either in your right side or left side.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is soft and subtle, and it is close to two fingers (two levers), if you hurry, and do that: put your two fingers together, and the woman lie on her back, spread out her legs; then bend the two fingers so that the subtle syfach is fixed, until she stops bleeding and is free from stitches; then take wool, and ghee in oil, and place it on the wound, and let the woman rest at home every day, if she cannot solder.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syfach is hard and dense, it is fitting that you cut with the spatula like a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stitches are made of linen, if you tie the onction and cut; and have medicinal poultices to apply, like aloe, dragon's blood, incense, etc., in abundance of wine; then bring in a large poultice cake, so that the wound cannot heal; and do it for a long time, and bring a tent made of dry linen; and cure with other remedies until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes a hare, then they should cover it according to this manner, if it is not an enchanted spell.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the apostles that are in the marsh are not to be touched with fire.
des emorroides	wounds from hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually do not close on their own, and when old hemorrhoids develop they turn into ulcers; and we have said in the division the similarities of warts and the signs; and I will tell you here which ones respond to treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and ulcers when they are completely filled in the marsh and do not appear to the touch, unless it is with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the mare can be cured.

It is therefore necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then fasten the altar with tongs, and chop it at its roots, then powder on medicine restraining blood, like dragon's scale and incense, and similar things; then pour her feet into boiling water for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if she continues to bleed, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and grape pomace and gall and similar things, and then take flour from barley, and mix it with honey and easily, and make her drink the emplastrum on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she stops bleeding, that's good.

And when the abscess is closed, treat the patient with ointment until it heals; and if it is called "albathir" and appears as a red head, with a rough skin like a thorn, so that they cover it as I said earlier; and then treat the patient until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the marrow, such as chancre and abscess of the bone, herpes, eczema, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and other diseases that I have mentioned in this division.

It is necessary that I tell in this treatise the abscess that comes to the marrow, which is not an abscess but a swelling; and if you see how it is, when it approaches with fire, look at whether the abscesses are formed in its beginning of arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red then you will be able to see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	And therefore do not pierce it, but let it rest for a while until the pain is alleviated; and then place the sick person on two stools, or have three stools where they recline, and support his back and assemble his feet towards the leg; and spread out his knees, and put his arms under his shoulders, and bind them well with a good knot; then take the stool from the right side, and bring it to the mouth of the marrow, so that later comes its shape; and it is necessary that when you see bring this instrument into place, that you pierce first by the side to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters through the instrument does not go beyond the proper extent, and does not wound the patient; and if the instruments are larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with cloths, so that the instruments do not hurt the patient; and it is necessary to put the horn of the instrument on top, and tie the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is covered with linen, so it is fitting that you should be careful not to apply hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The master (doctor) is first at the birth when he knows the shape of the natural child, and the signs you see when the woman is in labor and desires to push out her bowels: then hasten the arrival of the child; for if you know this sign, you will recognize a natural delivery, and the issue will come forth quickly from its head and second birth with it; and when you see these signs, so it is fitting to press gently on her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it emerges from its head, the second birth follows with it, and cleanses the menses of its superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes in other ways does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For there is sometimes that the feet come out, and comes forth the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon his stomach, or sovain, and is turned by chance or other evil forms; so it is necessary for the physician to know how to handle these things carefully and subtlety, and avoiding error and deception, and I will show you all the figures of how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes to sit on his head naturally, and the pregnant woman groans, and the virtues of her body are weak, then she should be placed upon a saddle or carried by women; and when it is cooked in oil or fenugreek, and then drinks the broth between its two small instruments of which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cuts the second limb, and strikes at its joint until the moistors (or swellings) that are hot with fire; and presses the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to bind the woman in musk and fenugreek with olive oil; then make her press and expel the condiments, and hold her mouth and nostrils for an hour: now remove the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out more, it is proper to reset them lightly one by one; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on the seat, lift the feet high; then loosen the seat on the ground, and let the woman, that she may not slip at setting up; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, cut off the hands with the knife which is there previously put, and extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes on to its feet, it is proper to push upwards; and then turn a little bit at a time, until they are even; then grasp the feet and extend them a little by a little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can he jump as soon as the joints are set, if commanded to do so, and make him fall from condition; for if he jumps, God will save.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not so as we have said, if the blood flows little by little, day by day, until it reaches its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come as we have said, then take mustard and oil of santon, gum and flour, and grind them all into a fine mortar; and apply this ointment to the woman's form inside and outside, covering up this ointment, then put her in hot water until she reaches down to the chest; and when she is softened downwards, let her wear a collar of iron, and put it on, and let her stay for an hour; then put her back on the chair, then make her vomit and tie her mouth and nose, and give her gentle breath, because now she will be sick.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child after its birth on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the infant comes in this form, if he mits his belly his hands little by little; then take hold of his neck, and hang down his feet, and be sitting on that bed; and bend his hands little by little, and then press his hands against the wind, and pull tight the cussins under, so long as it is prepared below; and if the infant does not fall, then seize his feet and move them firmly, then press the belly upwards, then take hold of the hands again; and stroke the infant little by little; and instruct the woman to fasten herself thus until the infant is ready.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child that comes out wide with one hand only
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I suppose it is necessary to bring back the hand: if you cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on that bed and bend down the knees; then apply the muscillianie as I have described it; and if she does not bear children, then sit her on the stool again, and then study how to bring back the hand; and do the child according to its natural figure, and let it be delivered, and instruct the woman to fasten herself thus until the infant is ready.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child from his neck down to his arms, and had spread out his hands, and his face turned towards his back towards his mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I suppose that the bale ( probably a bloodletting) is applying pressure to one's hand, then turning it a little and a little, and letting him lighten up; and when he is evened out, she puts on the muscillaige ( probably a medicinal ointment) of gold and oil, as we have said, then commands that she moves a little and a little; and when you have done this, she will sit down on the chair, and tells him to take hold of it; and he should pull himself up.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of the same manner to all the rest.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When he comes forth in this manner to all the rest, she cuts off the vein at one angle until it is free from moisture; and if the child coughs on his face and neck, she cuts the throat, so that it be not retained, and the child dies; then pours out the infant into him, as far as you have put him in order, and commands the woman to take hold of him no more: then he takes lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born many times, and sometimes they do not emerge at all; and this is no strange thing, for it has happened.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	There are two strange things, and they do not live if not named; I know this, that they are multiplied, and are destroyed by the womb that conceives them, which is linked to the blood; and sometimes they issue just as naturally as all of us do, like we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born severely, then the treatment is as we have said, and let the subtle bile be applied quickly and lightly what it does; and do so as if it were for salvation.
de plusors enfans	Many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No one is born with the form of I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, but rather are all formed in the shape of an infant according to its body's weight and size glorious, for the physician must be cautious, because by chance a similar thing may have happened; so do what seems appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman with the dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and no fire comes forth, and you are bound by obligation to observe hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman has a healthy disposition, and whether she has had an accident, or fears death; then it is advisable that the woman be sitting upright on her back, with her limbs inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the physician should apply two parts of oil to the mouth of the womb with musk and fenugreek and sesame seed, then rub his hands in these oils and musk and fenugrec, then pour them gently into the womb; then choose one of the onces that are suitable for this, and take care if the child is palpable when it comes down above its head; then pinch the onces onto her eyes or on her chin or in her mouth or on her neck or in the nostrils or under the beard or near the breast or under the armpits, and when the descent occurs, pinch or prick at the costal regions; and it is advisable to put a drop of oil into its hand, and place a horn between his two fingers of the right hand, and pour gently with both hands, and pierce the onces in one of these places that we have said, until it comes to an empty thing;
