and this is the form of the onces:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then fix the wound in another place, where it is needed, so that the extraction is even; and then extend it equally by moving from one side to the other, so that it can move, and hold the stitches tight, as is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if it remains a part of it, apply some oil to the ball of its two fingers, and pour it into that part, and treat the other part; and if it does not remain at all, place this cut or more above him, and do so until it has burned all through.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be returned to its place by straining, so that you cover the above cloth until it settles; then strike in the joint of the foot or at the knee, and do so with the other hand also, as is done on two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the patient is sitting on his feet, so that there is less pressure on the legs, and the direction of the stomach towards the mouth is lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if he is thinning out at the belly or in the groin, so that you draw him to a tied-up cloth over his hand; and make the belly or groin, until the moistors come away; and if other members are swollen, and the head remains still, so throw his bile into his hand by pouring from above of the marrow, and treat just to the mouth of the marrow; then pour one or two, and let it flow; and if the mouth of the marrow is tight due to an abscess that has come, it is not advisable to struggle, but rather it is advisable to apply moist things and grasses; and apply them immediately after, and cut in a soft water, and make smooth and easy.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child lies on its chest, and you can put it in an even position, then make sure what we have said about the living infant; and if you do not have the power, cut him into pieces, and do not leave anything of the second line.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done that, if they are put in the shape of what we have said about the arrow that comes out through the flesh; and if bleeding commences, then let it be restrained in water, and put them on other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom an infant was dead, and she sought another one above it, and then the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After many times the thing happened in the mouth, and it swelled so much that it burst, and great pain came.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was deceived; there is no translation to provide. The text appears to be incomplete or contains formatting issues. Please provide the rest of the text for me to translate.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed a splint of great attraction, and from it an os came out, after some other days.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed a great deal, because this has no bone in the belly.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound, and with great effort I pulled out bones, until the woman was in better shape; and it took a long time to put her back together again so that she had only a small piece of bone left on her; and I have never seen this chapter before except for this one reason: whenever a master finds an extraordinary thing, he seeks my help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	Let go of your hair to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Then comes the form of pressing, so that we remove the livers; and it turns back to the second joint in the same way.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	In all cases, the corns are more subtle in their restraint, and should be made of ivory or boxwood; and the mouth of the forceps should be one and a half fingers wide, and the margin of the branches should be one finger's width less; and it should be long by one palm and a half; and in both limbs they should have two similar clasps, which are firmly fastened on each other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two clasps are inserted into the mouth of the hair to open when turning the two corns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, which is more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of an ivory or boxwood rod, in accordance with the shape of the tongs; and it should have two joints with clasps, just as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when opening the hair with all the instrument, place a woman on a stool near the fire, bend her knees and feet over, then push the two clasps together into the hair, and hold the head of the instrument between her pelvises; then open your hand over the entire instrument, just as you did with the tongs equally, according to the quantity you see opening the mouth of the hair, until they make that which she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all above, and they are multiplied in their likenesses; and when the mirrors show them prepared, so it is faster to do the work, and higher for the height of their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you don’t see the instrument that is prepared in front of you, for it is not unnecessary.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second tooth is retained in the child, it is wise to instruct the patient to hold their hand, and then pull it out with care, and tie up your hands to the mouth and nose; and if she falls out by that means, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If that does not work, try to pierce the spot, and make a perforation or ulcer, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the mare, such as camphor, anise, chamomile, cassia lignum, and centaury; whichever of these herbs are cooked or boiled in water on the fire. Then put a candle or perforated pot, and the other herb in the mouth of the mare, and tie tight until the vapors come out from within the mare's mouth; then pull it out as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If he has a broken bone immediately.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment, and is not better, instruct the surgeon to make her moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or musk, and then soak it in water, and get the bone; and when she has found it, grasp it and stretch it little by little straight, so that the marrow does not stick to the extraction; but they must move gently to the right and to the left, and then treat; if she comes and discharges.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the swelling of the marrow is tightly closed, we have said to bring about the cure of expelling, and fumigation of herbs; and if she does not improve from all that we have said, be careful so that you do not go mad in treating her; but it is likely that whatever is at the mouth of the marrow will bind to the crotch of the woman, then close with ointment tetrafirmacoon; put a poultice and she will come forth; but beware, whenever she puts it, if there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and it afflicts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is then, then fumigation is suitable for this one: none of the ancients have tried fumigation with dried grass and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which to fumigate a woman, when it is held by the flowers and second joint if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to look like a dog's snout, and put the subtle head in nature, and tie the hairs wide on fire; and so be the fumigation over the coals, until the lice are eaten, and renew another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	But many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, instead the earth is cooled with a subtle knife: if it is then, then put in the bath that they pierce that knife at its root, and not the piercing of the stumpy spoon, and fasten the bandage so that she does not touch; then put on a linen moistened in wine and oil, and apply the treatment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt whether it will stop bleeding, then tie off a vein with a tourniquet and let the hands rest for a while, and put on an ostomy when the child gets up to go to bed in the room.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And at some times there is a sudden stanching of blood from a wound or an abscess; if you cover the source immediately: if it heals, as we have said about the tourniquet.
de la fistule dou fondement	of a fistula on the underlying part
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from beneath the underlying part are nodules, and those that come from beneath the surface, or in the space between the two parts, if there is an abscess or more; and when that nodule becomes old, it becomes painful, and with moisture comes a whiteish or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas pass through; and they are caused by what is discharged or by pressure from the patient's discharge, and by chance some of them break.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if fistulas occur in the bladder and in half of the penis; and they reach as far as the joint of the thigh, and also near the kneecap.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so they also notice the fistula continuing to the base, but not further: and therefore you push your little finger into the fundament, and insert a fine needle of iron or of thread into the fistula when there is some twistness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twistiness, so that you put a fine net of linen or horsehair into the fistula until you feel the net or hair at your point; and if you do not feel it, and there is no emission of pus, nor ventosity, nor bleeding, as we have said: search to see whether it will perforate through; for it is necessary to hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is passed just to the bladder or just to the channel of the urine, then it falls into the urine, and cannot be fixed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And if it is perceived just at the joint of the thigh, then there are attempts to go back to the place where it was; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of the pain in the vicinity, then it is fixed in that bowel, and there is no benefit from medicine or surgery with ointment; and for such passing fistulas, there is nothing but labor and vanity of foolish doctors who get involved.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that case where it is not passing and is not old, there is hope for health by iron, just as I have done; and the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his thighs, and incline his thighs towards his abdomen; then pour a little powder of arnica or plonc if it has tortuosity, until you see where the artery is coming from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in their lower back, then it is appropriate to give them your two fingers, if they feel anything at that point when the wound is being pierced; and whether it is discovered or you sense between your thumb and nail the syphilitic or the char, then you know she has syphilis; for not working on it will not cure her.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	But no one can be cured entirely, but it often happens that the aid given, if it is a cauterization subtle according to the size of the fistula, as said before; and you pour all down into the fistula, until it comes from the lower back; and do this twice or three times, until you know which charlatans must be treated with heat, which resemble a bird's feather; and then apply moist compresses to cover it, until those chills are gone, and then apply ointment to heal.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he has such a sickness, this is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If that, then it cannot be healed in any other way; and if he tries to squeeze between (the wound) and does not penetrate enough into the foundation, but puts a thick covering of cloth or fat over his skin where you see the fistula emerging with blood; and you make an incision at the beginning of the fistula, and suck out before the skin tightens up, and then do cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the fistula; and he will be freed from the tension, and relieved; for those fats that seem like a goose feather are needed, and none of them remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he does not want you to cut between yourself and the wound, but cuts in place of you, whether with fire or with a cooling medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Car the fire cautery has two effects: it is to cut off the blood from these charred areas, and then to cauterize the wound with fat or in a hot broth, until it takes hold, and so the wounds are sealed in the bowel; then cure the wound of ointments and apply hot char on dur, and those medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes just to the bottom of its foundation and is distant from the body, then put two or three pounds into its center and inquire.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the abscess and it is between two pounds or the fascia or char, if it is very close to being pierced, then without having set fire to anything but the way of hope and expectation, by the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut just at its bottom, or if you can, put on bandages and treat it as before; do not go too far into the depth, lest you cover up what holds the foundation, and let the exhalations come out by natural movement; then treat it, as we have said. By chance, it may be healed, or the covering will be removed when it is cut away from its bottom, or with some instrument pointed at; then remove the useless char that has been in the wound, as far as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the abscess in the area behind the foundation: if things become lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And there are times when fistulas are made in this way: and it is when you put a tent over the fistula, and it protrudes from the edge of the skin deep under the leather above, that one puts a tent around the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I cut the thread on one side and put a tent all along the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is purulent on the edge of the foundation within, then remove the thread from that puncture, so that you put your foot or foundation; and take out the head of the thread, and assemble the two joints together, and bind one to the other, and let them be for a day or two; and bind it no more than while the threads are separated, and bleeding; then cure the wound until it is sound and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If they have a fistula or abscess, so pierce it in every manner that you can, if it's not too deeply penetrated.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to tie with a cover if it's too deeply penetrated, and then treat it, as we have said, until it's safe.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form that appears when a spine bone is pierced to make an abscess is most often one part and a spiny edge; and on the other side it's not at all, because of which we do not cut into those things that should not be cut.
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are in two manners: or they are inside the fundament like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and on the surface there is a small wound, and sometimes there is one or more; but those that are outside do not have much moisture, and are often cut with a little cold water or a little saffron, and have a different color from the flesh. The cure for those who have them inside the fundament, is that you instruct the patient to press on the area in beds, until they feel the bone; if it's too tight, then you tie them up with twine, or linen, or a piece of camel hair; and you pull them out with your two hands, then cut them, and powder over some hot powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize as has been said in the cautery chapter, because other cures until they are safe. If the fundament does not come out, then tie the patient tightly to a harsh strap for lancing what is inside the fundament, if it can be done openly; and when the patient is ready, and the tendons have emerged from the fundament, then the cure is light; and you tie them up with your finger or with tongs, and cut them, then cure as we have said, until they are safe, and that there should be fear of the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to tie his costume in this manner: take a thread, and put it through an eyelet, and then pull the thread up above and pierce the eyelet on the other side, and turn both joints with the thread below the eyelet, if so loose; and tighten the thread firmly, then untie the thread, and pull out the needle, and do this for all of them, and leave one to drain the superfluity of blood; then put a wet cloth on the fundament of the drapery, in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the fundament, and command the patient to rest; and then let him lie down, and when he is sick, if the cure of ointment and other cures, does not make him well, so that he may be whole.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when cutting firmly with a knife or fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It happens frequently when there is a sharp pain in the intestine, and by the force of nature, and because the illness is old and medicine is useless.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to reset to the point of a splinter or at the angle where the scab is removed, which does not allow it to dry out; then treat as long as the wound is sound if it so requires; and if it will not heal, continue to rub more vigorously than before until it is healed and cleaned.
dou fremit	do the trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	The formication is a false appearance in the body, and goes all through it; and at times the coldness, and the feeling of death from trembling, come to all parts of the body, and most especially to the hands than to other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Instruct the physician to take a thorn from an owl's quill or a strong vulture's feather, and place that thorn on the affected area until it draws blood; then turn your hand around the thorn so that you cover all of the affected area, making a circle, and secure the thorn with its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if it is a thorn of thistle or iron, do so with a thorn from the same material and in that shape, being subtle under and above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, lest you hold to the wrong thing, and press. And if you see, then cauterize the thorn as it is in front of or near the fire of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of a hollow castor bean.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one uses a silver needle or an awl, or melted lead, or a bandage; and sometimes one uses these small and large instruments according to which one has brought them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These are therefore the instruments used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the needle small and large when it is used large, or if the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a rupture or the belly is tied, as you see, and the needle goes in deep, and one side has a wound, and on the other side too, and the belly is stuffed with medicine from a horn of flesh or parchment, or it is filled all around with small wounds, and between each wound there must be an inch of space, then take up the medication, put it inside through a needle that cuts hard, thick as a blacksmith's iron, into X or where in the belly it enters, and assemble the belly like a sow; and when the medicine is inside, if it sticks to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then clisterize; and this is the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Instruct the medicine not to be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or of beeswax or lard, or a similar thing, then give it lightly; then press the hands together in the hands of the minister as long as they are warm, then remove the dressing, and lift up the patient's legs to show, and if the medicine comes out, so that the boils come out as it can; and if he sleeps one night completely, then is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you bind the boils in a disease of decayed belly, and the medicine comes out quickly, so that it recurs when he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoides are on the fundament or abscess, so that the dressing is as subtle as for an infant; and this is the form of a subtle dressing upon which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or you will tell me the cures for hands and medicine, according to fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to which part or place the wounds are located, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things are made of wounds because of falling on stone, cutting with a sword and knife or lance or fist or saddle, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, since wounds can be placed in the throat, head, neck, side, belly, liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds because that will bring back a remembrance in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I dis that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn apart and the wound is great, and you doubt somewhat about an abscess: if you make it heal as soon as possible in the cephalic area itself, if it has come from a cut on the wound, and let it be healed to the contrary of the navel part; and avoid the patient being replete with wine and coarse foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't heal, if he is weakened by his meat and does not drink wine, nor eat pork; and applies to the wound, if an abscess forms on his cheek, apply a moistened cotton in rose oil alone, or in vinegar syrup; and if there is no abscess, apply to the wound, if it is fresh with all its sanc, and is not moved by air, powder, as I will say later; and if he has been moved, apply some ointments, until he heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by stitches, then assemble them by suturing, as I will say about wounds in the belly, of the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and flesh, and it holds only for a little time, if scratched; then treat the wound with medicine, and apply a hard cover made of skin in its place, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as testes and boiled bread, as well as fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotting skin or flesh that is not adhered to the bone, and it rots completely, and it falls out, then treat the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound which cannot be stopped by medicine without cutting, whether you cut it or leave it as it is, and if you cut it loose with a thread, and that does not benefit at all, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then is the cure light: and you put on this powder which unites so well that the artery has been moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take cense three parts; blood of dragon two parts; calcined vivae three parts, and a fine powder, and apply the wound, and bind it firmly, until it has dried well and united with all its blood; then tie it well, and let it be so that it does not swell; for one must keep the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made alone with calcined vivae, when you do not have cense or blood of dragon, but the artery has been moved by the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the arrow pricks the wound, itself present, do not put on this powder; but put some ointments prepared, or made from flour of rye and water and honey, until it is dissolved; then the physician will treat other remedies until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If the fracture of bone comes with the wound and it is small, if you make subtle pins; and I will tell you about fractures of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between the one on the head and the other, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's the nerves, just leave the cure alone and don't put anything to restrain it, because night has no effect on the nerves and makes them retract; and don't apply anything to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of the ailment is with the brain, which is in the higher members; but if medicine is needed, as calomel is washed in sweet water, and melted with olive oil, and the calomel is also washed again in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so that the skin and tendons are cut and bound with bandages, then the treatment continues until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and the head is swollen and filled with pus, so that they penetrate further below; and if the arteries are cut, and blood comes out, then it is necessary to bleed, and ligate, and apply cauterization as needed; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the joints, and the cord is preserved, because the flesh will move, so cut the joint on the chain of the neck, and do not touch the throat but apply it according to its natural figure; and then bind immediately, and leave for some days, and then treat with herbal remedies such that they are healed; and if the wound has caused impression in the bone, and there are pieces of bone, so cut them off at once, and those which cannot be removed, leave until they rot, and fall away from the wound, and make it clean and easy for it to heal; and if the wound is fresh, then apply powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has an abscess, then the treatment will be as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of arrow or sword wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a wound from an arrow or sword and the wound is deep, then look at the wound to see if there are signs of pus coming out: since seeing that the wound is mortal; and if it's not deep, and fresh as all its blood, then do not put powder on it or tie it with the wound until you have examined it thoroughly, and return to him, but apply a soothing ointment, and tie it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put a woolen cloth in the wound to soak up the moisture, and make the patient sleep above the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there is no spasm, nor male nervousness from the heart, nor any other sign of death; and when you see the bones have good disposition, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Cure the wounded of tenets and other cures, until they are healed; and if she cannot be healed or cured, then it is necessary to know that there is an abscess; if the cure should do so as it must.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is of a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or on the back, if the cure in front; if it is large, of stitching; and if it is small, of powder; and if it has pierced into the bone, and cut off pieces, as it pleases the wound, and removes the pus if there is any; and if there is no pus, then allows the wound to dry, which will alleviate the extractions; and for other wounds in other limbs, make judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	a rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IV manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies du cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I have an idea of what the text is about. Here are the translations:
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	In the cold, heat it in this manner: moisten a sponge or half a cloth in hot water only, or cook it in boiling water squant and cipre and spique, and tie the intestine until the swelling subsides; and never do this twice, and wait for a while before removing it, lest it be inflamed again.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling go away, moisten the intestine in water or boil it until they are soft, for by this is alleviated the entry into a little thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound on the instrument with which you strike the varicose veins; and the first treatment is cooling down that size, so that none of us should cut it unless there is great necessity, because that's how the strumens are broken: pierce inside in the nest and beware not to miss, and see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines spring out, if you put it back in its own natural form according to its own place, if you have the power, because this is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen under the belly, it is advisable to have the patient lie on their back, with their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, it is to place the head and the navel higher than the other parts, and so you should attend to this when there are great and moderate wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, put on what is suitable for it; then take a pin or needles, and with the pitiful minister who holds all the rupture in his hand, assemble the lips; and this is the common way of suturing, where you prick an eyelet or several, according to the width of the wound; and leave from the top of the wound two fingers' space, and pierce with a strong thread; and pierce both sides of the skin with both sides of the needle, which are under the skin, until you pierce it from that part; then assemble the two ends of the skin together four times; next tie a double thread around the eyelet of two parts; then assemble the two ends of the wound to its present state; and leave two fingers' space; and prick another needle; then tie with a thread as you did the first, and do not cease until the whole wound is sewn; and it's better that the needles be in between subtle and coarse, because subtle needles pierce through all the flesh, and coarse ones cannot enter well at all: therefore they should be in between. And it's not advisable to push the needles too far from the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open the wound before the sewing; and then prick the ends of the needles, so that they do not disturb the patient while sleeping; and tie knots or cloths around the ends of the needles so that they may be held tight; and leave them until the wound is sewn; and this way of suturing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because there is an eyelet or a second stitching where it's common to sew dresses; and when you have pierced all those stitches, tie the needle at the place where you started, in the manner of sewing clothes; and leave space between each stitch equal to the thickness of two fingers' worth; this is done by one man, and I stitched a wound on one man who had a wound under his belly, which was cut with a knife, and was two palms wide, and the intestines were well three palms wide, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I let my intestine alone for 24 hours then it stopped bleeding after 15 days, and the cure, and was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they thought he was going to die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with medicine, for I was in the forest where there is no one found, nor any medicines; and I placed cotton wool above the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle and thread from the inside out as far as it can go; when it pierces the vein straight on to straight on, if you pull the skin tight or cut the wound with the needle, and have pierced it the other way from the inside out as far as it can go; and this is the sense of sewing just like the barber sews hair, leaving one side of the suture uncovered and covering the other, until the whole sewing is done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing, as the Greeks properly call it, is done in this way: whoever does so, they assemble both parts together naturally and fix one end of the thread to the other end with a needle. In such a manner: puncture one end of the thread with the nail of a nearby mirror, and pierce only that part, leaving both joints loose; then turn the needle and pierce it from the opposite side, inside those two joints; then pierce both of them from the opposite side again, in two other nails on the same side as before; and this is the most natural manner of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks are said to have spoken of this saying, and no one testifies to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, or thread in each; and that one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when the rupture is inside the belly, the sewing is more painful than for others.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like that of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, after the arrow has moved, remove the intestines, and the wound; then put on powder with salt, and if the arrow has moved, put on any ointment present, until the wound heals; and sew the thread, and tie up the stitches, and the poultice; then cure the wound like others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, just put on, as soon as they come to vomit, cotton wool, and move II times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	But you do not need other medicine beyond the usual dispositions for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound will cause swelling in the main joints, it is wise to apply a light linen cloth soaked in hot olive oil or rose oil between the wounds, and under the swellings; and if he feels pain or pus in his bowels, and this often happens, then take away the clisters of black wine juice, and also when the putrefaction comes just inside the intestine; and pierce it again, and find that since it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "youth" cannot heal when it is diseased, and this is because of the coldness of the veins, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the approach of its nature towards death.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the artery jumps from the wound, if you remplace it as quickly as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black or brown, then it is necessary to tie the patient who is black, because there will not be any bleeding, because he has veins and arteries; then cut what is between the bandage, and hang both knees down from the part below the wound until the artery bleeds, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the burn from a hot iron.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is broken and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I saw that one man was wounded by a lance in the stomach; and his wound was on the right side of the abdomen, and became inflamed and turned into an abscess, and this caused the evacuation and flatulence; I put him to cure according to what I know, and did not stop until he was cured, and the healing took place.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healing, I doubted that the patients had illness in their stomach; and there was no harm to it, but he improved in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this manner: take two large pieces of cloth, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the cloth has covered the entire mouth, place them on both lips so they tighten the mouth; and then strike the head, and if it stays that way, he cannot untie it, then put another cloth after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and tie the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, and there is no trouble to the patient, and it can be tied to the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the head of that fine thread of intestine which is completely matted, and then tie it to the head of that fine thread of linen so twisted, then pour the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull the thread out through the anus; and this method of stitching does not burn at all, except according to the way of hope and expectation; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there will be no healing nor recovery, unless by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or however it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	That which has grown long, when it begins to wither, is called a fistula; and even when it is swollen and has turned into an abscess.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	The fistula is as according to the nodulation of the vertebrae, which are hard and raw, or else there is no pain felt, and it is also swollen like the feathers of a bird; sometimes it opens up with a clear abscess, and at other times it becomes thick; sometimes little pus, and at other times quite a lot. I have already mentioned these in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healing and does not produce pus, is caused by one of the seven causes: this is to say, due to the smallness of the wound or body cavity; or because of malice; or because it has a hard clot inside, and on the lips, which prevents anything from coming out; or there is too much swelling; or the leg is swollen, and the matter is of poor quality; or medicines are not good in the treatment; or because of corruption, which is a type of pestilence; or because the property in that region is late, digestion is slow, and recovery is delayed, and it escapes by nature; or there are veins or bones. I have already shown all these causes, signs, and medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is fitting that I inform you about the treatment of fistulas, which are created by hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	There are fistulas in every part of the body, for there are those that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the scrotum, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or on the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and if they occur at the property of the main member, and are similar.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas of this kind are a source of pain and disease, except for one thing: labor and ignorance. If there is any fistula that I have not mentioned, and you have entrusted me with its cure, and it seems to be curing, take a needle or iron rod, if the fistula is straight, take it as is; but if it is crooked, search for a subtle probing, because these probes bend and follow the tortuosity; and if the fistula has lost hands and you cannot reach it well with needles, then search for a way through one of the lost fingers, because the moisture from one finger is different from another, and muddies it; then take your best guess to know whether it is near an artery or nerve, and ask the patient where they feel pain when you press on that place with your hand; and when you have truly determined its location, and if it is near a joint or nerve or artery or vein, or any of those things I mentioned earlier, follow my advice exactly as I told you, and apply pressure to the same spot whenever possible. Then fill in the gaping space with the right material and the dead flesh that are inside; and then perform the cure until it is healed, if the fistula is deeply rooted in the straight direction, take it as deep as possible, whenever possible. If it does not heal by this means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, take out the dead tissue as well.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	For the vein or nerve that is swollen or inflamed, if it grieves or bothers you, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it as long as the corruption is entirely visible, then treat the flesh with cautery until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns to its former state, as before, know that you are not at fault: if it is so exposed as to be at the bottom, and you desire to see it, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb. And if it is in this state, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep, you cannot save it: if there is no other means than to tie back to nature; and if there are little bones corrupted, and you can treat them with tongs, if there is a convenient instrument for this, and if there are many bones, take all of them, do not leave any one; and if the moisture makes against you, and there is no error or fear, tie up moisture and cautery, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre,
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.
