Instruct the patient to let the vein's wound dry completely so that they may treat it on the head and on the body, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said. And it is fitting for the lord that he takes care of the nerve beneath, and if he pricks too much in front, and then cuts the nerve, it will swell and the sicknesses will be grievous, and by chance they may not heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open on anyone's body for its subtlety, so it is fitting that you cleanse it with a sterile instrument beforehand. And take care of your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it with length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic wound is aided by having treated the head with a salve, and also aiding the eyes; and it is fitting to heal through pricking at the flame of olivaire or mirtin, for this is the most safe of all veins, because it does not have a nerve or artery beneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Everywhere, it is convenient to seek the lighter solution first, and not distress anything if we must try it for the first time, and then resume; and by chance, it may swell in some men, when we try it for the first time, but it will not cause trouble.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that healing is not done only to preserve health, and to get rid of coming diseases; and it can be done in one of the three veins: head (cephalic), breast (faste), or arm (basilique); and you should start healing at the beginning of prayers with fasting, and after autumn and winter when they appear the signs of repletion; and you should heal on the first day or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick person who is in charge has no fixed time for illness but rather as needed each day or night, at all hours and times; and it does not suit to heal the children just before XIIII years, nor pregnant women except during the first six months just before seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	It does not suit to heal those who have passed LX years (60 years).
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wants to be healed in any manner whatsoever, it is suitable that one infuses their intestines with a light castor oil, if they have much constipation retained, so that the veins do not press on the superfluous parts of the intestines and cause harm to the principal members; nor does he heal those who are too salty from meats, nor those who are sick with fever, as long as it persists, nor with dropsy; and if one warms oneself up after a bout of colic, vomiting, and flatulence of the stomach, and many nights spent with woman, and labor, watching and striving, then subtilize the humors, since they have not been swollen, by meats and drinks and medicines; take out from them as much as you can; then enter into a bath, if no other thing prevents it, in order to subtilize the wound, and heal the vein at the third part, just like we said; and beware that day of work, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be humble and joyful, and be more careful than those who are being healed, and rub the arms twice or three times, then loosen the binding from the middle moment, because when it is too tight or not tight enough, it cannot hold still without being hurt; and then rub the healthy person with their hands, until they swell, and one can feel them; then pour them a bit of hot oil old, then put on some ointment of his own hand from his left side under that vein at which he will heal, so that the vein does not bleed and fail to be healed by the iron.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For in such veins that are as thin as a cord to the vein, and for those that are full of windiness, so that when you put on the flame, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and so are these; and if they cover the vein, then the wound is too tight, therefore it is fitting that the scribes should be advised in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it's good; but if not, if you reapply it again a little under that place or above quickly, and if the veins are inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed, and the patient hopes for an outcome, let them leave it alone for a day or two, and do not tie up the arm: by chance there may come pus; do not enter into the bath, then reapply the treatment if they please; and if the puncture is small, or if you cut underneath with subtle caution, and you doubt that it will not burst as much as you see, be brave in that same puncture directly with all the flame; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swelling in the leg, do not resume the treatment, and apply a little oil to it, for it relieves the body of pain, and softens the limb which is tied with oil; and thus administer oil to each wound that you treat, to quench the flow of blood; and this same procedure also makes a tourniquet and bow when putting on the leg; so subtlety will save and spare it when it becomes too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes up, which has happened many times, especially when it is only bound with thread after opening the vein, then hasten and apply to it an oiled sponge soaked in water and wine, and tighten for one hour; it is fitting that you do this after the issue of the blood from the vein, and if it remains on the leg for some days without any pain or color, it will not be harmful; and if you see, apply some aloes or mirror juice mixed with calamus or similar substances.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance at the opening of the basilica: so put your hand on it, and if you feel it soft to the touch with the pressure of the hand, that is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So avoid putting on anything that we have said, for perhaps by cutting without touching the artery; but make the wound dry first to harden the liver, then treat it with another treatment, until it is sound.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And deal with each according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is not black, let it breathe out until it becomes red; and if you see a big one, let it breathe out until it becomes subtle; and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	Instruct the patient who is robust and strong, who needs extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, and let the festerings be wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and it will heal soon and frequently, and should be healed by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing is safe from worsening of blood and of numbness of nerves, and is more effective than the healing done long or short.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose blood needs to be cut away, it is proper to give him a moist pain in juice of green pomegranate; if he is hot, take out the blood three or four times; and if his complexion is cold, take some pounded meat before the healing, a moist pain in syrup made with muskmelon, or in an aromatic syrup of honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a very fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If the patient has a wound on his palm, after a great amount of bleeding, it is advisable that he drink a broth of char and a subtle-smelling syrup, and use other things as we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If he is to cut off one arm and heal it again, if this is allowed, when the patient is weakened by great bleeding, it heals little by little, according to the continued power of the virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If he who is to cut off one arm after the first bleeding has strong flesh, it heals in seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the eleventh hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever is to be healed in another part, if it must be healed the next day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood inside the body which causes fever; if one wants to treat it greatly, and widen the wound so that the bone protrudes from the surface; then when you reward all conditions of healing, put your hand under some fingers until the bone grows, lest the mort come in the place of the bone, and this happens often, when the healers are careless; and do not want to, when you see the arm being released, and making blood flow again, the wound is closed, because you press strongly on it; but if it is crooked, extend the arm quickly, because this would be bad; but leave it so that it heals the second time; or one will find a point of flame at the end, until the vein is frozen with blood loss, and put under a little cloth in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is sprouted, so let it be and do not strangle it any more, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to treat the wound a second time, then in the same vein as before, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healed in place of the vein on the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of healing if it is such that the patient puts his hand in hot water, until the pulse becomes red; then he ties it lightly, so that the vein appears well; then now heal through it, not too long or too short; and cut off large wounds, and suture them well near the joint of the hand, and if they won't come out, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the wound seep into the water, until you have had enough; and if it is like this, do not put the hand back in hot water again, because it is set on worse than when it was like that; and the healing of this vein is better than all others, for there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sickness of the salvation of the right hand is worth all other diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and pour into hot water, until the wound be cleansed, if it can; and if it is out of place, and you copy it to its proper place, do not trouble anything; and do not go too far for a while, because the nerves are without all care at that time, and then put the hand in hot water again, if it has not frozen in the wound, and it will come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the wound as much as necessary, then put oil and sinew on the vein to solder it hastily, and do this for each place.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness of the sinew in the left hand is worth the disease of the mouse, and do this just as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the spine is worth as much as all other diseases that are in the body, since they are such as those of the mare's, and retention of flowers, and disease of the rains, and of the joints and the legs old, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his spine is such that the patient drinks some stone in hot water, and strokes on the vein until it dies, and lies above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot goes a great amount of rain; then heals the one or is larger than the other, or at the ankle, that is worth.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal above the foot, then beware of the nubs that are beneath, and the healing of crossing as with cutting; and so let the swelling.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out by itself, he puts the foot in the water, and lets well empty the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wound needs to be opened for the first time, then reopens it above by a little more, because the liver is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so make the opening of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The liver of the saddle vein is in the heel of the foot and its wound is worth the pain of the groin, when it is cut.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its wound if it is that the patient enters into (bath), and strains above the heel by turning four fingers, because otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then you must heal in all ways possible, and crossing over; and beware to copy it, because the liver is poisonous, and it is very returned with human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find it, then any rain of the body that opens or the back of the foot, and towards the small toe, and beware of the pain; and make as much care with the wound as you see, and then release the ligature, and put on cotton and bind; now she is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wind sickness
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Wound cauterization is made of horns, or arsenic, or vinegar; and wind sickness occurs in two manners: either by striking and attracting the wound, or by striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this wind sickness which is done by striking so occurs in two manners: either she is with fire all over or by fire; and the wind sickness that is made by striking and by extracting the wound occurs in 13 ways of the body, for one is on the head completely, and others are on the neck, and two others on each side of the neck; and there are wounds under the chin; and wounds under the armpits; and wounds above the shoulders; and wounds on both arms; and wounds on both legs; and wounds on both knees; and this wind sickness does not touch the wound at all, except for small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and because of this it does not make anyone weak, as much as one makes with a vein dressing; and it is not suitable to be made in any disease that comes from overeating, until the entire body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is in its third month, we command to be ventilated after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sickness of the liver is helpful to the grieft of the head… that comes in the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the sickness of the cephalic, and should not be done by those who are of a cold complexion, or who have chatharre, for this does much harm to them; and therefore they should not use it, nor those who have head cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become blind, and for this reason they must put the ventilation instrument a little further down by the doubt of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wound in the neck is near the vein of the head and basilica, and for this reason it is swollen due to the tightening of the flesh, and breaking of the channel of the breast, and scorching, and repletion; and one should not press too much, because if she holds too tightly, she will be overcome by inclination or stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The swellings are on both sides of the neck if it causes pain in the head, eye inflammation and emigraine, and strangulation, and pain as a result of the roots of the teeth, and is near the vein of the basilica; and one should command to the lord that he presses his hand not to cut the artery, and does not delay in taking out blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The swellings under the chin are worth suffering from diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and they are near the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are worth the disease that comes from heat and overcharging.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the sides are worth as much as three veins in the arm, because it will bring blood from these large veins; instruct the lord to not make the incision too deep, for the veins are bare and know under nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The windings on the lower back are worth as wounds on the fundament, and as diseases beneath; it is necessary that the winding be large and made of linen, so that it may well treat; but by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and thus makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The windings of the legs heal completely, because they bring blood from all the body; they are worth as old pains from rain, and of mares, and bladder, and cause flowers to come; and are like the two sinews, and the two knees; and whatsoever they weaken the body after a long time, they also lead to weakness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the ventose is that you place it first empty, and suck accordingly, and hold it firmly, and move equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the blood flowing red and swollen, and feel the redness of the wound; then stop, and remove the ventouses, and take care in the disposition of the corpses, because there are many who have soiled their flesh, and it is advisable to cut only once, and it is advisable to make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if they are not gross, cut twice: the first time to subtlety the way of the large wound.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if they are very thick, it is advisable to cut the third time: and when we wish to suck on small wounds little by little, we should only make one incision.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	In order to cure a great deal of blood, you must renew them often; and if the wound is thick, you should make a furrow by cutting deep. If the terminus is such that it can be seen suddenly, you must take care not to cut too deeply, and you must oint those limbs with olive oil apertif and dissolutive: if this is a balm, use violet oil, or almond sweet oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if this is in yew, use cresson oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or any similar thing.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the flow is large and cold, you must take turmeric oil, or balm oil, or anet oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If those whom you have healed with a tender touch and large pores, do not put any oil on them, but rather wash them after the application of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain melon water, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, so they lift themselves from the air, or from water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large purulent swelling, so they lift themselves from old wine, or from sickly water, or from decoction of anise or camomile, or similar things; and do not like to be treated with suction in front of the bath or by immersion, but only after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after the evacuation, and are likely to worsen, when they need to be evacuated and when they are already congested.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And they should eat those who have recovered are choleric, and if the stomach is not too inflamed and congested; so that he takes cold things, as apples, grapes, endives, and lettuce at the air, and similar things; and drink plenty of vinegar, and meat broth from a castron, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Instruct the patient who has a cold complexion to drink syrup of honey and aromatic wine that is midway between old and new, which contains little, and serves small fish and pigeons and polecats, and the next day when they are expected to be ventouse, they must drink more than eat; and it is fitting to give some men anise or muscat before or after the ventosacion, or for comforting the main members; but subtlety is necessary without it, but it is not suitable for those who are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The ventouses that are applied to be injured are those placed on the liver and gallbladder and podagra and on the abdomen and the throat and the perineum, because these members do not suffer from being cut or pierced, and one forces them only to attract blood into a member as we put venesections on the nipples when they heal; in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put ventouses on the abdomen and on the boil to soften the member; and to take away pain, when there is opilation or stone, it takes it away by its attractive power by chance, or removes the stone from its place; and thus does it when one puts it on the liver and on the gallbladder when they have retained a ventosicity, and these ventouses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes are administered together with fire, and sometimes plain with cold water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such manner that we fill the ventouse with hot or cold water according to what has been concoiled herbs suitable for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction to be administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two fingers of length and half a thumb, and there are seven small punctures on one side of the middle, as if to prick with an awl, so that the needle will not harm the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle have a vertical piece of linen or iron for tying a bandage, and be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for children's suction tubes are different from adults' and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus you must put this suction tube on the limb: tie a linen or wax thread around it through the middle piece that is tied to the suction tube, so that the heat is at the bottom of the tube and does not burn the patient; then place the tube on the limb, with two fingers above the punctures we have said about, so that when you pull, if there's vapor, it comes out, and take off the suction tube; and tie the linen as before, often, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	When in the cough that is serving as an assistant for the disease of pleurisy, it has fever and no pulse or pulse is felt, and it is served only when it is full of fever, and is placed on a limb solely; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	No sutures are served only in members where you cannot put vents (pressure devices) because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar ones; and in the nose, if it is cut out like two or six, and other similar ones; and the qualities of using them are that when you find sutures that are in fevered water, so take them; and put one nut (suture) into fevered water, until they become accustomed to it, and do not have anything in the belly; and then they can be freed from vein and ventouse, then rub the member until it is red, and place sutures on it; and when they are full and swollen, if this is possible, put a vent (pressure device), because this is very valuable afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If it is so, then lift the limb from ashes, and then from water, well; and then examine it; and if the limbs are too swollen after the operation, put a linen wrapping soaked in cold water on it, and cover it, until they are stopped; and if the swelling multiplies, put vitriol crushed or vinegar, and similar things, until they are stopped; or you place a half-dozen boiled peels on the limb, and leave them there until they dry out, so that now they will be quenched; and if you have more need, then take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the poultices will not take effect, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or put a needle in until the poultice forms, and then cover it, as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry out; and when you see that they start to ooze, then powder some aloes and ground silk, or ashes, on them, so that they will now be quenched.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The book of fractures begins.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the art of cutting is found in this chapter, which no one has seen or read before in the ancient books, nor have they understood letters; and for this reason the science was lost in our land, because I could not find anything good; and I know nothing but through the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so thoroughly that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described here what is contained, condensed it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments you will need, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we speak in this prologue of the book about the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and keeps it on the virtuous, so that those who have experienced this art noble learn and acquire it, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when breakage or dislocation or torsion or splintering occurs in any part of the body, it is necessary to quickly treat the sick person from one side and the other, so that no weakness affects them, as with weaknesses of the body, or because they are feeble, or old; or if their skin is too thin, or too cold; and treat chills caused by cold, which means cold juts, and charred flesh of birds and of deer, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with viands that fill the veins with blood, until you are certain whether it is an abscess deep or an expansion of matter in a limb; if the patient returns to their previous governance before they have used them.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore themselves, it is fitting that you nourish the patient with foods that cause great swelling, such as those which have a lot of viscosity, like bread cooked in water, and risotto, and testicles, and pork fat, and oysters, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because the swelling causes more sprains and sooner the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old people and decrepit ones cannot be well restored or healed according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, and also those which are too tender, like the bones of small children; but there is no cure, you must put back the big joints where the bone has hardened and joined the limb together, so that it takes its former shape again; and do not leave it entirely without work, and for this reason they should be nourished with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And finds that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all sorts of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that grow inward, and others that grow outward, just like the thickness of a hairpin to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture with just a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own nature and specific instrument for treatment, according to what the memory brings in its place; and it is known that the fracture of bone comes from the joint being twisted, and opening well due to moisture, and it sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no tortuosity or swelling at the toucher, and the patient feels no great pain, unless there is a point of fracture; but he can still have tortuosity, a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move your hand, but apply medicines that come after this, and then restrain now with subtlety.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And knows that if there is a break in the arm and two parts are dislocated, he should now put them together equally, so that they may heal; and if they begin to close (because of swelling), let one day pass before putting pressure on it, until the swelling subsides; then set it at ease as much as you can see and feel, and knows that the restoration of this part is lighter than the restoration of that part where there are pieces; then restrain, as seems proper afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and you cut two parts, whether it is a hand or a small limb, or two cords, or one cord and a hand; and place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the damaged member are diminished, reattach them by all means at their joints as much as possible, and take care that through your work there does not come to the patient an additional lesion or pain; and add well both ends of the bone in the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the patient feels well in the hand if it seems that he is not doing well: If the dress is made perfectly, and not strained too much, nor pressed as those do who make it come by their own work with hot and painful contraction to the member, as we have wished many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at a point, if you chastise the patient well so that he does not move, neither while waking nor sleeping, neither turning nor in any other manner; and carefully ensure that the limb be securely fastened so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	Because when he feels no pain, it is not at a point, and so you must put him in proper position so that he feels no pain; and be careful that he is placed correctly, lest twisted movements occur when restored; and the quality of the broken member will be as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Things which the member is broken are various in size and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small members, such as arms and forelegs: it is advisable to wrap with strips of soft and subtle linen; and for the large ones, such as thighs and legs: it is advisable to wrap with a wide and hard band, because the wide bands embrace the entire great member, and strain it evenly from all parts, so that there is no gaping. Then tie up lightly around the edges, three or four times according to the member, and tie your hand onto the whole ligament, then go to the top of the break and tighten less, until the break slowly stretches a little; and soften the ligature little by little, until you take hold of most part of it with sound flesh; then take another band, and turn towards above upon the broken limb; then go back down on the part below the break, and strain moderately, not too tight nor too loose, as we have said in the first line above; then put between the ligatures strips of linen or cloths, until it is all evened up, then tie everything by above with a band, and then put your splints well-made on top, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, he puts a soothing balm on the abscess, and who cuts out the inflammation, and leaves it in that way for some days; then pull out the arrow, and set aside with a gentle bandage of one-half inch wide, or of a stick used to make splits, or palm of a tree, according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is fitting that the bandage put on the break is a bit larger and wider than the others; and so long as it needs to be, according to the size of the limb either small or large; then tighten up the bandages in such a way as you did with the first binding, then tie over it with a rope after that, just like the first binding on the break; the tighter it is, the less so; and it is fitting that the rope be medium-sized, not too thick or too thin, and made of linen flax; for if the ropes are too big, as I have wanted to make some works with leaves that make their bindings with threads of linen twisted, and this is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too subtle, and does not fit that it should have two fingers' breadth between each bandage.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is wounded by arrows after an injury, then tie off those places with linen or woolen strips so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a break and the joints are fractured, I will say this treatment after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to tighten the arrows on all members, even the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it is not necessary to put arrows on them every day, only after five or seven days, or more according to the security of the surrounding abscess; and here is the way of the ancient surgeons to restore breakings, dislocations, and torsions: and take from the flour that clings to the walls of the mill, and mix it with a lot of fat, and make this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, for it's the common way of the surgeon restoring the breaking in many situations, and especially women and small children, because it is not too harsh nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of applying plaster restores fractures and dislocations and torsions: take barium and ladanum and unguent and asefetide and gum arabic and myrrh, one X; mirror and aloes, one V; alechil VIIII; and make powder, and mix with honey and wine; if the complexion of the flesh is hot, use this plaster, for it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and saves many lives.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that is good for twisting: take myrrh and visnmalve, one X; mirror and aloes, one VIIII; acacia VI; Armenian boric acid X, grind well, and congeal with water or honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to treat a dislocation with and without joints is necessary; you need to take out the tendons and bones from their place, and alleviate the pain that follows, and use the bone to repair the break: take new linen, and apply it quickly and easily in oil cooked, and put on its place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not heal, but they are good for soothing abscesses and properly placing bones, the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat a fractured bone that heals: take leaves of dried figs and earthy leaves, break them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat a plaster for the healing of a bone fracture and to relieve swelling from an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of willow bark, camomile flowers, violet flowers, wheat flour, of each one an equal part; and grind, and mix with wine, and apply to the limbs when warmed up, or mixed with moist coriander water, or water alone, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to treat is stronger than the first, when an abscess comes back to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of willow bark, and seeds of flax, balsamum, meletum, and sassafras, and flowers of violet and camomile, each to an equal part; grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iporas writes in his book that you should not put broken bone on the limb to restore it, rather, one should use a mixture of cerote made from wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between too hard and too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that one must place the broken limb on high in order to restore, using dry things moistened with hot stuffs, such as myrrh and aloes and incense, just like we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to heal wounds is that it values the flesh and pain: take mud from broken men or crushed animals, or feathers, and myrrh, and cut them equal, and grind them, and make an emplaster of the wound and the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then take it away a little after, and beware that the patient does not feel any pain, nor any movement of the bone in its place; if he does not take it out by hand every day. If pain comes to the limb, or prurite, with rest, or swell, you hasten, and take it out, and remove the emplaster now; and take a lighter bandage, and a sponge soaked in moist sea water, and plunge into the water, and lift up the limb, until the itching ceases, and the pain is alleviated. Then let him rest for an hour, then put on a dry linen cloth, moistened in water or olive oil, and tie it on with a nut, until you are sure of abscessed swelling; and treat the inflammation on the limb, and remove the pain, then resume subtle treatment, and a little emplaster, and do not strain it too hard as before; and be subtle until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess swells and is red and painful and inflamed, I have already treated it by draining and stitching, just like I did before when the pain came on.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the member anything of what we have said, and if you do not release it until after three days or four or five, or seven, and never for twenty days, as is observed, until the break heals, and approaches the setting of the bone near; then tighten it more than before, and let its flesh swell, just as I have said earlier. And if you see the limb drying up more than necessary is not, know that necrosis cannot come; therefore lift the swelling at once with hot water and vinegar every time you release it, and thus cut off the necrosis in the member, and do what the barber surgeons do, which cause the member to be twisted: this is bad, and if it is caused by fear, I see nothing else but to bleed and to set it straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	From diverse ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of breaks, and diverse shapes, and the causes are determined; for there are breaks that are made by the impact of a sword, and the bones crush the entire bone just beneath the bone, such as from hitting or being struck with a fist; and for this reason it is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword strikes the bone from above to pierce it, and is called "absolute" break; and there are two types of wounds resulting from these breaks: great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact into a hollow space, or tearing, or fracture of the bones by stone, or through the bone on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has an open fracture which is near to the bone under the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is either great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is covered with bone in such a subtle way as our hands cover themselves, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called "capillary" break; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or by some similar thing, and the piece of the bone falls inside, and the hairs are so thin like the metal used when making pots over the pot lids.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This happens more often in those who have moist bones like the skull of a child; and in all these kinds of fractures, small pieces are separated as if it were splinters.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all kinds of fractures by the removal from them, and the inquiry has been tried, and by the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of the hair is known by this: that when one discovers the bone and strokes on top of it, if the fracture opens.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be careful for all accidents in the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, paleness, fever, eyes turning red and swollen, and other similar signs, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no extraordinary accident and you expect a good outcome, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the sickness comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is fitting to take out the bone before the fourteenth day at night when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	But if it is in this state, then hastening to take out the bone before the seventh day, will only make the skin below the bone corrupted, and accidents that we have described will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone break comes right next to the cloth that covers the brain, it is fitting that you cut off the broken part thus: and take hold of the head of the sick person, and uncover above the bone in all ways that you can, and according to the shape of the wound as well as you can, and if blood comes from the uncovering the bone or an abscess, then use what is necessary, and it is so that you fill up the space with moist cloth soaked in olive oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed down, and be sure of there not being any more bleeding; then begin to take out the bone, and this is done according to two kinds of work: one kind is that you cut off at the narrow cutting beforehand, and it's like this:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then after this treatment, a more severe amputation is performed than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have various cuts of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, with a pointed tip, made of iron, and do them lightly so as not to strike the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is advisable that you pierce through it, in such a way that you administer cuts with sharp edges, not by cutting too deeply, so that the edge does not go beyond the softest part of the bone, and over the point there should be a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you need to have more than one cut, so that each comes in its own time with the growth of the bone, so that you will always have sharp edges for every test; and this is the form of the three kinds of cuts.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing inside the bone break is that you place an iron tare on top of the bone, and turn to your two hands until you know when the bone is pierced; then put the tare elsewhere a little after, and do so around, and then cut at the incisive space of the bone between the pertu, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you feel the bone in your hand, or on any of the instruments that you have such as pliers, forceps; and beware that you do not touch the brain or the sinew.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and cut it, if it covers that which is left behind of the bone at all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it must be more nuanced and subtle than the others; and if it leaves nothing of small bones or scales, then gently take out the bone with one of the instruments; and cure the wound as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of operating is what the Galenians say, which is more precise; and it is spoken very loudly, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary to uncover a part of the bone, in that place where the break opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you put under the head of this incision a lens-like shape, because it is this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut at one side, and the part is weak in both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then with a small hammer above, you lightly copy the bone all around, and be well guarded from the netting that is under; if it is rough against the bone, then the bone cuts easily, because we cut well with pain, and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone is not pierced through the cloth until now and only the top part of it is struck so that small pieces form, then cover with the roughness again and remove the scales at the razor-thin sharpener which you must have in various amounts to provide for each person what seems most convenient according to their work and figure of the break.
