Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have before many rough razors, and after subtler ones, and do not cease to do this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other small cuts and subtle breaks, it is necessary to provide according to its direction; and this is something that cannot be answered by anyone who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the syphilitic is uncovered, it is necessary that you apply linen bandages according to its quantity, and moisten them in rose oil, and put them over the wound; then take another doubled cloth, either of two or three thicknesses, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not weigh down the syphilitic, and then apply from above another bandage, and do not bind it too tightly lest the wound bleed excessively; and let it remain for one or two days, until the abscess is allayed, and then remove it, and administer medicines as with the roots of lilies, flour of violets, and powdered incense, and other similar things; and make powder from these things, and put it on the wound, and administer medicinal ointment; and be careful that the wound is completely dried, lest you leave a discharge or assemble bowels, for when the bowels are assembled over the cloth of the brain, they burst and bring great evil to the patient, because when something is applied on top of the syphilitic something mordant, it dries up from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful whether they will doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But if it does not come from fire only because of the medicine that has been put on it, which has some virtue, it is wise to take a part of honey, three parts of rose oil and one part of glue, wrapped in a cloth, and apply it to the wound; then cure the patient according to the treatments that are suitable for them, until they are healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two lower parts of the nose are sometimes broken, or one part alone, because they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it becomes deformed or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, so that you put your small bone or fragment into the broken part, and into the pouch, for lack thereof, until it returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain by your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone and it cannot be returned to its place, so that you put a small peg into the head of a nail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do this again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; but if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses have subsided, then put a cloth made of linen into the head of the bone, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you want to break the other bone on the same side, if there is a fracture; and let the swellings be so large that they fill up the empty places of the sinews.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And doctors said that you should moisten the swellings in butter, and move each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem quite right, but it is necessary that they be moistened in the composition of butter and egg, and powder of millstones; then let the swelling, until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at no time pour in or pennes of goose fat instead of swellings, and if the swelling is drawn out within, and it holds the fracture, and blows the patient, then make a knot as you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	If the abscessed joint comes near while you are working, then put some cold or moist cloth in oil or rosewater, or apply a poultice of dung.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscessed joint does not come near, then apply an ointment made of flour of sesame, and powder of incense, mixed with lard, then put on light poultices, and do not tie the wound; and if it breaks open with small pieces, and is broken into small parts, if you have suitable instruments for this, then cut the opening, and apply a plaster to treat fractures, and stitches, if they are suitable for that; and if there is no pain in the wound, cure the sinuses, and put on poultices of onion, until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	About the fracture of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is fractured without any open wound, and there is only a bruise inside, without breakage in two, but only a slight separation of the cheekbone, if one weighs lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your right index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, put your right index finger into the left hand, and gently push the fracture inside, and tie off with the other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is displaced in two parts, it is necessary to manage the extension of two parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	In case of movements or dislocations, if the teeth are broken out or a wire is strained from gold or silver or silk, then put the broken mandible on one side and put the double drapes on; and put a big bow well-made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it above the muscle that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve light viands.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, if you take away from three days and then put back to its original shape; and apply plaster on it, with powder of flour with a lot of water or sement flour after you have opened the wound; and put on the plaster a light linen, and if the plaster hardens and the disposition of the patient does not change, let him stay until he is healed; many are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If an abscess comes to a head, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If there is a break and wound together, repair the broken piece of bone once it has been taken out; if you are subtle about removing the splinter.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have removed all these bone pieces, and it does not stay in place, apply the wound dressing, if it is large, and put on suitable poultices according to that, in order to heal the wound.
de la forcele	of the fistula.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fistula breaks more often at the shoulder joint, and there are three kinds of fracture: either it is broken and separated into two parts, with fragments, and is easier to restore; or it has a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Instruct the patient to bind the wound when it is broken and injured so that you have two assistants: one who tightens the shoulder so that the fractured bone feels the pain; and the other stretches out the neck towards the part where the fracture is located; then set the break straight with your two hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you have to stretch it further, put a round sword or piece of cloth on the patient's shoulder so that its size is as needed; then bind tightly and steady the pain, and tie the sword to your hand, so that you set the break straight as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot treat the head of the pain in front because it comes from within, so that the patient lies on his back, and put a pillow under the shoulder, and pour the medicine down the throat, until the bones of the pain are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the break to your two joints, and if you find the debris, it is fitting that you cut it up; and take out the pieces lightly, and if the bones cannot join again for any sort of covering, if the knife cuts at one of the incisions you have; but make sure to put this instrument down, in order to ward off the syphilitic:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And resemble a spoon, and it is not of wood, and so large as you want it to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two heads, just as you see, and let one be wide, and the others pointed, as is the wound's routine when you cut the bones; and once you are certain that you have reached a good spot, count the wound, and if the routine is small, or if you doubt it is far, then apply the wound with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms on your flesh, then apply rose oil, asbestos, and vinegar to it, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The constriction of the bone when it is hurt and swollen is that you put on the bone the plaster made from flour and brimstone, and place light strips on top, and set a spear under the shoulder, if necessary; then take a very large bandage, one palm wide, and wrap double over the strips and the plaster; then take a fine needle of three times the width and length, and weave it through that bandage, so that the edge of the bandage hangs down; and place the needle on the break, and turn the bandage up over the shoulder, and under the arm, and above and below the injury; and tie each part, and when you see that the limb holds the break in place immediately, and you see clearly that the spear does not move above the broken bone, then apply it every day, and when the ligaments are tight, set it; and make the patient lie on their back, and put a small pillow under the armpit, to lift the armrest up; so that the break in the shoulder is made easier by the stretching of the shoulder blade, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie unless there is bad accident, just for twenty days; then reapply the plaster, if necessary, and set it again, as before, until it is restored; and it is restored in 28 days, and less often than once a month.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It is not often that the shoulder breaks or gets dislocated unless it has been moved by force; if you set it back in its place according to the shape of the break, and tie it back to its natural form, in all ways possible, then put on the patient powder from the mill with a great deal of flour and fine stones, and attach a double cloth. Then put on a large and subtle needle, one piece larger than the shoulder, so that the needle is sewn into any part of the shoulder, with threads of linen, so that the needle cuts evenly; and then tie it tightly to all, so that the needle does not move from its place, and examine every day whether the bandage is tight; and whenever you untie, re-attach the needle, and put on a fresh bandage if necessary, for the patient's sake, and let them lie on their back; for after twenty days or twenty-five, the shoulder will be restored.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if one piece of bone is pushed forward and does not adhere to the wound below, then raise it up, and the bone, and do as we have said in soothing an abscess with great heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The piece is never broken in the middle, but it often breaks at a surface.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, so that it inclines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of feeling, and swelling, and sometimes vomiting blood, and in order to open up the marrow in the broken bone, and the sensation is much worse.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and you place a cloth between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the two ribs with your hands, and be careful to put everything in order as much as possible, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then place poultices and strips over the subtle part of the salt, or lighter substance, and cover them with a cloth wrapped around the broken bone, so that it does not move; and tighten the binding round the back, immediately, and secure every hour the bandage, and if it loosens, you restrain it; and if they want to loosen it, because of corrosion or itching that comes to them, or pain or abscess, you hasten, and release it, and scrape off the poultice, and direct those who have come with cures, in such ways as healing; then remove the poultice, and bind it so long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	It is observed that the fracture of the ribs comes only from the big one after the back, and in the head within, and they bend because they are fragile; and some people feel very bad when inquiring with them.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are such that you must put the fracture back, as it seems fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster, and tie with a splint, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the ribs fracture inwards towards the belly, it causes the patient great pain, and puncturing, like pleurisy, because the bone pokes into the membrane; and they become irritable to needles, and swollen, and vomit with a lot of bloody matter, and this is due to bad health, and the old people have given much treatment.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who claim it is suitable to administer foods that swell the belly in order to push the fracture into its place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless an abscess has come from a burnt flesh.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then cut it out.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that one should put vices on the limb to cut off pus, and it seems reasonable; all see, there is doubt whether the vice attracts the superfluities of the limb due to its weak condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that one must cover the limb with a moist linen in hot oil, and place tentes ( probably a type of bandage) between the ribs to make the wound even, then treat with the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the head of the shoulder is injured by a spear point and breaks the bone, and there is great pain in the patient that he cannot bear from the sharp edge of the bone, and fear comes to the patient, then it is fitting to break open the wound on the broken side of the ribcage, and it is fitting to apply some instrument to ward off the sore; and thus it must be carved the bone, and treated lightly, and then sew the two leaves of the wound, if they are great, and cure with plasters until he is sane.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess comes to the skin, put moist cloths in olive oil on it, and apply them to the limb; and cure as long as the limb requires the opening of the abscess, until the swelling subsides over the costal side where it must be, until he is sane.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never does a fracture occur in the bones of the neck, and it often happens when he bends; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens that he cannot tell if he will be sane or not, take care and see if you notice these signs: when his hands are soft and swollen and lifeless, and cannot move nor stretch, and when you poke them with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortal in these other dispositions, and if he is mute and feels well when you restrain and press him, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will recover, if you put them on treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens at the back of the spine, and you see whether it heals or not, take care if the feet are soft, and if the accidents occur in the hands, and on the back there is a sudden movement and expulsion with voluntary effort; and when one has become aware of what is happening on his chest, so there is an expulsion with voluntary effort.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he becomes aware of it on his back and tries to relieve himself, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that this is fatal if you do not work on his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if such an accident does not happen to him, then it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if the cure is that you apply oil to the abscessed place, or pour oil of rose or oil of mouse fat on the spine until it is appeased; then put on a bandage comforting and drying, and tie with a rope, and command the patient to rest; and do not lie down on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is cut open, it is proper to cover the wound with linen; and take away the bone, then put two stitches on the wound, if it is large, in a seam, then apply an ointment, wrapped in cloth, until it is healed; and if the joint of the bone is broken, which are called "joints of the knee", if you pour your left hand pouch into it, and put it equal to the other hand, with your power, then put the plaster and the stake on, if you have need; then bind it, and if it has a bone that needs to be cut open again, it is done, and take away the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the femur
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	There is little that happens when the femur bone is broken, and if it has, then if it has not had a slight amount of rest at first; then do long, and incline to the parsonage, and comes to the patient pain in the limb, and swelling, and that which breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	Instruct the patient to extend his hand above the break so that he is on top of the fracture; and find out which type of fracture it is and its shape; and if the fracture is only in the head, tie up the fracture so that it takes the natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or declines inward, so that it points to the inside, have the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have tied it up, put on the plaster, then put on a splint made of wood or bone, and bind the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the lower part under the ribs, until the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If the abscessed foot comes, so that it is not touched, until the abscessed foot is calmed down, and apply to what we have previously said; and then return to restoration, and tighten as needed, if there is no new bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is fractured, then one must restore it according to one of the two ways: one way being that you take a piece of bone of a middle size, in the shape of this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind both shoulders with two bands, and place them upwards, cut the sick man on that bed; then put the broken arm on the bone, until it comes to rest, and has an anchor of bone, then place above any weighty thing or have the ministers extend it away; then tie the wound equal in size to its hands together, until the wound returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that you must put the patient above his head, and tie his neck, then command to two ministers who one holds the thing that is on the breakage in their hands, and the other holds below all the ligature, and each of them extends it to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then tie the ligature below the breakage, and above the breakage, and extend each of the ministers to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the breakage is close to the head of the shoulder, it is advisable that you tie a middle ligature under the clavicle, and the other towards the joint, below the breakage; and so if the breakage is towards the joint, it is advisable to put a lighter ligature, with care, until the breakage is evened out on its own, and on the joint; then tie up the breakage as desired, and tighten, if abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, then use needles, and place one needle larger and stronger than the others on the break, and put between each needle two spaces, and so that each needle is as big as it should pass through the break three times from each part; then pull on the needles, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, stronger and less loosening.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the position of the needles and the straining, as we have said, when you restore the broken limb, and you doubt whether to open the abscess, leave it tied for seven days, as we have said; then look at each one of them three days later, whether they cause swelling or a discharge, or if any numbness comes to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is true, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if such accidents do not occur, then it is only necessary to delay the application of the cure for three days or more, and the patient should lie on his back and have his hands over his stomach; and beneath the elbow apply a bandage of linen, evenly fitted, and observe each hour of the day or night, that the figure of the broken member does not move, or be weakened by the ligaments; for it will appear according to the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat that we have beforehand placed before him in such manner that the meat is softened first; and when he begins to recover, if it is thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the elbow and leg should be reset after forty days of treatment; and therefore, one must remove the bandage and administer baths and remedies for limb movement.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is tight and swollen, so it stays tied for three days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fossicles", because one is small and contains the pouch, and the other is large, and is beneath, towards the small bone; by chance only the larger fossicle breaks alone, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fossicles are broken, restoration is light, and healing; and when the larger ones are broken, so is the healing, and they become more grievous than when both were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small fossicle that is broken alone, then it must be extended lightly and put back in place.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	In case of great swelling, he must draw it out stronger; and stretch upwards to the cusp, and elevate the pouch on his hand higher than the others, and lower the nails more than the others, so that the patient crosses his own limbs, and stretches up before him, above them, so that the patient may not suffer any labor; then extend one's other arm to the part below his hand, or to the joint, and one other minister to the upper part.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put him on equal ground, in his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no matching piece that can be held close to the joint, and you cannot restore it to its proper place, then fix it with bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If the break has a wound, I have spoken of it to the single doctor; take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	If in the beginning of the restoration, swollen abscesses appear, then apply a dressing made from olive oil, rose, and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; tie up the dressing gently, until the abscesses are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then apply the olive oil, and put on the poultice of powder from the mill with a lot of fat, since it is placed on the arrows; and make the arrow head over the break stronger, and just a little wider than the others; and know that it must have six arrows or more of this disposition: whether the break is in one bone or two; and tighten above the break more than elsewhere, every day less as you remove, just as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and so be the dressings that are on top of the break soft and moist, not hard nor dry; and make the strings, from which it is strained, of linen, neither too big nor too small, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident happens to the limb, just like when it prurites (itches), then it is fitting that you raise the limb in warm water, until the itch is appeased; and let the limb not be tightly constricted rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the tightening, and if the joint is loosened and the bone is separated, and it seems like a similar thing, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the numbness persists and cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then it is fitting that you loosen it a little, and let it stay like this for some days, until the numbness goes away, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if any of these things do not happen to the patient, so that they are freed after twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and if it is necessary to cut the hands to his neck, and his necks are even, and he watches out for movement and grasping, and sleeps on his back; and you know that this injury is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps twenty days, according to the humors and the constitution of the person.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand break
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand there is a small amount of breakage, and it comes but pain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the finger of the hand is broken or bruised, it is best for the patient to cross his fingers, and sit up straight in front of him equally; then place his hand on an extended sleeve, and extend the jointed bones, and make them even the joints; and put a bandage and casts, unless there are any abscesses, then put an arrow according to the quantity of the injury; and if it is not improved after four days of linen wrapping.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, so let the breakage be in the tendons near the belly of the foot, then make a sparrow's feather of cloth, and instruct the patient to tie it to his broken foot; and then tie an arrow of linen around the same thickness as the plantar part of the hand, and tie it so that it suits.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the breakage is in the fingers, it is advisable to place an arrow above and another below on the foot, so that the fingers are covered and straightened; then tie all around the hand, and bind the ligament between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the breakage comes to any of us in the fingers, and it's a boil, put a bandage on it as seems fitting; bind with cloth around the foot, and if you see if binding is straight and still, place an arrow-sized bandage above to lift the fracture; but if the fracture is elsewhere than on the other fingers, as in the index or another, put a bandage on it as seems best, and tie the one that's sound after; all bound together with care, until it heals, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	The part of the bone breaks.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the joint is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns before and behind; and restoration is like tying up above the break, and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, and then each of these ministers stretches out the bandage to their equal length; and that's when the break is set in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the joint of the bone, then it's one of the bands to the point of the finger, and the others below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the joint of the knuckle, and therefore so are the bands of the knuckle, and so is the extension above; then put the mirrors against the bone equal to its two hands, so that it becomes according to his natural figure, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, so that the abscess does not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess in this place, so let it be calmed and then return to your work and care; the relief is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap a bandage around the fracture with a strong double bandage in II or III, and keep the swelling there, then turn the leg so that the toes reach to the root of the nail, and put I long thread between the cistern and the leg, below, and let the chief hang above; then turn upwards the leg and the cistern with the bandage, then put on a splint over the fracture, and put an iron on the bone of the leg; then apply soft drapes between the leg and the cistern to make equal the tension, then start to tie firmly III turns or IIII above the fracture; and as you go higher in the fracture, and less is the tension; then take out II threads of thread that you have put between the leg and the cistern, and tie III iron pegs that are on top, then return below to the chief of the thread until you see the foot; and if the strain does not move from its place, then leave it so, for there will be no new abscess or swelling or similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to do this when he has it and dislocation occurs, and follow what we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that can be grasped, take them out, for one should do so; and if one cannot, then you must break the limb, and treat with force; and the cure as we have said, until he is sane.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no time is broken in such a way as when we put needles into the shoulder and the arm; all this goes well, for the patient does not suffer any harm.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And the bone is restored in three days, or a little less or more, according to the diversity of the complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the femoral channel
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	The body of a child has no fracture, but it often bends.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, but is only a crack or split, and has pain to the wound and the flesh, and it hurts very.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts equal those who are worn out on their joints, until they are assembled again, when it can be done; then applies an ointment, and puts on a round stick, if necessary, and tightens as it should, then takes all the dispositions we have said about other fractures, such as abscesses and similar things; for each accident, one applies that which is fitting for him, until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	When there are two bones in the leg, so that one is called "stump" and the other "ankle", and they have every other fracture just like when it happens to the arm, and for this reason their restoration is as if of the arm, and the wounds are all equal; and if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, so turn it before.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then feels great pain and it can be seen well; and turn below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And therefore apply an extension, and put it in its place, and tie the bands equally; but be careful, if the break is ugly and there are many pieces, so that the extension is less and lighter, then adjust according to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all of your work, take two flexed fingers that bleed from the thigh on both sides, and be long enough from the knee to the groin; then tie them around the wrist in two places, and hold it firmly at the middle, so that the leg cannot bend either to the right or to the left, and thus is well; and no one will be served with short lengths of the thigh, whether it is made of wood or has been put on, and he puts the leg on to prevent movement, and this is done properly in the break where there was a wound; and move each limb every day to see if it has an abscess or another accident.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone fracture of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not come to a break, but sometimes the bone of the foot breaks and sometimes it is bruised, and there is no force required except for shock at other dislocations.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bone of the foot breaks and you see these bones lying one on top of another, put this patient's foot on the ground, just as they are going to run, and then put your foot on their side, where the bones are raised, then press them so that they settle into their place; then apply plaster and bandages, and tie around the lower part of the foot a small tube with two holes, and secure it until you have finished wrapping, and other things as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if you release the bandage, because you will find that the bones are even, whether they are broken, or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If it is broken into two pieces, restore them in the same way as we have said about the fingers of the hand; then put one piece on top of the other according to their length, and make it a little larger, then set the foot in place, because it will happen so. And if there are II or III or more broken bones, if you put one stel (nail) on each bone according to its quantity, wrapped up in an I strip of linen, and tighten the foot under the leg; and as long as he stays above the head of the broken leg away from his belly under the foot, it will be fixed.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is also necessary that you not forget the other things I have said about other breaks, since we have said them; and cure each injury in the way it seems to be fitting.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of a bone at the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman is fractured, if it swells, then incline it towards the back of the back, and hold it behind; then fill the socket with the patient's cloth in the same way as I stated; and so bind the woman's back tightly, and slowly lift her back piece by piece, until the sock comes to the entrance of the nature, and returns to the bone with its state; and when she urinates, tie up the sock, and when she has urinated, release it again, thus for seven days or before: if she is restored to health, then take a vessel of wool, and bind the puncture with a rope, and pour all the vessel into the nature; then blow into the rope tightly until the vessel is drained within; the nature will return to the fracture; then fill it with cloth again, and leave it in this manner for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the shoulder blade is broken, or in a woman, so it restores itself as we have said about the knucklebone; and these close breaks are not concealed by those who apply their study and practice, and observe my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For this break means that there is more danger on the right path of restoration: therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the female genital organs, when they are broken, take a swab of dove and pour it into the vagina; then wrap it in cloth, and let it sit for three days or longer, and he will be quickly healed.
de brisure avec plaie	Of breaks with wounds.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has a break with a wound, especially if it's great, so that the bone of the shoulder or arm joint, or similar, is set now, if what we have said testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the wound is clean, then apply the vinegar again, if you have nothing else, then restart the healing process in that same hour or the following day, unless an abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess comes, then wait until the next day to restart the healing process, up until the abscess is calmed down, and do not touch it again on the third or fourth day, for you will bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the broken bone appears near the joint discovered, it is to be put at a gentle point on your fingers, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the extension does not fit to be put on equal to your fingers, take this instrument of iron, with 7 or 8 inches long, and make it large according to the quantity of the wound; and for that it is the master's duty to apply 3 or 4 times, according to how much he has need in each cure of fracture; and it should be rounded and not too small, so as not to bend with compression on the limb at your work, and it should be placed in front, and large from one inch behind, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because it must be placed on the curved part of the skull bone; and pour one, until it returns, and the sides become equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	But if the break is subtle and the splints cannot grasp the bone properly, it is advisable to copy the skull bone, so that the splints have hold of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot set the bone as we have said, do it with a tool that is suitable for this purpose, or incise and scrape, to your ability; then take away what remains stuck in the bone of roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that he is not in his natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is in its place, then make the arrow point to it (i.e. fix) with a vinegar tourniquet black and clean, and that's how it should be done for that part; and don't put any ointment or other thing on the wound except oil if you want to bring rot and corruption; then provide stitches when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover all of it (i.e. the entire area) completely, according to the size of the wound; and be careful that the wound is not tightened with a break; and many times those foolish doctors have done this, and have brought up the patient either dead or corrupted at some time; and so the gentle and soft compresses are better than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that more accidents will come upon it, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, do not put on stitches; but instead wrap around, with a hard bandage, and bind.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after the first day or second day that the bow has healed to the wound, so know what you have put on top of it all wine, and apply the ointment healing wounds, just as ointment of four parts and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is fitting that you dislocate the limb a second time every day, morning and evening, until it is softened and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is fitting that the limbs be dressed in a certain way so that the bow heals along the leg more lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the wound opens again every day and it cannot heal but falls apart bow, see how small pieces of bone there are, for that's why you should cover the wound with a poultice, and remove all those pieces which cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If an abscess comes to the leg or in another manner of corruption, then it is fitting that you cure it, according to what he advises in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens up on the limb, like the bone of the arm or shoulder, and other similar bones in the large members, do not treat it immediately, for often one dies but leaves it open until it putsrefies; by chance it will fall out after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of wounds that come on from a boil.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	These wounds come often after the health of the fracture, especially when it's near the joint, and one sees a strange thing in the figure of the limb; and by chance it cannot do its own work naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Instruct the patient then to let them be fresh: if they administer medicinal remedies such as aloes, incense, and mirror, and saffron, acid, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together, and mix with wine medicinal or with a large quantity of oil or with ease; and place it on the nose in powder form, and strain well, and do not loosen in hands daily; and then uncover, and renew another, until the nodules are removed; or you strain on a piece of pounce well made; for the properties of pounce are that they remove all swellings above the members; and if the nodulation is converted into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, so that the flow is visible afterwards; or you take them away with any rasurer, until they are removed, and the cure until they are healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A limb that is weak after childbirth.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and stays after the weak limb moves subtly, such things happen for many reasons: because one is too tightly bound and was not bound as it should have been; or because there are too many ties, and cannot come to the swelling of the member; or because of excessive swelling; or because of too great movements, neither in its hour nor after; or because it has little blood in its body, so weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until it has multiplied in him; then administer baths, and give joy and ease; next put poultices on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great swelling, and the artery opens frequently with water, until the swelling subsides from the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	One de la main after the health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	If the limb is twisted after the restoration and the bone breaks open, and the form of the limb is ugly, and one cannot regain its natural vigor: do not believe foolish people who say that you must break the limb anew; for many fools have done this in our land, and these wounds are blamed, and they often result in great harm, and sometimes death.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no joint is straightened by constant and prolonged friction with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And make the joint move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted thing is old and hardened, like a stone, and it needs to be dressed with iron, then if you think it can cover just at the bone, at the subtle incision lightly, put cushioning and study in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs for no apparent reason, if you think now is the time to restore it properly.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Because if you wait too long, the limb swells up and, by chance, it may set in on a bone; therefore, it is not advisable to move the joint when it is swollen: many times this has brought on inflammation and other pains. For all cases, when it happens, cure the patient, then let it be, until the swelling subsides; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then move it lightly, and cure each member as the cure comes to its own place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of the treatment for dislocation of the shoulder joint, since it is a painful injury.
des mandibules	of the jawbones.
