Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There is often that the jawbones are displaced and dislocated in two ways: either they have a little bone and softness; or they are completely displaced, hanging towards the chin, and cutting off the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot be held in place, nor can his mouth be closed, and he swallows with the word.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it recurs more often in various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and has come to a full stop, it is necessary that you reset it hastily, and not delay; and in this manner that the masters will show the head of the patient, and pour some hot water from one of his hands into the root of the dislocated jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other two should be avoided, so that they may be equal; and instruct the patient to relax his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And put the mirror on him equal, so he regains his place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if he returns wounded, especially when the two mandibles are put together, then use warm water and oil to ease the movement; do not press too hard to return it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned evenly, and the diseased mouth swells well with mucus, put on moist cloths coated with rose oil and beeswax, then tie it lightly with soft strings; let the patient lie on his back, and his joints be between two pillows, so he does not move at all in head or arm or hand, nor tries to straighten, but takes easy food until the pains are gone and the mandibles are stiff, and then take what he wants easily, and do not trouble opening the mouth to drink or swallow, until the mandible is well stiffened and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset to their point in one hour, and are not converted back to their places, then fever and sickness are set in, and by chance, belly pain occurs, and by chance, vomiting of clear blood.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a bad sign; and many die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the forearm.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forearm cannot move across the bone inside the joint and against the flesh, and it is dislocated every time without fail, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back, stretches out his arms; and then presses down with his hand to his palm, and it returns; then puts on the plaster and bandage, and binds it; and the elbow which was near the bone cannot move unless provoked; if not, and if it dislocates at all, then one must reset it as we have said; then puts on the plaster and bandage, and binds it, and commands the patient to rest until he is healed; and so himself returns the shoulder joint when it is set in its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	About the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three kinds of dislocations of the shoulder: one occurs at the lower part of the scapula below, and another at the lower part of the arm bone; sometimes it occurs above, which happens rarely; and never behind the shoulder, or inside the nerves; but more often down towards the scapula, equally in those with little flesh, because they become dislocated suddenly; in those with enough flesh, it becomes dislocated at joints.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some people that they are struck or crushed, and an abscess forms on the shoulder hot with inflammation, and they think they have a dislocation.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they are pulled downward toward the joint, and you will notice a difference between the diseased and healthy shoulder; and you will find among their differences a clear manifestation; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a depression, and below the joint at the bony end of the shoulder, just as if it were one; and the patient cannot return their hand to its natural position or move any movement from any part; and also, if they are pulled up high, it is not concealed because you will find it clearly at the bony end; and this manner of dislocation is not hard to treat when it is new, or if the child is sickly.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts up the hand of the sick man above, then puts his fingers below the joint, and lifts up the joint to strength in the upper part; and the minister lifts up the hand, and extends it upward, since he put it downward; if it happens suddenly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not happen as we have said so many times before, then it is fitting that the sick man be immersed in hot water; and he should be anointed with a mild and soothing substance, such as a decoction of alums and fenugreek and mellilot in hot water, and applied to him; then sit him on his back, and put a linen bandage below the joint, neither too soft nor too hard, and put mirrors under it, and lift the shoulder joint virtuously, and treat the sick man's hand; and another minister should apply pressure to the head of the sick man so that he does not move downward; this shoulder will return all now, and if you see whether he is restored according to this manner: and thus make him be present a large person who is greater than the sick man; and stand upright towards his side, and pour hot water over the joint of the sick man, and lift it up high so that the sick man hangs in the air; and another minister should treat the hand of the sick man downward towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then they must put with them any heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the remedy is done in another way: it is a long iron bar put into the ground, whose length is equal to a rod, and not too thick nor too thin; then placed under the patient, but so that he can wrap himself around, and his joints be straight from the long stick; then extend one hand down from the other part, and the joint will return to its place quickly; if it does not come back for all those things which we have said, do this cure: take an iron bar of two arms long and four fingers wide, with the head retracted into the hole under the shoulder, according to this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Instruct the patient to lie down on his chest under a soft cloth so that the wound does not bleed on him, then place it below the abscess of the patient; and stretch out both arms over the chest of the long wood, and tie the assistant above the chest, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm above one eschele (or scale) of large length, and so extend the hands downward, and leave the body hanging from another side: now the joints will be joined again.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, in any manner whatsoever, it is suitable that you put below the abscess a spear of wool equal, then place the plaster made from pumice powder on it with incense and onions of oil, over the entire shoulder and around, then strain from beneath the abscess immediately, and turn the bandage back onto the plaster, and encircle the hand around its neck, so that the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	Instruct the patient to rest for a while until his limbs are comfortable, because he will recover sooner; and then instruct him more after five days or seven, and move him; and if it is firm and does not soften, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen from moisture or from some other reason, then it is advisable to apply cauterization at three punctures, as he is placed in front of or beside the cautery container.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do this and the joint does not stay in place after seven days, and it cannot lift up one arm above, then know that the nerves at the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and know that the joint has never been set back to its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is near the hip and knees, or behind, is done by force and extension of hands, and serves another joint; and treatment continues until it is cured.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes pain in the member, and slow movement, then use the patient baths many times, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder cut
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	It is known that the shoulder joint is displaced to one point, and then returns; and if it has been displaced in all directions, both in front and behind, and dislocations do not come back because they are seen and felt well; and each displacement follows its own form.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased limb with the healthy one, so the wound can be seen clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, or reach one's shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is advisable to reset him so that the swelling comes out, because if the swelling comes out, he will feel pain when resetting; and by chance it cannot be set in place at all, especially since it is at the back; this one is worse than other dislocations, and feels great pain, and by chance many die.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is done, when she can be reset so that one can be extended, then stretch out both hands; extend his arms, and let the joints relax according to the cost, above and below, until the joint returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation, so that it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and very strong on the root of the palm where the finger is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm, and two of them bind the elbow with each minister, so that it does not move at extension; then turn the arm from one side, after you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when the joint fixes the joint in its place by oil to relax the joint, then tighten the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in its place, apply plaster dry with ash and wine, and bind tight, and bend the arm to the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, then untie the ligament and let it go, and if you see that the joint does not grip well, then reapply the plaster and the ligament, and let it go again after a few days, until it is firmly fixed; then untie.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels great pain after the joint has been put back in place and it grips well, then bathe him thoroughly and rub him well, and press until he is comforted; or apply a fat mutton plaster on the joint, then let it stay for one day and one night, then take out the bone, and put in the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint temperately, then put back the plaster, and then enter him into the bath; and do this two or three times until he is cured; and if you see that applying a warm moist poultice with butter on it and straining, he will return to his normal state.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and if it returns to its place lightly, more so than other joints, then one must return it immediately to its own place, in order that the flesh does not swell, or that an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And if the treatment is to be carried out so that you place the diseased hand on a board, and stretch the fingers of the other hand, and straighten the nails, such that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and press down until it returns To all appearances, one must carefully look whether it has returned to its proper place; then put the patient's back of his hand on a board at extension and at setting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, so instructs the patient to put his back on his hand above the table, and he places his hand above this appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	But if it now returns, because if the straining of poultices does not calm down the abscesses and he leaves it so that in this way to start again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put him on his feet after some days, then the joint will remain twisted; and there is no benefit for the patient except that his hands are swollen, and he cannot stretch or strain anything: thus you know that the nerves have been struck, or the arteries; since there is no other cause except to apply cauterization to the case, and by chance it may not be worth anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hands are at rest, so put on the bandage that we have said, then tighten and let it be for four days, then take it off and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	But if it cannot be made to move and there is no pain, apply the poultice of hot water and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of a dislocation in both hands
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	For neither hand is dislocated on each side, but sometimes on the back of the palm or in the belly; therefore take the joint, and pour out the dislocation into your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the affected joint, and push it towards the area where it is dislodged; and leave it for two days, and then tie it with the same bandage as we have said, and remove it on the following day, and make it move again, and bind it as before; do this often until it tightens up, and do the same if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand, and do it just like you did before, until it heals; and do the same when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	From the wound of the dislocated shoulder of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or neck is dislocated, and there are other dislocations, if there is no remedy, because the disease hastens the patient's death.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that if there is vomiting without control, or it cannot be held, and many limbs become soft, or both knees or both arms, and sometimes the dislocated area becomes numb in four parts; that one who becomes numb in the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that if gilbositez has come from childhood: if there is no remedy or healing for the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or impact, or similar things, the ancient ways of cure were said in great words, without much benefit; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in various forms.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I dis that in the goutiness that comes to the foot before, no aid is found; and similarly that which comes directly on both sides, and cannot be cured by fire alone, as I say; and it is that the patient should lie on his face so that he does not fall; then put one log to the head in earth, and another at the feet, and tie a rope behind the legs of the sick person, and another around the hams and knees, and the two servants will take hold of the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two logs; and they should be well closed, the log as we have said, and the mire puts his palms on the stake formed, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not revive by this cure, then take a table of three arms long, and shave off the skin underneath, and place the sick person on his side, and beat the head of the table against the skin, then put the middle of the table on the stake; and put the mire's feet on the other end of the table, and press well, until he revives to lie; and if you see, do it to the turnip which turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Instruct the patient to put two thorns on the head of one arm and on the other foot; and between each thorn, a palm-sized space of bone should be left, so that they do not move; and between every two thorns there should be another thorn turning in the same direction as the turnets, and two palm-sized bones to make them turn; and then tie the bandage around the assel (around the joint) on the turnet towards the head, and the other around the feet, so that each minister turns his turnet until the entire bandage is tied, and the master puts an equal-sized spike as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is evened out, put up an emplastre desiccating with many beeswax, and then the poultices, and then the head of a three-dozen pound table made from this size (of bone), which stains the leg of goutiness and the healthy part of the spine, and tie it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle nursing treatments until it is healed; and if no condition comes to an end in the healing, then it is wise to administer medicine mollifying and soothing, using the head that we have mentioned before; and sometimes apply a piece of poultice, and sometimes there appears something on the back spondil (spine) in the hind part, and think that it is dislocations; and this is because the bone opens, so that one must not have much hope: by chance, it may come to death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the knee.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Knowing that the joints of the knee and shoulder only come to fire dislocations, not like other joints. The joint of the knee is displaced according to four parts: inside and outside, and before and behind; and more inside those places, and little displaced before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of dislocations inside is that when you join a sick leg to a healthy one, it is longer, and the malady's knees are more open than the healthy ones, and the malady cannot double their knee in the fire; and there are the swellings which are located under the abscess, because the swelling of the crotch comes on.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which comes to the outside is that these accidents are against what is before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that person who suffers from this, are that they stand well with their leg according to the completion; all see, do not double bend the knees in pain, and if you want to make them walk, it cannot be done beforehand, and holds back their urine, and swells the ankle, and when they walk, passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that person who suffers from this (afterwards), are that they cannot spread their knees, nor double bend them, and the leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle has been softened, and there is the swelling of the groin at the level below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this semblance of dislocation are that if you have been wounded with (dislocated) joints before, and the swelling remains according to its condition, there is no cure; and it is not wise to assume.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that one where the dislocation is fresh, and it's four kinds of dislocation, so hurry up to set the joint, and draw it inside and out, and move it from right to left and left to right; perhaps if you return to it, and there's no need for another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it doesn't return in that manner, so it is fitting to have a strong minister, and draw the leg strongly with two hands, or tie it above the knee; and some other ministers extend their hand upwards in this way that they pour water over their hands below their haunches, then grasp with a soft cord on the navel; and some others tie the head to the cord; and stretch everything up and down once, until the patient is lifted from the ground once, and remains.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in four forms, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it's quite true.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	But if it's not so, you should take care of its resemblance When the dislocation is at the joints, it's recommended to lift the patient up onto their healthy side, then tie the limb to the base of the skull, and the one that is below the angle, then tighten the bandage towards the angle, and towards the fold; then take other attendants and wrap the large limb of the sick person tightly around, stretching it away from the pain: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	But if you can't tighten it in this way as we have said, it's recommended to tie the two legs of the sick person together with a strong bandage on both heels and knees; and make the affected leg extend two times more than the others; then hang it over the chief of a stake, and above ground for two long sticks; then command one attendant to encircle the head of the skull, and have other attendants accompany the sick person, who form a circle around the skull, because the joint returns immediately.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocations are at fault, if the patient is cured, as we have said in the chapter about gout, and strains the joint on the diseased leg properly, and on the knee as well; then puts two stitches, one on the head and another on the joint, then puts a thorn between the bones of the sick man in the shape; and puts moist cloths around it so that the patient does not bleed, then stretches each of these remedies towards him, and puts an equal-sized bandage on his hand to hold the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it doesn't return, put the leg on a surface, and press it as we have said in the chapter about gout, and cure the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocation occurs in front of it, one must extend the diseased leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and place the mires on its pain of being above the injured angle, then press with the other hand, and stretch all away towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if dislocation occurs in the back, it is not necessary to extend the diseased below, nor lift up on the ground, but rather one must keep it as if the limb had been dislocated in the back, as we have said when lying down on the two hind legs; and let its face be upwards, and stretch out the ligament so as we have said previously, and must not press upon the joint at the table; and will be at a point when the diseased extends its legs, and they become even; then add the splints, and apply the plaster, and the bandage of a strip, so that the limb does not move; and if one rests for three days or four, then one must lift it, and apply the plaster on; and if you see that they are even, then the bandage, as before, and let it rest for three days; then lift it, and have them walk gently, until the members become comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the shoulder joint dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The humerus is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and behind, but not before.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his knee to his groin, and if he does not settle onto it, know that he is dislocated; and for restoration all of these: you sit the patient upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put your foot on yours; then take his humerus in your hands, and press between them, then bend both sides of the humerus together; and another minister extends his foot, until the humerus returns to its place, and it is known that he has returned his knee to its proper position lightly; and apply plaster on it, and let him rest by his groin for three days or four, then remove it; and do not let the patient get up again, until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	If the limbs are not at all, then treatment is extended greatly, as we have said in the cure of the gout, until they become whole again.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the foot dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The feet are sometimes swollen and sometimes completely inflamed, and within and without.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that if the ankle is swollen and also has an abscess: the cure is lighter, and it should be extended lightly with the hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely swollen all over, it is advisable to seat the patient upright, and apply pressure firmly with your left hand above the ankle; then take the foot into your right hand twice, then in your left twice, then stretch it up high, and pour the foot down heavily into its place; and do this twice, as we have said, pouring and taking the foot; if it returns, that is good; but if not, for he will return; and if he cannot come back so, seat the patient on his back on the ground, and put a firm bandage between his knees, that the patient may not bleed; then stretch the ministers of the knee, and other of them extend the foot to his hands or to its binding, whichever binds above the neck of the foot; then stretch each minister equally, and let the bandages be tight enough so that they hold fast when you stretch him; then place the mires (splints) in equal position at his hands, and other ministers stretch the healthy leg downwards, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when he pricks at a point, so he puts on the plaster and bandages, and forms the strain, and binds the foot to the leg, and watches the nerves that are above the ankle, so they do not bind too tightly; then let him be for two days or three, and if his binding is swollen, apply the strain again; then release him in four days or a quarter, and wait for the patient to recover in four days; and if he goes before that time, it's no safety at all that he will still dislocate.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms on the foot comes up, it is advisable to make him calm, as we have said elsewhere, until he is cured.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, they are advisable to be extended with work, and it's a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to place himself on an even surface or on a flat table so that his foot is above the joint, and put your foot above what is open of these joints, then press down with your foot firmly, until it stops; and when he is evened out, and there is nothing open, put under the sole of the foot one table at two fingers, then strain firmly, and let him rest for three days, then release him.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wound comes with dislocation, and you want to restore it, many patients die: do not be presumptuous in the treatment, unless you are wise in the art and have used this for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow, do not become hard; use soothing remedies at the beginning of things, and let God take care of the patient, unless you see no hope of recovery; and when you see hope, restore the limb now, just as the abscesses come with life; and when the limb is restored, administer soothing remedies again, and treat the wound, if it suits you, with dried bandages; and if there is a dislocation with broken bones and small fragments, take care of them, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware not to enter into the path of fear, according to what I have said, for this will bring you punishment according to your Creator, and for the wisdom you have been armed with and your body.
Amen	Amen
